Branches: Overhanging Branches, Buildings, and Mills
Presents branch rulings on neighbor disputes and property modifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi rulings on neighbor disputes involving overhanging branches, building height restrictions, and converting a house into a mill or oven.

Core Idea
Neighbors have rights to prevent harm, but fatwa often favors freedom of use unless clear harm is proven.

Shared or adjacent property often leads to disputes. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules on what a co-owner or neighbor can demand. This lesson covers four branches from Nawādir Ibn Rustam and other sources: overhanging tree branches, raising a building that blocks sun and wind, converting a house into a mill, and installing a small oven. The rulings balance rights with practicality.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the branch on overhanging branches
If one partner's tree branches overhang into the other's airspace, is the latter entitled to demand cutting? There are two narrations from Muhammad al-Shaybani.
One narration says yes, the other says no. The preferred fatwa (in al-Dhakhīra) is that he can demand cutting.
2
Examine the building height issue
If one neighbor wants to raise his building to block wind and sun, can the other prevent it?
Two opinions: some early scholars say yes, but the fatwa (in al-Fatāwā) says no, he cannot prevent.
3
Understand the mill/oven conversion
Converting a house into a mill or a fuller's press is not permissible (due to harm), but installing a small oven is permitted.
This is a clear ruling without dispute in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة
وللإمام أن التهايؤ في الخدمة جوز للضرورة لعدم إمكان قسمتها ولا ضرورة في الغلة لأنه يمكن قسمتها لأنه عين مال ولأنه يتغير بالاستغلال بخلاف الدارين لأن الظاهر عدم التغير في العقار. وجملة مسائل التهايؤ اثنى عشر مسألة : في استخدام عبد جائز بالاتفاق، وكذا في استخدام العبدين على الأصح وفي استغلال عبد واحد لا يجوز بالاتفاق، وكذا في غلتها، وكذا في سكنى دارين وفي غلتهما خلاف والأظهر أنه يجوز بالاتفاق، وفي ركوب بغل أو بغلين على الخلاف، ولا يجوز في استغلال عبد واحد بالاتفاق وفي بغلين على الخلاف، أما التهايؤ في ثمر شجرة أو لبن غنم فإنها أعيان باقية ترد عليهما القسمة عند حصولها فلا حاجة إلى التهايؤ لأن التهايؤ في المنافع ضرورة بخلاف لبن بني آدم حيث يجوز التهايؤ فيه كما تقدم، وتقدم بيان الحيلة في ذلك قال : ولم يذكر في الكتاب المهايأة على لبس الثوبين قال بعض مشايخنا : لا يجوز عند الإمام خلافاً لهما لأن الناس يتفاوتون في اللبس تفاوتاً فاحشاً؛ في المحيط . لو كان عبدان بين رجلين غاب أحدهما فجاء أجنبي وقاسم الشريك وأخذا عبداً للغائب فقدم الغائب وأجاز فمات العبد في يد الأجنبي فلا ضمان عليه، وإن مات قبل الإجارة بطلت القسمة وللغائب نصف العبد الباقي، وإن شاء ضمن حصته في الميت لشريكه أو للأجنبي القبض ؛ كذا في الأصل . (فروع) قال في نوادر ابن رستم : إذا كان لأحدهما شجرة أغصانها مطلة على قسمة الآخر فله أن يطالبه بقطع أغصانه؛ رواه عن محمد. وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد ليس له ذلك. وفي الذخيرة وبه يفتي وإذا أراد أحدهما أن يرفع بناءه ويسد الريح والشمس على الآخر قال نصر بن يحيى وأبو القاسم الصفار: لصاحبه أن يمنع ذلك. وقال في الفتاوى : ليس له منعه وعليه الفتوى وإذا أراد أن يجعل داره طاحوناً أو مدقاً للقصارين لم يجز له ولو تنور صغيراً جاز والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب.
Book of Division. The imam has [the rule] that temporary allocation in service is permitted due to necessity because division is not possible, and there is no necessity in produce because it can be divided because it is actually wealth and because it changes through exploitation unlike two houses because the apparent is no change in real estate. The total issues of temporary allocation are twelve issues: in using a slave it is permitted by consensus, likewise in using two slaves according to the most sound opinion, and in exploiting a single slave it is not permitted by consensus, and likewise in its produce, and likewise in residing in two houses and in their produce there is a difference of opinion, and the most apparent is that it is permitted by consensus, and in riding a mule or two mules there is a difference of opinion, and it is not permitted in exploiting a single slave by consensus, and in two mules there is a difference of opinion. As for temporary allocation in the fruit of a tree or milk of sheep, they are remaining physical objects, division reverts to them when they occur, so there is no need for temporary allocation because temporary allocation is in benefits out of necessity, unlike human milk where temporary allocation is permitted as previously mentioned. The explanation of the legal stratagem for that has preceded. He said: The author did not mention in the book temporary allocation regarding wearing two garments. Some of our mashāyikh said: It is not permitted according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] because people differ greatly in wearing. In al-Muhīṭ: If there were two slaves between two men, one of them was absent, then a stranger came and divided with the partner and took a slave of the absent one, then the absent one returned and approved, and the slave died in the hand of the stranger, then there is no liability upon him. If he died before approval, the division becomes void, and the absent one has half of the remaining slave. If he wishes, he may hold his share liable in the dead one against his partner or against the stranger who took it. Similarly in al-Aṣl. Branches: He said in Nawādir Ibn Rustam: If one of them has a tree whose branches overhang into the division of the other, he has the right to demand that he cut his branches; narrated from Muhammad. And Ibn Samāʿah narrated from Muhammad that he does not have that. In al-Dhakhīrah, and with it is issued fatwa. And if one of them wants to raise his building and block the wind and sun from the other, Naṣr ibn Yaḥyā and Abū al-Qāsim al-Ṣaffār said: His partner may prevent that. And it is said in al-Fatāwā: He does not have the right to prevent him, and upon it is the fatwa. And if he wants to make his house a mill or a fuller's press, it is not permissible. And if a small oven, it is permissible. And Allah, the Exalted, knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Division explains temporary allocation (tahāyuʾ) in the context of shared property. It begins by stating that temporary allocation in service (khidma) is permitted due to necessity, as service cannot be divided physically. However, produce (ghalla) can be divided because it is tangible wealth, so no necessity exists. Real estate like houses is treated differently because it does not change under use. The author then lists twelve issues of temporary allocation, though only some are detailed. For example, temporary use of a slave for service is unanimously permissible, but use of a slave's produce (i.e., earnings) is not. For two slaves, the ruling varies. For fruit or milk from animals, since these are physical assets that can be divided when obtained, temporary allocation is unnecessary, except for human milk where it is permitted by a legal stratagem. The passage also covers a case where an absent partner's share is taken by a stranger; if the absent partner approves, the division is valid, and if not, it is void. Further branches discuss issues like overhanging tree branches, building height, and converting a house into a mill—rulings are given based on differing opinions, with the preferred fatwa noted.

Key Terms
التنور (al-tannūr): A small oven used for baking, considered permissible due to minimal harm.
المدق (al-midaqq): A fuller's press or stamping mill, causing noise and vibration, thus not permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, converting a shared house into which of the following is NOT permissible?
A) A small oven
B) A mill
C) A storage room
D) A garden

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh balances property rights with harm: small ovens are allowed, but heavy industrial use like mills is prohibited due to excessive disturbance.

Sharecropping: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Validity
Defines sharecropping, lists conditions, and presents the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on sharecropping and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Sharecropping is valid per Sahibayn, void per Imam; the difference turns on interpreting the Khaybar episode.

This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute over sharecropping (muzāraʿah). While Imam Abu Hanifa rules it void due to the prohibition of mukhābarah, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) validate it by prophetic practice and analogy. The practical consequence affects whether the worker receives the agreed share or fair wages.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and positions
Identify that sharecropping is a contract on cultivation for a share of produce. State that Imam Abu Hanifa considers it void (fāsida) and the Sahibayn consider it valid (jāʾiza).
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's evidence
Examine the hadith of Khaybar where the Prophet gave land in sharecropping, and the analogy with mudārabah (partnership in profit) due to mutual need.
The Sahibayn argue that necessity justifies the contract despite general prohibition.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence
Examine the hadith prohibiting mukhābarah (sharecropping for a fraction) and his interpretation of the Khaybar report as a division tax (kharāj muqāsama), not a valid contract.
Imam prioritizes the explicit prohibition over the Khaybar precedent.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: if the contract is void, the worker gets fair wages (ujr al-mithl); if valid, the agreed produce share is given.
This affects how disputes are resolved in court.
5
Note the later fatwa practice
Recognize that later Hanafi fatwa generally follows the Sahibayn due to necessity and widespread practice, making sharecropping enforceable.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المزارعة
هي
كتاب المزارعة
عقد على الزرع ببعض الخارج وتصح بشرط صلاحية الأرض للزراعة وأهلية العاقدين وبيان المدة ورب البذر وجنسه وحظ الآخر والتخلية بين الأرض والعامل والشركة في الخارج وإن تكون الأرض والبذر لواحد والعمل والبقر لآخر أو تكون
كتاب المزارعة
لما كان الخارج من الأرض في عقد المزارعة من أنواع ما يقع فيه القسمة ذكر المزارعة عقب القسمة، فهي لغة مفاعلة من الزراعة وشريعة ما ذكر المؤلف، وسببها سبب المعاملات، وركنها الأيجاب والقبول وشرائط جوازها كون الأرض صالحة للزراعة وكون رب الأرض والمزارع من أهل العقد وبيان المدة، فلو ذكر مدة لا يخرج الزرع فيها لم تجز المزارعة. وصفتها أنها فاسدة عند الإمام جائزة عندهما، ودليلها ما أنه عليه الصلاة روي والسلام دفع الأرض لأهل خيبر مزارعة قال رحمه الله : (هي عقد على الزرع ببعض الخارج) فقوله «عقد) جنس وقوله على الزرع يشمل المزروع حقيقة وهو الملقى في الأرض قبل الإدراك ؛ قاله خواهر زاده أو باعتبار ما يؤول إليه بأن كانت فارغة. وقوله ببعض الخارج فصل أخرج سائر العقود والمساقاة لأنها عقد على بعض الثمرة. وأطلاق في العقد فشمل مع الأجنبي أو الشريك قال في فتاوى الفضلي أرض بين رجلين دفعها أحدهما للآخر مزارعة على أن الخارج ثلثه للدافع وثلثان للعامل جاز في أصح الروايتين ا هـ. قال رحمه الله (وتصح بشرط صلاحية الأرض للزراعة وأهلية العاقدين وبيان المدة ورب البذر وجنسه وحظ الآخر والتخلية بين الأرض والعامل والشركة في الخارج) وهذا قول الثاني والثالث. وقال الإمام لا تجوز المزارعة لهما ما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام دفع الأرض مزارعة لأهل خيبر على نصف ما خرج منها من ثمر أو زرع ولأنها عقد شركة أحد الشريكين وعمل من الآخر فتجوز اعتباراً بالمضاربة والجامع دفع الحاجة فإن من صاحب المال قد لا يهتدي إلى العمل والمهتدي إليه قد لا يجد المال فمست الحاجة إلى انعقاد هذا العقد. وللإمام ما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن المخابرة وهي المزارعة بالثلث والربع، والذي ورد في خيبر هو خراج مقاسمة لا يقال هذا مخالف لما تقدم في باب العشر
Book of Sharecropping. It is. Book of Sharecropping. A contract on cultivation in exchange for a portion of the produce, and it is valid on condition that the land is suitable for cultivation, the legal capacity of the contracting parties, specification of the duration, the owner of the seed and its type, the share of the other, handing over the land to the worker, and partnership in the produce. And whether the land and seed are from one and the work and oxen from the other, or... Book of Sharecropping. Since the produce from the land in a sharecropping contract is among the types where division occurs, he mentioned sharecropping after division. Linguistically it is derived from cultivation, and in Sharia it is what the author mentioned. Its cause is the cause of transactions, its pillar is offer and acceptance, and its conditions of validity are that the land is suitable for cultivation, that the landowner and the farmer are legally capable, and specification of the duration. So if he mentions a duration in which the crop cannot mature, the sharecropping is not valid. Its description is that it is void (fāsida) according to the Imam [Abu Hanifa] and valid according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. Its evidence is that it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave the land to the people of Khaybar in sharecropping. He (the author) said: (It is a contract on cultivation in exchange for a portion of the produce). So his word 'contract' is a genus, and his words 'on cultivation' include the cultivated plant literally, which is what is placed in the ground before ripening – as stated by Khuwāhrizādah – or considering its ultimate outcome if the land was empty. And his words 'in exchange for a portion of the produce' is a specification excluding other contracts and musāqāh because it is a contract on a portion of the fruit. And the absolute in the contract includes with a stranger or a partner. He said in Fatāwā al-Faḍlī: Land between two men, one of them gave it to the other in sharecropping on the condition that the produce be one-third for the giver and two-thirds for the worker, it is valid according to the most sound of the two narrations. He (the author) said: (And it is valid on condition that the land is suitable for cultivation, the legal capacity of the contracting parties, specification of the duration, the owner of the seed and its type, the share of the other, handing over the land to the worker, and partnership in the produce). And this is the opinion of the second and third [Sahibayn]. And the Imam said: Sharecropping is not valid for them, due to what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade al-mukhābarah, which is sharecropping for one-third or one-fourth. And what is reported regarding Khaybar is a division tax (kharāj muqāsama). It should not be said this contradicts what preceded in the chapter on tithe.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Sharecropping (Muzāraʿah). It defines sharecropping as a contract on cultivation for a portion of the produce. The author lists the conditions for validity: land suitable for agriculture, legal capacity of parties, clear duration, specification of seed and its type, the worker's share, handing over land, and partnership in produce. It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), sharecropping is valid based on the Prophet's practice at Khaybar and by analogy with mudārabah (partnership in profit) due to mutual need. However, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that sharecropping is void (fāsida) because the Prophet forbade al-mukhābarah (sharecropping for a fraction). The report from Khaybar is interpreted as a division of land tax (kharāj), not a genuine sharecropping contract. The passage also clarifies that the contract is considered void according to Imam Abu Hanifa but valid according to the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
المزارعة (al-muzāraʿah): A contract on cultivation for a portion of the produce; a partnership between landowner and worker.
المخابرة (al-mukhābarah): A form of sharecropping where the worker receives a fraction like one-third or one-fourth; prohibited by the Prophet according to a hadith.
الخارج (al-khārij): The produce or output from the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider sharecropping (muzāraʿah) void?
A) Because the Prophet forbade a form called mukhābarah.
B) Because the land cannot be shared.
C) Because the worker must be paid a fixed wage.
D) Because the Sahibayn disagreed with him.

Key Takeaway
The validity of sharecropping in Hanafi fiqh is disputed: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it void due to the mukhābarah prohibition, while the Sahibayn validate it based on prophetic practice and necessity; later fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

Sharecropping (Muzara'ah): Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Defines sharecropping, lists conditions, and presents intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of sharecropping, identify the conditions for its validity according to the Sahibayn, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute and the reasoning behind the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah is valid per the Sahibayn due to prophetic practice and public need, despite Imam Abu Hanifa's view that it is void.

Sharecropping (muzara'ah) is a contract where one party provides land and seed, and the other provides labor and oxen, sharing the crop. The Hanafi school has a well-known internal dispute on its validity. This lesson unpacks the definitions, conditions, and the arguments of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), along with the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Define sharecropping
Identify the legal definition of muzara'ah as a contract on the crop for a part of its produce. Note its distinction from musaqah and other contracts.
The term 'kharij' means the produce that grows from the land.
2
List the conditions for validity
Enumerate the seven conditions mentioned by the author: land suitability, legal capacity, specification of period, seed owner and type, known share, handing over land, and partnership in produce.
These conditions are according to the Sahibayn's position.
3
State the intra-Hanafi dispute
State that Imam Abu Hanifa considers the contract void (fasid) while the Sahibayn consider it valid (ja'iz). Identify the key proofs: for Imam, the hadith forbidding mukhabarah; for the Sahibayn, the Prophet's practice at Khaybar and analogy with mudarabah.
The text also discusses the rebuttal regarding the Khaybar land being kharaj, not 'ushr.
4
Analyze the response and tarjih
Understand the author's conclusion that the fatwa today follows the Sahibayn due to public need and customary practice. Note the reason: analogy is abandoned in the face of contrary text (athar) and necessity.
The text states: 'wa qalu al-fatwa al-yawm 'ala qawlihima'.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a modern case: A landlord and a farmer agree to share the crop equally, with the landlord providing land and seed, and the farmer providing labor and oxen. Using the mufta bihi, the contract is valid if all conditions are met.
If a condition is missing (e.g., undefined period), the contract may become fasid according to the Sahibayn as well.

Source Text

كتاب المزارعة
هي عقد على الزرع ببعض الخارج وتصح بشرط صلاحية الأرض للزراعة وأهلية العاقدين وبيان المدة ورب البذر وجنسه وحظ الآخر والتخلية بين الأرض والعامل والشركة في الخارج وإن تكون الأرض والبذر لواحد والعمل والبقر لآخر أو تكون
كتاب المزارعة
لما كان الخارج من الأرض في عقد المزارعة من أنواع ما يقع فيه القسمة ذكر المزارعة عقب القسمة، فهي لغة مفاعلة من الزراعة وشريعة ما ذكر المؤلف، وسببها سبب المعاملات، وركنها الأيجاب والقبول وشرائط جوازها كون الأرض صالحة للزراعة وكون رب الأرض والمزارع من أهل العقد وبيان المدة، فلو ذكر مدة لا يخرج الزرع فيها لم تجز المزارعة. وصفتها أنها فاسدة عند الإمام جائزة عندهما، ودليلها ما أنه عليه الصلاة روي والسلام دفع الأرض لأهل خيبر مزارعة قال رحمه الله : (هي عقد على الزرع ببعض الخارج) فقوله «عقد) جنس وقوله على الزرع يشمل المزروع حقيقة وهو الملقى في الأرض قبل الإدراك ؛ قاله خواهر زاده أو باعتبار ما يؤول إليه بأن كانت فارغة. وقوله ببعض الخارج فصل أخرج سائر العقود والمساقاة لأنها عقد على بعض الثمرة. وأطلاق في العقد فشمل مع الأجنبي أو الشريك قال في فتاوى الفضلي أرض بين رجلين دفعها أحدهما للآخر مزارعة على أن الخارج ثلثه للدافع وثلثان للعامل جاز في أصح الروايتين ا هـ. قال رحمه الله (وتصح بشرط صلاحية الأرض للزراعة وأهلية العاقدين وبيان المدة ورب البذر وجنسه وحظ الآخر والتخلية بين الأرض والعامل والشركة في الخارج) وهذا قول الثاني والثالث. وقال الإمام لا تجوز المزارعة لهما ما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام دفع الأرض مزارعة لأهل خيبر على نصف ما خرج منها من ثمر أو زرع ولأنها عقد شركة أحد الشريكين وعمل من الآخر فتجوز اعتباراً بالمضاربة والجامع دفع الحاجة فإن من صاحب المال قد لا يهتدي إلى العمل والمهتدي إليه قد لا يجد المال فمست الحاجة إلى انعقاد هذا العقد. وللإمام ما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن المخابرة وهي المزارعة بالثلث والربع، والذي ورد في خيبر هو خراج مقاسمة لا يقال هذا مخالف لما تقدم في باب العشر والخراج من أن أرض العرب كلها عشرية لأنا نقول : أرض خيبر ليست من أرض العرب لأنها لا يقر فيها على الكفر. فإن قلت هم يهود قلنا خيبر ليست داخلاً في حدود أرض العرب، وإذا فسدت المزارعة عنده يجب على صاحب البذر أجرة مثل الأرض أو العمل والغلة له لأنها نماء ملكه. قال في العناية : وهذا منقوض بمن غصب بذر آخر وزرعه في أرض فإن الزرع له وإن كان نماء ملك صاحب البذر وأجيب بأن الغاضب عامل لنفسه باختياره وتحصيله فكان إضافة الحادث إلى عمله أولى والمزارع عامل بأمر غيره فجعل الامر مضافاً إلى الآمر .اهـ. ولقائل أن يقول : السؤال غير وارد والجواب غير صحيح أما أولاً فقد تقرر أن الغاصب ملك البذر بالمزارعة فالبذر نماء ملك الغاضب فلا إبرد والجواب لم يصادف محلاً وقالوا الفتوى اليوم على قولهما الحاجة الناس إليها وللتعامل والقياس يترك بمثل هذا والنص ورد نص بخلافه فيعمل به لأنه هو الظاهر عندهما. ثم شرط في المختصر لجوازها عندهما أن تكون الأرض صالحة للزراعة لأن المقصود لا يحصل بدونه، وأن يكون رب الأرض والمزارع من أهل العقد لأن العقد لا يصح إلا من الأهل، وأن يبين المدة لأنه عقد على منافع الأرض أو العامل وهي تعرف ويشترط أن تكون المدة قدر ما يتمكن فيها من المزارعة أو أكثر، وأن لا يكون قدر من لا يعيش إليه مثلها أو أحدهما غالباً. وعند محمد بن سلمة: لا يشترط بيان المدة ويقع على سنة واحدة وفي الخانية قال المشايخ : يشترط بيان الوقت وتكون الزراعة على أول سنة والفتوى على بيان المدة وإن بقي بعد تمام السنة ما يمكن فيه الزراعة لا تبقى الزراعة وفي العتابية : ولو ذكر مدة أن يخرج فإن خرج ظهر أنه صحيح وإلا فلا وأن يبين من عليه البذر لأن المعقود وهو منافع العامل أو منافع الأرض ولا يعرف إلا ببيان من عليه البذر وأن يبين جنس البذر لأن الأجرة منه فلا بد من بيان جنس الأجرة. وفي الذخيرة وفي الاستحسان بيان ما يزرع في الأرض ليس بشرط، فوض الرأي إلى المزارع أو لم يفوض، بعد أن ينص على المزارعة لأن ذلك يصير معلوماً بأعلام الأرض ومثله في الخانية. وإن بين نصيب من لا بذر من جهته وهو المراد بالأجر لأنه أجرة عمله وأرضه فلا بد أن يكون معلوماً، وأن يخلي بين الأرض والعامل لأنه بذلك يتمكن من العمل، وعمل رب الأرض مع العامل لا يصح . وأن يكون الخارج مشتركاً بينهما لأنه هو المقصود بها فتنعقد إجارة في الابتداء وتقع شركة في الانتهاء، ولهذا لو شرط لأحدهما قفيزاً مسماة فسدت لأنه يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة في البعض المسمى أو في الكل أو لم تخرج الأرض أكثر من ذلك، وكذا إذا شرط أن يدفع قدر بذره لما ذكرنا بخلاف ما إذا شرط أن يرفع عشر الخارج أو ثلثه والباقي بينهما لأنه يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة وهو يحصل أن يكون حيلة للوصول إلى رفع البذر. وقيدنا بقولنا ببعض الخارج لأنه إذا كان الخارج كله لواحد منهما فليست بمزارعة قال رب الأرض
Book of Sharecropping. It is a contract on the crop in exchange for a part of the produce. It is valid on the condition of suitability of the land for cultivation, legal capacity of the contracting parties, specification of the period, the owner of the seed and its type, the share of the other, handing over the land to the worker, and partnership in the produce. And that the land and seed belong to one, and the work and oxen to the other, or... Book of Sharecropping: Since the produce from the land in the sharecropping contract is among the types subject to division, sharecropping is mentioned after division. Lexically it is a mutual verbal noun from cultivation, and in Sharia it is what the author mentioned. Its cause is the cause of transactions. Its pillar is offer and acceptance. The conditions for its validity are: the land being suitable for cultivation, the owner of the land and the sharecropper being legally capable, and specification of the period. If he mentions a period in which the crop will not grow, the sharecropping is not valid. Its description: it is void according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] and valid according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. Their proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave the land to the people of Khaybar as sharecropping. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (It is a contract on the crop for part of the produce). His word 'contract' is a genus, and his word 'on the crop' includes what is sown literally—meaning what is placed in the ground before ripening, as said by Kharazadah—or in terms of its ultimate outcome if it was empty. His word 'for part of the produce' distinguishes it from other contracts and musaqah because the latter is a contract on part of the fruit. The word 'contract' is general, so it includes with a stranger or a partner. He said in Fatawa al-Fadli: Land between two men, one of them gives it to the other as sharecropping on the condition that one-third of the produce is for the giver and two-thirds for the worker: it is valid in the most sound of the two narrations. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And it is valid on condition of suitability of the land for cultivation, legal capacity of the contracting parties, specification of the period, the owner of the seed and its type, the share of the other, handing over the land to the worker, and partnership in the produce). This is the statement of the second and third. Imam said: Sharecropping is not permissible for them [the two] because it is reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade mukhabarah, which is sharecropping for one-third or one-fourth. What is reported concerning Khaybar is a tribute (kharaj) of division. It cannot be said that this contradicts what preceded in the chapter on 'ushr and kharaj that all Arab lands are 'ushri, for we say: The land of Khaybar is not from the lands of the Arabs because they are not allowed to remain there upon disbelief. If you say: They are Jews, we say: Khaybar is not within the borders of the land of the Arabs. When sharecropping is void according to him [Imam], the owner of the seed must pay the equivalent of the land's rent or the work, and the produce is for him because it is the growth of his property. He said in al-'Inayah: This is rebutted by the case of one who usurps someone else's seed and cultivates it on land: the crop is for him even though it is the growth of the property of the seed owner. The answer is that the usurper acts for himself by his choice and acquisition, so attributing the incident to his work is more appropriate, while the sharecropper acts by the command of another, so the matter is attributed to the commander. One could say: The question is not valid and the answer is not correct. As for the first, it has been established that the usurper owns the seed through the sharecropping, so the seed is the growth of the usurper's property, so there is no objection. And the answer does not hit the mark. They said: The fatwa today is upon their statement [i.e., the Sahibayn] because people need it and due to customary practice, and analogy is abandoned in such a case, and a text has come contrary to it, so it is acted upon because it is the apparent meaning according to them. Then it is stipulated in al-Mukhtasar for its validity according to them that the land be suitable for cultivation, because the objective is not achieved without it; that the landowner and sharecropper be legally capable of contracting, because a contract is not valid except from a capable person; that the period be specified, because it is a contract for the usufruct of the land or the worker, and it is known; and it is stipulated that the period be an amount in which sharecropping is possible or more, and that it not be an amount in which such crops do not usually survive, or one of them predominates. According to Muhammad ibn Salamah: Specifying the period is not required, and it falls for one year. In al-Khaniyyah, the mashayikh said: Specifying the time is required, and the cultivation is for the first year, and the fatwa is upon specification of the period. If after completion of the year there remains time in which cultivation is possible, the sharecropping does not remain. In al-'Atabiyyah: If he mentions a period in which it may grow: if it grows, it becomes evident that it is valid; otherwise not. And that he specify who bears the seed, because the subject matter is the usufruct of the worker or the usufruct of the land, and it is not known except by specifying who bears the seed. And that he specify the type of seed, because the wage is from it, so specifying the type of wage is necessary. In al-Dhakhirah: In istihsan, specifying what is to be sown in the land is not a condition, whether he delegates the opinion to the sharecropper or not, after he specifies the sharecropping, because that becomes known by the known customs of the land; similar in al-Khaniyyah. And if he specifies the share of the one who does not bear the seed—which is meant by the wage, because it is the wage for his work and land—it must be known. And that he hand over the land to the worker, because thereby he is able to work. The landowner working together with the worker is not valid. And that the produce be shared between them, because that is the objective; thus it takes effect as a lease initially and results in a partnership at the end. For this reason, if he stipulates a specified quantity of grain for one of them, it becomes void, because it leads to cutting off partnership in the named part or the whole, or the land does not produce more than that. Similarly, if he stipulates that he pay the amount of his seed, due to what we have mentioned, unlike if he stipulates that he take one-tenth or one-third of the produce and the rest between them, because it leads to cutting off partnership, and that serves as a legal stratagem to reach removing the seed. We restrict by saying 'for part of the produce' because if the entire produce is for one of them, it is not sharecropping. The landowner said...
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rules of sharecropping (muzara'ah). The author defines it as a contract on the crop in exchange for a portion of the produce, and then enumerates the conditions for its validity. Crucially, he presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds the contract to be void (fasid), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) deem it valid. The Sahibayn base their view on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with the people of Khaybar and analogical reasoning with mudarabah (commenda partnership) due to mutual need. Imam Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith prohibiting 'mukhabarah' (sharecropping for one-third or one-fourth) and interprets the Khaybar transaction as a special case of tribute (kharaj), not a true muzara'ah contract. Despite the disagreement, the author notes that the relied-upon position for fatwa today is that of the Sahibayn, due to public necessity and prevailing custom. The passage then details the conditions for validity: land suitability, legal capacity of parties, specification of period, seed ownership and type, known share, handing over land, and partnership in produce. It also discusses secondary issues like the need to specify the seed owner, the type of seed, and the prohibition of stipulating a fixed quantity for one party. The text ends mid-sentence on page 290, likely continuing with further details.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzāra‘ah): A contract on the crop (a grain) in exchange for a share of its produce, typically where land and seed are from one party and labor and oxen from another.
خارج (khārij): The produce that grows from the land, which is the subject of the contract and is shared between the parties.
بذر (badhr): The seed that is sown. In muzāra‘ah, it is important to know who supplies the seed as it affects the ownership of the produce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a sharecropping contract (muzāra‘ah)?
A) It is void (fāsid) in all cases.
B) It is valid (jā’iz) when certain conditions are met.
C) It is invalid unless the parties are partners in land.
D) It is equivalent to a lease with fixed rent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa today validates sharecropping (muzara'ah) under specified conditions, following the Sahibayn due to necessity and prophetic practice.

Legal Stratagem (Hila) for Invalid Muzara'ah and Rejection of Qiyas
Ruling on hila for invalid muzara'ah and refutation of qiyas extension.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply a legal stratagem to rectify a defective muzara'ah contract and explain why analogy (qiyas) cannot extend permissibility beyond the narrated (athar) cases.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah is allowed by specific narration only; qiyas cannot create new valid forms.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a practical challenge: an agricultural partnership (muzara'ah) that is invalid due to an unequal combination of inputs. The Hanafi school provides a legal stratagem (hila) to restructure the contract into a valid one. It also confronts an internal objection: some argue that a particular invalid scenario should be valid by analogy, but the commentator firmly rejects this, reminding us that the permissibility of muzara'ah itself is based on a narrated practice (athar), not on analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defective scenario
Recognize which inputs are misallocated: here, the landowner wants to use seed from another party without a proper exchange.
The seed is not owned by the landowner, creating uncertainty.
2
Understand the hila
The landowner buys half the seed for a known price and then instructs the seed owner to sow with that seed, creating a proper partnership.
This transforms the arrangement into a valid muzara'ah where both parties contribute.
3
Recognize the third invalid scenario
When seed and cattle are from one party, and land and labor from another, the contract is invalid because no athar covers this combination.
The land cannot be made subsidiary to labor due to differing benefits.
4
Analyze the qiyas objection
Some analogize this to valid forms (worker alone or land alone) and claim it should be permissible.
They assume a general principle: if providing one major input suffices, then cattle should also suffice.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The response: muzara'ah is not based on qiyas but on a specific athar; without such narration for this combination, analogy is rejected.
This preserves the school's method of relying on narrated exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز. والحيلة أن يأخذ أرضه ثم يستعين صاحب البذر بصاحب الأرض في العمل فيجوز. وفي النوازل : رجل له أرض أراد أن يأخذ بذراً من الأرض حتى يزرعه في أرضه ويكون الزرع بينهما، فالحيلة في ذلك أن يشتري نصف البذر بثمن معلوم ثم يقول له ازرعها بالبذر وهذه الحيلة تجري في كل صورة وقعت فاسدة .اهـ. وأما الثالث وهو ما إذا كان البذر والبقر لواحد والباقي لآخر وهو العمل والأرض فلما ذكرنا أن الأرض لا يمكن جعلها تبعاً لعمله لاختلاف المنافع ففسدت المزارعة . قال الشارح وهنا وجه آخر لم يذكره في الكتاب وهو أن يكون البقر من واحد والباقي من آخر قالوا: هذا فاسد وينبغي أن يجوز بالقياس على العامل وحده أو على الأرض وحدها والجواب عنه أن القياس أن لا تجوز المزارعة وإنما تركناه بالأثر وفي هذا لم يرد أثر اهـ .
It is permissible. The stratagem is that he takes his land, then the owner of the seed seeks the help of the landowner in the work, and it becomes permissible. And in al-Nawazil: A man had land and wanted to take seed from the land to sow it in his land, with the crop between them. The stratagem for that is that he buys half the seed for a known price, then says to him: 'Sow it with the seed.' And this stratagem applies in every defective case. End. As for the third: that the seed and cattle are from one party, and the rest (labor and land) from another. Since we mentioned that the land cannot be made subsidiary to his labor due to differing benefits, the muzara'ah is invalid. The commentator said: There is another aspect not mentioned in the book: that the cattle are from one party and the rest from another. They said: This is invalid and ought to be permissible by analogy to the worker alone or to the land alone. The response to it: Analogy dictates that muzara'ah is not permissible; we only abandoned it due to the narration (athar). In this case no narration has come. End.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings on defective muzara'ah and legal stratagems (hiyal) to fix them. It first presents a stratagem: if a landowner has seed from another, he can take his land and then have the seed owner assist him in work, making the contract valid. Another example from al-Nawazil: a landowner who wants to take seed from someone else can buy half the seed at a known price and then tell the seed owner to sow it with that seed, thus creating a proper partnership. This stratagem applies to all defective cases. Then the passage addresses a third invalid scenario: if seed and cattle belong to one party while land and labor belong to another, the contract is invalid because land cannot be treated as subsidiary to labor due to differing benefits. The commentator notes a variant not in the original text: cattle from one and the rest from another. Some argued this should be valid by analogy to cases where either the laborer or the land is provided alone. The Hanafi response is that the original permissibility of muzara'ah is based on a specific narration (athar), not analogy, and since no such narration exists for this case, it remains invalid.

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-hila): A legal stratagem to circumvent a prohibited or invalid arrangement by restructuring the contract to achieve a permissible result.
المزارعة (al-muzara'ah): An agricultural partnership where one party provides land and another provides labor and/or seed, sharing the produce.
الأثر (al-athar): A narration or reported practice from the Prophet or companions that serves as the basis for the permissibility of muzara'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the third scenario (cattle from one, rest from another) ruled invalid despite an analogy to valid forms?
A) Because cattle are not considered an input in muzara'ah.
B) Because the original permission of muzara'ah is based on a specific narration (athar), not on qiyas.
C) Because the worker must provide all inputs.
D) Because the contract does not specify the share of each party.

Key Takeaway
Muzara'ah is permitted only in specific narrated forms; legal stratagems can restructure defective contracts, but qiyas cannot create new valid forms beyond the athar.

Muzara'ah with a Third Party and Conditional Stipulations
Ruling on muzara'ah with third party and conditional stipulations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish valid from invalid muzara'ah contracts when a third party is involved and when conditional stipulations are present.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah validity hinges on seed ownership and whether a secondary contract is stipulated as a condition.

This passage examines complex muzara'ah contracts involving a third worker. The Hanafi school differentiates between cases where the second contract is merely mentioned versus stipulated as a condition. The ruling also changes dramatically based on who provides the seed. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correct application in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Parties and Contracts
Determine who is the landowner, the first worker (muzari'), and the third party. Recognize that there are two contracts: one between landowner and first worker, and one between first worker and third party.
The third party is not a direct party to the landowner's contract.
2
Check Who Provides the Seed
The seed provider is decisive. If seed is from the worker (first worker), the contract between landowner and worker is invalid (fasid). If seed is from the landowner, the entire arrangement becomes a valid hire (ijarah) of two workers.
Seed ownership transforms the legal nature of the contract.
3
Examine the Relation Between the Two Contracts
If the second contract (with the third) is merely mentioned without being a condition, the invalidity of the second does not affect the first. But if it is stipulated as a condition ('on condition that the second works'), some mashayikh rule the first also invalid.
The conjunction ('عطف') does not imply conditionality.
4
Apply the Takhliyah Rule
If the first worker is a lessee (not owner), he cannot sub-contract without handing over possession. Lack of takhliyah makes the second contract invalid, but the first remains valid unless stipulated otherwise.
Takhliyah is a condition for muzara'ah to take effect.
5
Determine the Final Ruling
Based on the above: seed from worker → landowner-worker contract fasid; seed from landowner → valid as hire. If the second contract is stipulated, follow the mashayikh's view that it invalidates the first.
The mufta bihi position is the one presented in al-Muhit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : ولو دفع أرضاً على أن يزرع ببذر الزارع وبقره ويعمل معه ثالث والخارج أثلاث فالعقد فاسد بينهما وبين أجنبي جائز بينهما ولرب الأرض من العامل ببعض الخارج، فلو كان المزارع الأول مالكاً لمنفعة الأرض بالاستئجار فصار كما لو كانت الأرض مملوكة ودفعها إلى العامل على أن يعمل معه لا يجوز لفوات التخلية بين الأرض والمزارع وفسادها في حق الثاني لا يوجب فساد المزارعة في حق الأول لأن المزارعة الثانية غير مشروطة في الأول والعطف لا يقتضي الاشتراط، فإن كانت الثانية مشروطة في الأول بأن قال على أن يعمل الثاني معه بالثلث هل تجوز المزارعة في حق الأول؟ قال بعض المشايخ : تفسد لأن الثانية صارت مشروطة لرب الأرض فإنه لا منفعة له في عمل الثاني مع الأول، ولو كان البذر من رب الأرض والمسئلة بحالها صحت في حق الكل لأنه استأجر العاملين ببعض الخارج وذلك جائز ؛ كذا في المحيط.
He said: If one gives land on condition that the seed and cattle belong to the sower, and a third works with him, and the produce is in thirds, the contract is invalid between them. [The contract] with a third party is permissible between them, and the landowner gets from the worker a portion of the produce. If the first cultivator owns the usufruct of the land by lease, then it becomes as if the land is owned and he gives it to the worker on condition that he works with him; it is not permissible because of the lack of handing over between the land and the cultivator. The invalidity regarding the second does not necessitate invalidity of the muzara'ah regarding the first, because the second muzara'ah is not stipulated in the first, and conjunction does not imply stipulation. If the second is stipulated in the first, such as saying 'on condition that the second works with him for a third', is the muzara'ah valid regarding the first? Some mashayikh said: It becomes invalid because the second became stipulated for the landowner, for he has no benefit in the work of the second with the first. If the seed was from the landowner and the case remains, it is valid for all because he hired the two workers for a portion of the produce, and that is permissible. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage discusses a complex muzara'ah scenario involving a third party. The main ruling: if a landowner gives land to a worker with the condition that the worker provides seed and cattle, and a third person also works with them, the produce divided in three equal parts, the contract is invalid between the landowner and the worker, but valid between the worker and the third party. The landowner gets a share from the worker. If the first worker is himself a lessee of the land (i.e., he has the usufruct), then giving the land to another worker on condition that he works with the lessee is not permissible because the land must be handed over to the cultivator. However, the invalidity of the second contract does not automatically invalidate the first contract, unless the second was stipulated as a condition in the first. If it was stipulated, some scholars rule the first invalid because the landowner gains no benefit from the second's work with the first. If the seed was from the landowner instead, the entire arrangement becomes valid because it is effectively hiring two workers for a share of the produce, which is permissible. The passage ends by citing al-Muhit as a source.

Key Terms
التخلية (al-takhliyah): The legal handing over or vacating of the land to the cultivator, a condition for validity of muzara'ah.
العطف (al-'atf): Conjunction (grammatical 'and') which does not imply that the second part is a condition of the first.
المشايخ (al-mashayikh): The later authoritative scholars (mashayikh) of the Hanafi school, whose opinions are given weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where seed is from the worker, what is the ruling on the contract between the landowner and the first worker?
A) Valid, because the landowner gets a share.
B) Invalid, because the seed is from the worker, making it a forbidden partnership.
C) Invalid, but can be corrected if the landowner provides seed later.
D) Valid only if the seed is from the landowner.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a muzara'ah contract with a third party depends critically on who provides the seed and whether the secondary contract is stipulated as a condition.

Invalid Conditions in Muzara'ah: Fixed Measures, Canal Produce, Seed and Tax Deductions
Rulings on conditions that invalidate muzara'ah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that any condition cutting partnership invalidates muzara'ah, and apply it to fixed measures, canal produce, seed deduction, and kharaj payment.

Core Idea
Any stipulation that gives one party a fixed or separate share destroys the partnership nature of muzara'ah.

Muzara'ah is a partnership in the crop. In this lesson, we examine four conditions that the Hanafi school explicitly declares invalid because they break this partnership: stipulating a fixed quantity (qafizan), separate produce from canals (madhiyanat), removing the seed first, or paying the land tax (kharaj) from the produce before division. Each condition risks leaving one party with nothing if the crop is insufficient. The commentary also clarifies a permissible stratagem: stipulating a common share (juz' shai') for tax or seed does not invalidate the contract.

Guided Path
1
State the essential condition of muzara'ah
Identify that a valid muzara'ah requires the entire produce to be shared between the parties in a known proportion. Any condition that allocates a fixed or separate portion to one party undermines this.
This is the core principle from which all invalid conditions are derived.
2
Examine each invalid condition and its reasoning
For each condition (fixed measures, canal produce, seed deduction, tax deduction), state why it breaks partnership: it creates a separate claim that may exhaust the entire crop.
The text uses 'yaddī ilā qaṭʿ al-sharika' — leads to cutting off partnership.
3
Distinguish fixed share from common share
Note that a common share (juz' shāi') for seed or tax is permissible because it does not break partnership—it is simply a deduction from the joint pool.
This is a key nuance: the impermissible conditions are those that give a fixed amount or separate portion.
4
Apply to the straw-and-grain example
Stipulating straw for one and grain for the other is invalid because a calamity might leave only straw, breaking the partnership.
This demonstrates the risk-based reasoning of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من قبل قال رحمه الله : (أو اشترطا لاحدهما قفزاناً مسماة أو ما على الماذيات والسواقي أو أن يرفع رب البذر بذره أو يرفع من الخارج الخراج والباقي بينهما فسدت فإن صحت يرفع رب البذر بذره أو يرفع من الخارج الخراج والباقي بينهما فسدت) يعني لو شرطا لأحدهما قفزاناً معلومة تفسد لأنه يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة في المسمى كما تقدم أو مطلقاً لاحتمال ما يخرج إلا هو. والمراد بأحدهما هو أو من يعود نفعه إليه بالشرط. هذا إذا شرط لأحدهما، فلو شرطا لغيرهما قالوا ولو شرطا بعض الخارج لعبد أحدهما فلا يخلو إما أن يكون مشروطاً لمن يملك رب الأرض وللعامل كسبه كالغائب والقريب وكل قسم على وجهين : إما أن يكون البذر من قبل رب الأرض أو من قبل المزارع؛ أما القسم الأول ولو أرضاً أو بذراً على أن ثلث الخارج لرب الأرض وثلثه لعبده وثلثه للعامل جاز وشرط دفع عمل العبد أو لم يشترطا لأن ما شرطا للعبد شرط لسيده وإن شرط عمل العبد فالمشروط للعبد حتى يقضي منه ديونه والمولى ممنوع من أخذه فكان العبد كالأجنبي، فإن البذر من المزارع، فإن شرطا ثلث الخارج لعبد رب الأرض فالمزارعة جائزة إذا لم يكن على العبد دين ولم يشترط عمل العبد والمشروط للعبد مشروط لمولاه، وإن شرطا عمل العبد لمولاه، وإن شرطا عمل العبد ولادين عليه فالمزارعة فاسدة في ظاهر الرواية وإن كان على العبد دين ولم يشترط عمل العبد فالمزارعة جائزة ، وإن شرطا عمل العبد مع ذلك فالمزارعة فاسدة في ظاهر الرواية، وأما إذا شرطا الثلث لمكاتب أحدهما أو قريبة أو لأجنبي، فإن كان البذر من قبل رب الأرض إن شرط عمله جاز وقد تقدم بيانه. هذا إذا شرطا قفزاناً، فإذا شرطا كله قال : فلو شرط الخارج كله لأحدهما فإن كان البذر من قبل رب الأرض جاز والخارج كله للمشروط له فيكون العمل متبرعاً بعمله، وإن شرطاه للعامل جاز ويكون رب الأرض أعاره أرضه واستقرض بذره، فإن كان البذر من المزارع وشرطا جميع الخارج لأحدهما فهو على أربعة أوجه : الأول أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك فيكون الخارج كله لي فهو فاسد والخارج كله لرب البذر وعليه أجر مثل الأرض الثاني أن يقول كله لك والمسئلة بحالها جاز وصار معيراً أرضه منه . الثالث أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك على الخارج بيننا نصفان والبذر قرض على رب الأرض. والرابع أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك على أن تكون كله لك فهي فاسدة والخارج كله لرب الأرض وصار مستقرضاً للبذر وكذا في المحيط . وأما إذا شرطا لأحدهما ما على المأذيانات وهي مجرى الماء والسواقي أو يدفع رب البذر بذره أو يدفع الخراج فلأنه يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة في البعض أو الكل وشرط صحتها أن يكون الخارج مشتركاً بينهما. والمراد بالخراج الخراج الموظف نصفاً أو ثلثاً أو نحو ذلك، أما الجزء الشائع فلا يفسد اشتراطه لأنه لا يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة وهي حيلة لدفع قدر بذره. ولو شرطا لأحدهما التبن وللآخر الحب فسدت لاحتمال أن يصيب الزرع آفة فلا يخرج إلا التبن فلو شرطا الحب نصفين ولم يتعرض
From before, he said (may Allah have mercy on him): (Or if they stipulate for one of them specified measures (qafizans), or what is on the drainage channels and waterways, or that the seed owner takes his seed out, or that the land tax (kharaj) is taken from the produce and the rest is between them, it becomes invalid. If it becomes valid... the seed owner takes his seed or the land tax is taken and the rest is between them, it becomes invalid.) Meaning, if they stipulate for one of them specified measures, it invalidates because it leads to cutting off the partnership in the specified amount, as previously mentioned, or absolutely due to the possibility that what comes out is only that. And the meaning of 'one of them' is him or one whose benefit returns to him by stipulation. This is when they stipulate for one of them. If they stipulate for someone else, they said: If they stipulate some of the produce for the slave of one of them, then it is either stipulated for the one whom the landowner owns or for the worker's earning like the absent and the relative, and each division has two aspects: either the seed is from the landowner or from the cultivator. As for the first division: if land and seed are such that a third of the produce is for the landowner, a third for his slave, and a third for the worker, it is valid whether they stipulate the work of the slave or not, because what they stipulate for the slave is a condition for his master. If they stipulate the slave's work, then the stipulated (share) is for the slave until his debts are paid, and the master is prevented from taking it, so the slave becomes like a stranger. If the seed is from the cultivator, and they stipulate a third of the produce for the landowner's slave, the muzara'ah is valid if the slave has no debt and they did not stipulate the slave's work. If they stipulate the slave's work for his master, and there is no debt, then it is invalid in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). If the slave has debt and they do not stipulate his work, it is valid. If they stipulate his work along with that, it is invalid in the apparent narration. As for if they stipulate a third for the mukatab of one of them, or a relative, or a stranger: if the seed is from the landowner and they stipulate his work, it is valid, as previously explained. This is when they stipulate qafizans. If they stipulate all, he said: If they stipulate all the produce for one of them, then if the seed is from the landowner, it is valid and the produce is all for the stipulated party, so the worker becomes a volunteer with his work. If they stipulate it for the worker, it is valid, and the landowner lends him his land and borrows his seed. If the seed is from the cultivator and they stipulate all the produce for one of them, it has four aspects: first, if he says 'sow my land with your seed so that all produce is for me', it is invalid and all produce goes to the seed owner, who owes the landowner the rental value of the land. Second, if he says 'all for you' with the same case, it is valid, and he becomes a lender of his land. Third, if he says 'sow my land with your seed on condition that the produce is half and half between us, and the seed is a loan from the landowner' (this is valid?). Fourth, if he says 'sow my land with your seed on condition that it is all for you? Actually the text is unclear: 'على أن تكون كله لك' – it is invalid and all produce goes to the landowner, and he becomes a borrower of the seed. Similarly in al-Muhit. As for if they stipulate for one of them what is on the drainage channels (madhiyanat) which are watercourses and canals, or that the seed owner takes his seed, or that the land tax (kharaj) is paid, it leads to cutting off partnership in part or all, and the condition for validity is that the produce is shared between them. What is meant by kharaj is the fixed tax, half, third, or similar. As for a common share, stipulating it does not invalidate because it does not lead to cutting off partnership, and it is a stratagem to pay the amount of his seed. If they stipulate the straw for one and the grain for the other, it is invalid because of the possibility that a calamity may strike the crop so that only straw comes out. If they stipulate the grain half and half and do not mention...
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage enumerates conditions that invalidate a muzara'ah contract, as stated in the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The basic principle: any condition that breaks the partnership in the produce or gives a fixed or separate share to one party renders the contract invalid. Specifically, stipulating a fixed amount (qafizan) for one party is invalid because it precludes the possibility of actual partnership; if the crop fails, that fixed amount cannot be met. Stipulating the produce on drainage channels (madhiyanat) or irrigation ditches separately is invalid because it similarly disrupts the partnership. Stipulating that the seed owner removes his seed first before division, or that the land tax (kharaj) is paid from the produce before splitting, also invalidates the contract because it may leave nothing for the other party. The commentary then provides extensive details about stipulating shares for slaves, relatives, or strangers. If a share is stipulated for a slave, the validity depends on whether the slave has debts, whose work is stipulated, and who provides the seed. The key difference: when the slave is debt-free and his work is stipulated, the contract is invalid in zahir al-riwaya because the slave's earnings go to him until his debts are paid, separating them from the partnership. If the slave has debts, the share is considered for the master, and the contract is valid. The passage also covers cases where all produce is stipulated for one party: the ruling varies based on who provides seed and the specific wording. These are essentially disguised sales or loans. Finally, stipulating straw for one and grain for another is invalid because of the risk that only straw is produced.

Key Terms
قفزان (qafizan): A fixed measure of grain; stipulating a specific quantity for one party invalidates the contract.
الماذيات (al-madhiyanat): Drainage channels or waterways; stipulating their produce separately invalidates the contract.
الخراج (al-kharaj): Land tax (kharaj) imposed on agricultural land; stipulating that it be deducted from the produce before division is invalid unless it is a common share (juz' shai').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is stipulating a fixed quantity (qafizan) for one party invalid in muzara'ah?
A) Because it leads to uncertainty (gharar).
B) Because it cuts off the partnership in that quantity; if the crop yields only that amount, the other receives nothing.
C) Because it is like a sale, and muzara'ah requires a pure partnership.
D) Because it violates the condition of the narration (athar).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muzara'ah, any condition that allocates a fixed or separate portion of the produce breaks the partnership and invalidates the contract, unless it is a common share (juz' shāi') that preserves proportional sharing.

Complex Stipulations in Muzara'ah: Slaves, All Produce, and Third Parties
Rulings on stipulations for slaves, third parties, and all produce in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the validity of muzara'ah when stipulating shares for slaves, third parties, or all produce, based on seed source, debt, and work conditions.

Core Idea
Stipulations for slaves or third parties are valid only if they do not break partnership; stipulating all produce for one party may be a disguised transaction.

Building on the general rule that partnership must be preserved, this lesson explores more complex scenarios: stipulating shares for a slave, a third party like a relative or stranger, and stipulating the entire produce for one party. The rulings depend on who provides the seed, whether the slave has debt, and whether his work is stipulated. Understanding these nuances is essential for proper contract drafting and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the slave scenarios
The passage discusses cases where a share is stipulated for the landowner's slave. The validity depends on the seed source and whether the slave has debt and whose work is stipulated.
When the slave has debt, his share goes to creditors, effectively separating it from the partnership, which invalidates if his work is also stipulated.
2
Examine the 'all produce' cases
When all produce is stipulated for one party, the contract may be valid as a loan or invalid as a disguised sale. The seed owner determines the ruling.
Four sub-cases are given, each with different consequences.
3
Apply the partnership principle
In all cases, the key question: does the condition break the partnership (cutting off a share)? If yes, invalid; if no, valid.
Even when all produce goes to one party, if it is a loan (seed from that party), it is valid as a separate contract.
4
Note the source authority
The passage refers to 'zahir al-riwaya' for the invalid rulings on slave's work without debt, indicating these are the relied-upon positions.
This shows the epistemological weight of the ruling.

Source Text

In the case where the seed is from the cultivator and a share is stipulated for the landowner's slave, when is the contract valid?
A) When the slave has no debt and his work is stipulated.

beginner
6 min
Conditions That Invalidate Muzara'ah
Explaining conditions that cut partnership and invalidate the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four conditions that invalidate a muzara'ah contract and explain why they cut the partnership in produce.

Core Idea
A condition that gives one party a fixed share or specific produce cuts partnership and invalidates muzara'ah.

In a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract, the produce must be shared proportionally between the parties. This lesson examines specific conditions that violate this principle and render the contract fasid (invalid). By understanding these conditions, you will grasp the foundational requirement of partnership (sharika) in the produce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the muzara'ah contract. The ruling: if any of the listed conditions are stipulated, the contract becomes fasid (invalid).
The hukm level is fasid, not batil, because the invalidity is due to a corrupting condition, not a missing pillar.
2
List the invalid conditions
Four conditions: (1) a fixed qafiz for one party, (2) produce from waterways/canals for one party, (3) seed owner takes back his seed, (4) kharaj (land tax) is taken from external produce and the rest shared.
These conditions isolate a portion of the produce from the partnership.
3
Understand the 'illa (reason)
The illa is that these conditions cut the partnership (sharika) in the produce. Muzara'ah requires that all produce be shared in a common portion.
If the condition benefits a third party, it is still invalid because the benefit returns to the one who stipulated.
4
Apply the talil
For example, stipulating a fixed qafiz for one party removes that amount from the shared pool. If the harvest equals only that qafiz, the other party gets nothing, destroying the partnership.
The possibility of such injustice makes the condition invalid.
5
Note the scope and exceptions
The rule applies regardless of whether the condition benefits the party or someone else. The contract becomes fasid, but the invalid conditions may be removed to salvage it according to some Hanafi positions.
This is a ruling from zahir al-riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المزارعة لواحد والباقي لآخر أو اشترطا لاحدهما قفزاناً مسماة أو ما على الماذيات والسواقي أو أن يرفع رب البذر بذره أو يرفع من الخارج الخراج والباقي بينهما فسدت فإن صحت يرفع رب البذر بذره أو يرفع من الخارج الخراج والباقي بينهما فسدت) يعني لو شرطا لأحدهما قفزاناً معلومة تفسد لأنه يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة في المسمى كما تقدم أو مطلقاً لاحتمال ما يخرج إلا هو. والمراد بأحدهما هو أو من يعود نفعه إليه بالشرط. هذا إذا شرط لأحدهما
For one and the rest for another, or they stipulated for one of them specified qafizes, or what is on the waterways and canals, or that the owner of the seed takes his seed, or that the kharaj is taken from the external [produce] and the rest is between them, it becomes invalid. If it had been valid, the owner of the seed would take his seed, or the kharaj would be taken from the external and the rest between them, it becomes invalid. Meaning if they stipulated for one of them a known qafiz, it invalidates because it leads to cutting the partnership in the named [amount] as previously, or absolutely due to the possibility that only that [amount] emerges. And what is meant by 'one of them' is him or the one whose benefit returns to him by the condition. This is if they stipulated for one of them.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage discusses conditions that invalidate the muzara'ah contract. The author states that if the partners stipulate for one party a specified quantity (like qafiz) or something specific on the waterways, or that the seed owner takes back his seed, or that the kharaj is taken from the external produce and the rest is shared, the contract is invalid. The reason is that such conditions cut the partnership in the produce, which is the essence of the contract. In a valid muzara'ah, the produce must be shared between the parties in a common portion. A fixed quantity for one party eliminates the partnership in that portion, and if the crop fails, the stipulated amount might not exist, leading to injustice. The author clarifies that "one of them" includes the person himself or any beneficiary of the condition. So even if the condition benefits someone else, it is still invalid.

Key Terms
قفزاناً مسماة (qafizan musamma): specified measures of grain (qafiz) stipulated for one party
المأذيات (al-mādhayāt): waterways or canals used for irrigation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does stipulating a fixed qafiz for one party invalidate the muzara'ah contract?
A) Because the condition is unknown
B) Because it cuts the partnership in the produce
C) Because the seed owner must take his seed
D) Because the contract becomes an invalid lease

Key Takeaway
Any condition in a muzara'ah contract that isolates a fixed quantity or specific produce for one party cuts the required partnership and renders the contract fasid.

Stipulating Produce for a Slave in Muzara'ah
Detailed scenarios on stipulating produce for a third party in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which stipulating a share of produce for a slave in a muzara'ah contract is valid or invalid, and explain the effect of seed ownership, debt, and labor stipulation.

Core Idea
Stipulating produce for a slave is valid unless the slave has no debt and his labor is stipulated, which invalidates in zahir al-riwayah.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author details various scenarios when a share of the crop is stipulated for a third party such as a slave. The ruling hinges on three factors: whose seed is used, whether the slave has debts, and whether his labor is explicitly required. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi position on mu'amalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify parties and key variables
Note that the stipulation is for a slave of one of the parties (landowner or worker). The outcome depends on seed ownership (landowner or cultivator), slave's debt status, and whether the slave's labor is stipulated.
These three conditions determine validity.
2
Analyze when seed is from the landowner
If seed is from landowner and one-third each is stipulated for landowner, his slave, and worker, the contract is valid regardless of stipulating slave's labor because what goes to slave effectively goes to master. But if slave's labor is stipulated, the share is for the slave to pay debts, master prevented.
This shows the rule: slave's share belongs to master unless slave has debts.
3
Analyze when seed is from the cultivator
If seed from cultivator and one-third stipulated for landowner's slave, the contract is valid only if the slave has no debt and his labor is not stipulated. If slave has no debt and labor stipulated, invalid. If slave has debt and labor not stipulated, valid; if labor stipulated with debt, invalid.
Labor stipulation always invalidates when seed from cultivator.
4
Apply to other third parties
For a mukatab, relative, or stranger, if seed from landowner and their labor is stipulated, the contract is permissible. The same reasoning applies: their share is for them, and stipulating labor is fine.
Simpler rule: no invalidity from labor stipulation for non-slaves.
5
Summarize the underlying principle
The invalidity arises when the stipulation effectively creates an obligation on the slave to work without benefiting his creditors or master, making the contract akin to having two workers (the slave and the actual worker) with unclear shares.
This is the talil (reasoning) provided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو شرطا لغيرهما قالوا ولو شرطا بعض الخارج لعبد أحدهما فلا يخلو إما أن يكون مشروطاً لمن يملك رب الأرض وللعامل كسبه كالغائب والقريب وكل قسم على وجهين : إما أن يكون البذر من قبل رب الأرض أو من قبل المزارع؛ أما القسم الأول ولو أرضاً أو بذراً على أن ثلث الخارج لرب الأرض وثلثه لعبده وثلثه للعامل جاز وشرط دفع عمل العبد أو لم يشترطا لأن ما شرطا للعبد شرط لسيده وإن شرط عمل العبد فالمشروط للعبد حتى يقضي منه ديونه والمولى ممنوع من أخذه فكان العبد كالأجنبي، فإن البذر من المزارع، فإن شرطا ثلث الخارج لعبد رب الأرض فالمزارعة جائزة إذا لم يكن على العبد دين ولم يشترط عمل العبد والمشروط للعبد مشروط لمولاه، وإن شرطا عمل العبد لمولاه، وإن شرطا عمل العبد ولادين عليه فالمزارعة فاسدة في ظاهر الرواية وإن كان على العبد دين ولم يشترط عمل العبد فالمزارعة جائزة ، وإن شرطا عمل العبد مع ذلك فالمزارعة فاسدة في ظاهر الرواية، وأما إذا شرطا الثلث لمكاتب أحدهما أو قريبة أو لأجنبي، فإن كان البذر من قبل رب الأرض إن شرط عمله جاز وقد تقدم بيانه.
If they stipulated for others besides them, they said: And if they stipulated some of the produce for the slave of one of them, then it is not free from being either stipulated for the one who owns the land and the worker has his earning (like the absent and the relative), and each division has two aspects: either the seed is from the landowner or from the cultivator. As for the first division: if they stipulated land or seed with one-third of the produce for the landowner, one-third for his slave, and one-third for the worker, it is permissible, whether they stipulated the slave's labor or not, because what they stipulated for the slave is a stipulation for his master. If they stipulated the slave's labor, then what is stipulated for the slave is for the slave to pay off his debts, and the master is prevented from taking it, so the slave is like a stranger. If the seed is from the cultivator, and they stipulated one-third of the produce for the landowner's slave, then the muzara'ah is permissible if the slave has no debt and they did not stipulate the slave's labor, and what is stipulated for the slave is stipulated for his master. If they stipulated the slave's labor, then it is for his master. If they stipulated the slave's labor and he has no debt, then the muzara'ah is invalid in the apparent narration. If the slave has debt and they did not stipulate his labor, then the muzara'ah is permissible. If they stipulated his labor along with that, then the muzara'ah is invalid in the apparent narration. As for if they stipulated one-third for the mukatab of one of them, or his relative, or a stranger, if the seed is from the landowner and they stipulated his labor, it is permissible, and its explanation has preceded.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage deals with stipulating a share of the produce for a third party, such as a slave, a mukatab, a relative, or a stranger. The author provides a detailed breakdown based on whose seed is used and whether the slave's labor is stipulated. The key principle is that what is stipulated for the slave actually belongs to the master unless the slave has debts, in which case the slave keeps it to pay creditors. If the slave has no debts and his labor is stipulated, the contract becomes invalid in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) because it resembles a contract with two workers. If the seed is from the landowner and the slave is from his side, the contract is generally valid. For a mukatab or stranger, the ruling is simpler: if the seed is from the landowner and the third party's labor is stipulated, it is valid.

Key Terms
عبد (abd): slave owned by the landowner or worker
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): the apparent narration attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in his six books
مزارعة (muzara'ah): sharecropping contract where one party provides land, the other labor/seed, and they share the produce

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does stipulating one-third of the produce for the landowner's slave invalidate the muzara'ah contract?
A) When the slave has no debt and his labor is not stipulated
B) When the slave has no debt and his labor is stipulated
C) When the slave has debt and his labor is stipulated
D) When the seed is from the cultivator

Key Takeaway
The validity of stipulating produce for a slave in muzara'ah depends on seed ownership, slave's debt, and whether his labor is stipulated; zahir al-riwayah invalidates only when seed is from the cultivator and labor is stipulated.

Stipulating All Produce When Seed is from the Landowner
Ruling on two permissible scenarios when seed is from the landowner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the seed is from the landowner and all produce is stipulated for one party, and explain why both scenarios are valid.

Core Idea
When the landowner provides the seed, any stipulation of the entire produce is valid based on ariyah and qard.

The passage begins by examining cases where the seed belongs to the landowner. In such a situation, the contract can be structured in two permissible ways: either the produce goes entirely to the landowner, making the worker a volunteer, or entirely to the worker, turning the arrangement into a loan of land and seed. Understanding these two scenarios clarifies that invalidity arises only when the seed is from the worker and the terms create uncertainty or contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seed provider
Focus on the condition 'if the seed is from the landowner'. This is the key variable that determines validity.
2
Analyze the two stipulations
First: produce stipulated for the landowner. The worker's labor becomes voluntary (tabarru'). Second: produce stipulated for the worker. The landowner is considered to have lent his land (ariyah) and borrowed the seed (qard).
Both are valid (ja'iz) despite the extreme outcomes.
3
Understand the legal recharacterization
The contracts are not treated as invalid sharecropping (muzara'ah) because the seed ownership eliminates the uncertainty (gharar) that normally invalidates such stipulations.
The worker either volunteers or receives the land as a loan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا شرطا كله قال : فلو شرط الخارج كله لأحدهما فإن كان البذر من قبل رب الأرض جاز والخارج كله للمشروط له فيكون العمل متبرعاً بعمله، وإن شرطاه للعامل جاز ويكون رب الأرض أعاره أرضه واستقرض بذره، فإن كان البذر من المزارع وشرطا جميع الخارج لأحدهما فهو على أربعة أوجه : الأول أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك فيكون الخارج كله لي فهو فاسد والخارج كله لرب البذر وعليه أجر مثل الأرض الثاني أن يقول كله لك والمسئلة بحالها جاز وصار معيراً أرضه منه . الثالث أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك على الخارج بيننا نصفان والبذر قرض على رب الأرض. والرابع أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك على أن تكون كله لك فهي فاسدة والخارج كله لرب الأرض وصار مستقرضاً للبذر وكذا في المحيط .
If they stipulated the whole [produce], he said: If they stipulated all the produce for one of them, then if the seed is from the landowner, it is permissible and the entire produce is for the one stipulated for, so the worker becomes a volunteer with his labor. If they stipulated it for the worker, it is permissible, and the landowner would have lent him his land and borrowed his seed. If the seed is from the cultivator and they stipulated all the produce for one of them, then it has four aspects: First: He says 'Plant my land with your seed so that all the produce is mine' – it is invalid, and all the produce belongs to the seed owner, and he must pay the fair rent of the land. Second: He says 'All is for you' – the situation is the same, it is permissible, and he becomes a lender of his land to him. Third: He says 'Plant my land with your seed on the basis that the produce is half between us, and the seed is a loan upon the landowner' – permissible. Fourth: He says 'Plant my land with your seed on the basis that it all belongs to you' – it is invalid, and all the produce belongs to the landowner, and he becomes a borrower of the seed. And similarly in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage addresses scenarios where the entire produce is stipulated for one party. The ruling depends on who provides the seed. If the seed is from the landowner, stipulating all produce for either party is valid because the worker's labor is considered voluntary or the landowner is lending. If the seed is from the worker, four cases arise. In the first, the landowner says 'plant my land with your seed, all produce for me' – invalid because the worker risks his seed without guarantee of return; the worker gets all produce but must pay land rent. The second case, which is valid, is when the landowner says 'all for you' – this is an 'ariyah (loan) of land. The third case, also valid, is a proper muzara'ah with half shares and the seed as a loan from worker to landowner. The fourth case is invalid: the landowner says 'all for you' but the seed is from worker; the produce goes to landowner and he must repay the seed as a loan.

Key Terms
عارية (ariyah): Loan of land without rent.
قرض (qard): Loan of seed, to be returned in kind or value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the seed is from the landowner and all produce is stipulated for the worker, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Invalid, because it is a forbidden sharecropping contract.
B) Valid, and it is considered a loan of land and a loan of seed.
C) Valid, as a proper muzara'ah contract.
D) Invalid, due to uncertainty (gharar) about the worker's share.

Key Takeaway
When seed is from the landowner, stipulating all produce for either party is valid, recharacterized as a loan (ariyah/qard) or voluntary work.
