Stipulating All Produce When Seed is from the Worker
Classification of four cases when seed is from the worker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four cases when seed is from the worker, state which are valid and which are invalid, and apply the rulings to new scenarios.

Core Idea
When the worker provides seed, only two of four stipulations are valid: clear gift or proper sharecropping.

This lesson examines the four scenarios when the seed belongs to the worker. The rulings depend on the wording of the contract. Two arrangements are valid because they avoid uncertainty (gharar) or are recharacterized as loans, while two are invalid due to contradiction or unfairness. Understanding these distinctions is essential for drafting valid agricultural contracts in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seed provider
Now the seed is from the worker (muzari'). This changes the analysis fundamentally.
2
List the four cases
Case 1: Landowner says 'all produce for me' - invalid. Case 2: Landowner says 'all produce for you' - valid. Case 3: Half-and-half with seed as loan - valid. Case 4: Landowner says 'all produce for you' but with condition - invalid.
Cases 2 and 3 are valid; 1 and 4 are invalid.
3
Analyze the invalid cases
Case 1 is invalid because the worker risks his seed with no guarantee. Produce goes to seed owner (worker) and he pays land rent. Case 4 is invalid because it is a muzara'ah contract with a condition that contradicts its nature; produce goes to landowner and he must repay seed.
The difference between Case 2 and 4 is the phrasing: Case 2 is an outright gift, Case 4 is a conditional contract.
4
Understand the valid cases
Case 2 is valid as an ariyah (loan of land) - worker gets all produce. Case 3 is a valid muzara'ah with seed as loan from worker to landowner.
Both valid cases eliminate gharar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا شرطا كله قال : فلو شرط الخارج كله لأحدهما فإن كان البذر من قبل رب الأرض جاز والخارج كله للمشروط له فيكون العمل متبرعاً بعمله، وإن شرطاه للعامل جاز ويكون رب الأرض أعاره أرضه واستقرض بذره، فإن كان البذر من المزارع وشرطا جميع الخارج لأحدهما فهو على أربعة أوجه : الأول أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك فيكون الخارج كله لي فهو فاسد والخارج كله لرب البذر وعليه أجر مثل الأرض الثاني أن يقول كله لك والمسئلة بحالها جاز وصار معيراً أرضه منه . الثالث أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك على الخارج بيننا نصفان والبذر قرض على رب الأرض. والرابع أن يقول ازرع أرضي ببذرك على أن تكون كله لك فهي فاسدة والخارج كله لرب الأرض وصار مستقرضاً للبذر وكذا في المحيط .
If they stipulated the whole [produce], he said: If they stipulated all the produce for one of them, then if the seed is from the landowner, it is permissible and the entire produce is for the one stipulated for, so the worker becomes a volunteer with his labor. If they stipulated it for the worker, it is permissible, and the landowner would have lent him his land and borrowed his seed. If the seed is from the cultivator and they stipulated all the produce for one of them, then it has four aspects: First: He says 'Plant my land with your seed so that all the produce is mine' – it is invalid, and all the produce belongs to the seed owner, and he must pay the fair rent of the land. And similarly in al-Muhit.

Commentary
This passage addresses scenarios where the entire produce is stipulated for one party. The ruling depends on who provides the seed. If the seed is from the landowner, stipulating all produce for either party is valid because the worker's labor is considered voluntary or the landowner is lending. If the seed is from the worker, four cases arise. In the first, the landowner says 'plant my land with your seed, all produce for me' – invalid because the worker risks his seed without guarantee of return; the worker gets all produce but must pay land rent. The second case, which is valid, is when the landowner says 'all for you' – this is an 'ariyah (loan) of land. Key Terms

قرض (qard): Loan of seed, to be returned in kind or value.
مزارعة (muzara'ah): Sharecropping contract where landowner provides land and worker provides labor, with produce shared.

Checkpoint
In which of the four cases (seed from worker) does the landowner get all the produce?
A) Case 1
B) Case 2
C) Case 3
D) Case 4

Key Takeaway
When seed is from the worker, only clear gifts (case 2) and proper sharecropping with seed as loan (case 3) are valid; claims of all produce by landowner (case 1) or conditional gifts (case 4) are invalid.

Stipulating Straw and Grain in Muzara'ah
Rulings on conditions that invalidate or are valid in muzara'ah regarding straw and grain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which stipulations regarding straw and grain in a muzara'ah contract are valid and which are invalid, and explain the reasoning based on the principle of preserving partnership.

Core Idea
Stipulating straw for one party and grain for the other is invalid because a blight could leave only straw, cutting the partnership.

In a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract, the basic requirement is that the produce must be shared. This lesson explores several conditions that may be stipulated by the parties. We will see that some conditions, like giving all straw to the landowner, are valid, while others, like giving straw to the worker, are invalid. The key is whether the condition risks cutting the partnership between the parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions mentioned
List all the conditions the passage addresses: proceeds from waterways, seed return, kharaj payment, and straw/grain allocation. Note that some are invalid and some are valid.
Waterways, seed, kharaj conditions are invalid; common portion of kharaj is a hila.
2
Apply the partnership principle
The governing principle is that any condition that could cut the partnership in part or whole invalidates the contract. Evaluate each condition against this principle.
Stipulating straw for worker and grain for landowner could cut partnership if only straw forms.
3
Distinguish valid vs. invalid straw/grain stipulations
Straw for landowner is valid (it is an appendage of his property); straw for worker is invalid; if straw is not mentioned, it is halved along with grain.
The hila for seed repayment uses a common portion of kharaj.
4
Identify the hila (stratagem) for seed repayment
Stipulating a common portion (e.g., half) of the fixed kharaj does not invalidate the contract and serves as a lawful means to recover the seed cost.
This avoids cutting partnership because it is a shared apportionment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا شرطا لأحدهما ما على المأذيانات وهي مجرى الماء والسواقي أو يدفع رب البذر بذره أو يدفع الخراج فلأنه يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة في البعض أو الكل وشرط صحتها أن يكون الخارج مشتركاً بينهما. والمراد بالخراج الخراج الموظف نصفاً أو ثلثاً أو نحو ذلك، أما الجزء الشائع فلا يفسد اشتراطه لأنه لا يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة وهي حيلة لدفع قدر بذره. ولو شرطا لأحدهما التبن وللآخر الحب فسدت لاحتمال أن يصيب الزرع آفة فلا يخرج إلا التبن فلو شرطا الحب نصفين ولم يتعرض للتبن صحت لأنه هو المقصود والتبن نصفان ولو شرطا الحب نصفين والتين لرب الأرض صحت لأنه شرط لا يخالفه العقد لأنه نماء ملكه ولو شرطا التبن للعامل فسد فلأنه شرط مخالف لمقتضى العقد فربما يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة بأن يصيب الزرع آفة فلا ينعقد الحب ولا يخرج إلا التبن قال : والعشر عليهما عندهما، وعند الإمام على صاحب الأرض، فإن لم يأخذ الإمام العشر فهو لصاحب الأرض عند الإمام وعندهما لهما ولو قال صاحب الأرض للعامل لا أدري ما يأخذ الإمام العشر أو النصف لأن النصف لي بعدما يأخذ جازت عندهما؛ كذا في المحيط
As for if they stipulated for one of them what is on the waterways, which is the course of water and canals, or that the owner of the seed pays his seed, or that he pays the kharaj, then because it leads to cutting the partnership in part or all, and the condition of its validity is that the produce is shared between them. What is meant by kharaj is the fixed kharaj, half, one-third, or the like. As for a common portion, its stipulation does not invalidate because it does not lead to cutting the partnership, and it is a stratagem to pay the amount of his seed. And if they stipulated the straw for one of them and the grain for the other, it is invalid due to the possibility that a blight may affect the crop and nothing but straw comes out. If they stipulated the grain in halves and did not mention the straw, it is valid because it [grain] is the intended object, and the straw is halved. If they stipulated the grain in halves and the straw for the landowner, it is valid because it is a condition that does not contradict the contract, as it is the growth of his property. If they stipulated the straw for the worker, it is invalid because it is a condition contradictory to the requirement of the contract, and perhaps it leads to cutting the partnership because a blight may affect the crop so that no grain forms and only straw emerges. He said: The tithe ('ushr) is upon both according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is upon the landowner. If the Imam does not take the tithe, it belongs to the landowner according to Imam, and according to them it belongs to both. If the landowner says to the worker, 'I do not know what the Imam will take, the tithe or the half, because half of it is for me after what is taken,' it is valid according to them. Similarly in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage covers several related rulings. First, it reiterates that stipulating for one party the produce from waterways, or the return of the seed, or payment of kharaj, invalidates because it cuts partnership. However, stipulating a common portion (like half the kharaj) is valid and can be a stratagem (hila) to recover the seed. Second, it discusses stipulating straw (تبن) and grain (حب). If they stipulate straw for one and grain for the other, it is invalid due to the risk that only straw comes out. If they stipulate grain half and half without mentioning straw, it is valid; straw is then also halved. Stipulating straw for the landowner is valid because it is an appendage of his property. Stipulating straw for the worker is invalid because it contradicts the contract's requirement of sharing the main produce. Third, the 'ushr (tithe) is a tax: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is shared between landowner and worker proportionally; according to Abu Hanifa, it is solely on the landowner. If the tithe is not collected, it belongs to the landowner per Imam, or to both per Sahibayn. If the landowner expresses uncertainty about the tax rate and says 'half is mine after deduction,' the contract is valid according to Sahibayn.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): fixed land tax imposed by the state
تبن (tibn): straw, the byproduct of grain

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is stipulating straw for the worker invalid but for the landowner valid?
A) Because the worker does not own the land
B) Because if blight strikes, only straw may come out, cutting the partnership
C) Because straw is worth more than grain
D) Because the landowner's share is always protected

Key Takeaway
A condition in muzara'ah is valid only if it does not cut the partnership; straw allocated to the worker risks this and is invalid, while for the landowner it is valid.

The Dispute on 'Ushr Liability in Muzara'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on who is liable for 'ushr in a muzara'ah contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the liability for 'ushr (tithe) in a muzara'ah contract and explain the practical difference.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds 'ushr is solely on the landowner; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it shared between landowner and worker.

In addition to the sharecropping arrangement, the state levies a tithe ('ushr) on the land. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on who bears this tax. This lesson presents the arguments of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this difference is crucial for drafting valid contracts and knowing who benefits if the tax is not collected.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
The passage presents two positions: one from Abu Hanifa (Imam) and one from his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). The issue is who bears the 'ushr tax.
'Ushr is an Islamic land tax of 10% on agricultural produce.
2
Present the position of the Sahibayn
According to them, the 'ushr is upon both parties (landowner and worker). This means it is deducted from the total produce before division or shared proportionally.
The text says 'al-'ushr alayhima 'indahuma'.
3
Present the position of Abu Hanifa
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the 'ushr is solely upon the landowner (sahib al-ard). The worker is not liable for the tax.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in later Hanafi scholarship.
4
Analyze the consequence if the tax is not collected
If the Imam does not take the 'ushr, per Abu Hanifa the amount belongs to the landowner; per Sahibayn it belongs to both parties. This shows the tax liability translates to ownership of the untaxed portion.
This highlights the practical difference: who gains the windfall?
5
Examine the contract validity with uncertainty
The passage ends with a case: if the landowner says 'I don't know what the Imam will take, but half is mine after deduction', the contract is valid according to the Sahibayn. This shows flexibility in stipulating shares when tax rate is unknown.
This ruling is from al-Muhit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

As for if they stipulated for one of them what is on the waterways, which is the course of water and canals, or that the owner of the seed pays his seed, or that he pays the kharaj, then because it leads to cutting the partnership in part or all, and the condition of its validity is that the produce is shared between them. What is meant by kharaj is the fixed kharaj, half, one-third, or the like. As for a common portion, its stipulation does not invalidate because it does not lead to cutting the partnership, and it is a stratagem to pay the amount of his seed. And if they stipulated the straw for one of them and the grain for the other, it is invalid due to the possibility that a blight may affect the crop and nothing but straw comes out. If they stipulated the grain in halves and did not mention the straw, it is valid because it [grain] is the intended object, and the straw is halved. If they stipulated the grain in halves and the straw for the landowner, it is valid because it is a condition that does not contradict the contract, as it is the growth of his property. If they stipulated the straw for the worker, it is invalid because it is a condition contradictory to the requirement of the contract, and perhaps it leads to cutting the partnership because a blight may affect the crop so that no grain forms and only straw emerges. He said: The tithe ('ushr) is upon both according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is upon the landowner. If the Imam does not take the tithe, it belongs to the landowner according to Imam, and according to them it belongs to both. If the landowner says to the worker, 'I do not know what the Imam will take, the tithe or the half, because half of it is for me after what is taken,' it is valid according to them. Similarly in al-Muhit.

Commentary
This passage covers several related rulings. First, it reiterates that stipulating for one party the produce from waterways, or the return of the seed, or payment of kharaj, invalidates because it cuts partnership. However, stipulating a common portion (like half the kharaj) is valid and can be a stratagem (hila) to recover the seed. Second, it discusses stipulating straw (تبن) and grain (حب). If they stipulate straw for one and grain for the other, it is invalid due to the risk that only straw comes out. Stipulating straw for the worker is invalid because it contradicts the contract's requirement of sharing the main produce. Third, the 'ushr (tithe) is a tax: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is shared between landowner and worker proportionally; according to Abu Hanifa, it is solely on the landowner. If the tithe is not collected, it belongs to the landowner per Imam, or to both per Sahibayn. If the landowner expresses uncertainty about the tax rate and says 'half is mine after deduction,' the contract is valid according to Sahibayn.

Key Terms
عشر ('ushr): the Islamic tithe on agricultural produce, typically 10% or 5% depending on irrigation
صاحب الأرض (sahib al-ard): the landowner

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if the 'ushr is not collected, who owns the amount that would have been tithed?
A) The landowner only
B) The worker only
C) Both parties
D) The state

Key Takeaway
The liability for 'ushr in muzara'ah is disputed: Abu Hanifa places it on the landowner, while the Sahibayn place it on both; the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.

The Validity of Stipulating Crop Type and Giving Options in Muzara'ah
Rulings on stipulating crop type and giving options in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and fasid conditions regarding crop specification in muzara'ah and apply the Hanafi rulings on choice (takhayyur).

Core Idea
Clear wording or limited choice makes a crop condition valid; ambiguity or unlimited options render it fasid.

In this passage, the commentator of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq elaborates on the rulings when a landowner specifies the crop to be planted or gives the worker options. The validity hinges on the clarity of the stipulation and the presence of uncertainty (jahalah). We'll explore the scenarios and understand the role of istihsan (juristic preference) in upholding certain flexible conditions that would otherwise be invalid by qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key scenarios
The passage presents three main divisions: (1) different levels of worker effort with corresponding shares, (2) specifying crop type with choice, and (3) timing conditions. Each has distinct rulings.
Focus on the second division as it is the core of the lesson.
2
Analyze the wording that leads to validity
For crop specification, phrases like 'Plant it' (ازرعها) or 'You planted in it' (زرعت فيها) give the worker a clear choice among the specified crops. This is valid because the subject matter is determinable.
The phrase 'You planted from it' (زرعت منها) is also valid.
3
Analyze the wording that leads to fasid
Phrases like 'Whatever you plant from it' (ما زرعت منها) or 'Some of it' (بعضاً منها) introduce uncertainty about the mix of crops. This jahalah makes the contract fasid.
Uncertainty in the crop mix invalidates because the shares cannot be determined.
4
Understand the role of istihsan
A special case: if the worker provides seed and the share varies depending on crop (e.g., wheat gives half, barley gives worker all), it is valid by istihsan. Qiyas would view it as a single contract with two different rulings, but istihsan allows it to be treated as two separate contracts (muzara'ah for wheat, loan of land for barley).
Istihsan overrides qiyas for practical flexibility.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
On the timing condition (planting in early Jumada or later), Abu Hanifa considers both conditions fasid due to gharar, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad uphold them as valid. The mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.
Also, Hisham narrates that choice among more than three crops is not allowed, but Muhammad did not explicitly state this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وفيه أيضاً : لو دفع الأرض والبذر سنة على أن يزرعها بغير كراب فللعامل ربع الخارج وإن كربها فثلثه وإن كرب وبنى فنصفه جاز ما شرطاه، وكذا لو كان البذر من جهة المزارع القسم الثاني دفع الأرض على أن يزرعها حنطة فالخارج كذا، وإن زرعها شعيراً فكذا وإن زرعها سمسماً فكذا فهذا على أربعة أوجه : أما إن قال ازرعها أو زرعت فيها أو زرعت منها أو زرعت بعضاً منها فالمزارعة في الأولين جائزة لأنه خيره بين العقود الثلاثة، فإن زرع شيئاً من الأصناف الثلاثة فالخارج على ما شرطاه، ولو قال ما زرعت منها أو بعضاً منها فالمزارعة فاسدة لأنه إن زرع البعض حنطة والبعض شعيراً وسمسماً فذلك البعض مجهول، ولو كان البذر من قبل العامل وشرط إن زرعها حنطة فبينهما نصفان وإن زرعها شعيراً فذلك للعامل جاز استحساناً وهو في الأول مزارعة وفي الثاني إعارة الأرض . ثم ذكر محمد التخيير بين ثلاثة ولم يذكر هل يجوز التخيير في أكثر من ذلك؟ روى هشام أنه لا يجوز القسم الثالث دفع الأرض على أن زرعها ببذره في أول جمادى الاولى فالخارج نصفان وإن أخر فالثلث للمزارع فالشرطان جائزان عندهما وبيان الدليل يطلب فيه اهـ .
He said, and in it also: If he gives the land and seed for one year on condition that he plants it without plowing, then the worker gets one-quarter of the produce; if he plows it, then one-third; if he plows and builds [embankments], then half – whatever they stipulated is valid. And similarly if the seed is from the cultivator. The second division: He gives the land on condition that he plants it with wheat, so the produce is thus; if he plants it with barley, then thus; if he plants it with sesame, then thus – and this has four aspects: As for if he says ‘Plant it’ or ‘you planted in it’ or ‘you planted from it’ or ‘you planted some of it’ – then the muzara'ah in the first two is valid because he gives him a choice among the three contracts; if he plants any of the three varieties, the produce is as they stipulated. If he says ‘whatever you planted from it’ or ‘some of it’, then the muzara'ah is invalid because if he plants some wheat, some barley, and some sesame, then that part is unknown. And if the seed is from the worker and he stipulates: if he plants it with wheat, then half between them; if he plants it with barley, then all for the worker – it is valid by istihsan; in the first it is muzara'ah, in the second it is a loan of land. Then Muhammad mentioned the choice among three and did not mention whether choice among more than that is permissible? Hisham narrated that it is not permissible. The third division: He gives the land on condition that he plants it with his seed in the first Jumada al-Ula, so the produce is half and half; if he delays, then one-third for the cultivator – both conditions are valid according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the evidence is sought therein.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage covers several scenarios related to specifying or choosing the type of crop to be planted. The first scenario involves different levels of worker effort (no plowing, plowing, plowing and building) with corresponding shares – valid as stipulated. The second division is when the landowner specifies a particular crop (wheat, barley, sesame) but gives the worker options. If the wording is clear (e.g., 'plant it' or 'you planted in it'), the contract is valid; if ambiguous ('whatever you planted from it'), it is invalid due to uncertainty. A special case where the seed is from the worker and the share differs depending on the crop is valid by istihsan (juristic preference). If the worker plants wheat, it's muzara'ah with half shares; if barley, it's a loan of land (the worker keeps all). Then, Imam Muhammad discusses choice among three crops; Hisham's narration says more than three is not allowed. The third division deals with timing: if the worker plants in early Jumada, shares are half; later, one-third – both conditions are valid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, implying istihsan over qiyas.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): juristic preference overriding qiyas for a specific case
تخيير (takhayyur): giving the worker a choice among crops

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes the contract invalid in the second division of specifying crop type?
A) Saying 'Plant it with wheat'
B) Saying 'Plant it with wheat or barley'
C) Saying 'Whatever you plant from it'
D) Saying 'Plant it with seed from the worker'

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muzara'ah, stipulating a specific crop or giving a clear, limited choice is valid; ambiguous terms that create uncertainty invalidate the contract.

No Produce, No Pay in Valid Muzara'ah
Ruling and reasoning for worker's compensation when crop fails in valid muzara'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a valid muzara'ah yields no produce and explain the legal reasoning (ijarah vs shirkah) that justifies the worker receiving nothing.

Core Idea
In valid muzara'ah, worker's compensation is tied to produce; no produce means no pay.

This passage from Al-Hidayah concludes the discussion of muzara'ah by addressing a crucial scenario: what happens when the land yields nothing? The author, al-Marghinani, provides a crisp legal analysis: the contract is either a hire (ijarah) or a partnership (shirkah). In either construction, the worker's entitlement is conditional on the existence of produce. The text then hints at a distinction from an invalid contract, where the worker might receive a fair wage. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage addresses a valid muzara'ah contract where no produce emerges from the land. The ruling is explicit: the worker gets nothing.
This is the default outcome in a valid contract.
2
Recognize the two legal constructions
The author reasons that a valid muzara'ah can be analyzed either as a hire (ijarah) of the worker's labor in exchange for a share of produce, or as a partnership (shirkah) in the produce itself.
Both constructions tie compensation to the existence of produce.
3
Apply the ijarah analysis
If it is ijarah, the named compensation (the share) is the agreed rent. Since the produce is non-existent, the named compensation is also non-existent; the worker cannot claim anything else because the contract is valid and the subject matter is absent.
In ijarah, the rent must be specified and existing at the time of payment.
4
Apply the shirkah analysis
If it is shirkah, the partnership is only in the external produce (al-kharij). Since there is no external produce, there is no subject matter for the partnership, so the worker has no claim to any share.
Shirkah in muzara'ah is strictly limited to what the land produces.
5
Contrast with an invalid contract
The passage signals a contrast: 'bikhilaf ma idha fasadat al-muzara'ah' – unlike when the contract is invalid. In that case, the worker would receive ujrat al-mithl (fair wage) for his labor, even without produce, because the invalid contract does not limit compensation to the share.
This distinction is critical for understanding the risk allocation in valid vs. invalid contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن لم يخرج شيء فلا شيء للعامل لأنها إما اجاره أو شركة، فإن كانت اجارة فالواجب في العقد الصحيح منها المسمى وهو معدوم فلا يستحق غيره، وإن كانت شركة فالشركة في الخارج دون غيره فلا يستحق غيره بخلاف ما إذا فسدت المزارعة ولم
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (If nothing comes out, then there is nothing for the worker, because it is either a hire or a partnership. If it is a hire, then the obligatory [payment] in a valid contract is the named [rent], which is non-existent, so he does not deserve anything else. If it is a partnership, then the partnership is in the produce only, not in other things, so he does not deserve anything else. Unlike when the muzara'ah is invalid and he [did not...].
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This final ruling addresses the situation where the land produces nothing. The worker's compensation depends on the nature of the contract. If the muzara'ah is valid, it can be considered either a hire (ijarah) of the worker's labor with a share of produce as payment, or a partnership (shirkah) in the produce. In either case, the worker's entitlement is contingent on the existence of produce. If no produce exists, the worker gets nothing because the promised share is absent. The author distinguishes this from an invalid contract (muzara'ah fasidah), where the worker might be entitled to the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) for his labor even if no produce results. However, the text breaks off before fully explaining the contrast, but the principle is clear: in a valid muzara'ah, no produce means no payment for the worker.

Key Terms
اجارة (ijarah): hire of labor; here, the worker's labor is hired in exchange for a share of produce
شركة (shirkah): partnership in the produce

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a valid muzara'ah yields no produce, what does the worker receive?
A) A fair wage for his labor
B) Nothing
C) Half of the seed
D) Rent from the landowner

Key Takeaway
In a valid muzara'ah, no produce means the worker receives nothing, because his compensation is conditional on the existence of the crop.

Ruling on Expiry of Muzara'ah Before Crop is Ripe
States the ruling for when the muzara'ah term ends but crop is unripe

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the muzara'ah term expires before the crop ripens and explain the role of istihsan in imposing ujrat al-mithl on the worker for the landowner's share only.

Core Idea
When muzara'ah ends but the crop is unripe, the worker pays ujrat al-mithl only for the landowner's share — preservation by istihsan.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a common point of confusion in sharecropping (muzara'ah). If the contract term ends before the crop is ready to harvest, the worker cannot be forced to uproot the crop, as that would cause loss. Instead, by istihsan, the arrangement continues until harvest, but the worker must compensate the landowner by paying the equivalent rent (ujrat al-mithl) for the landowner's share of the land during the extra period. The commentary corrects a potential misreading of the base text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the apparent ruling
Read the passage's opening: the author says the worker must pay ujrat al-mithl for the land until the crop ripens. Take note of the apparent meaning — that the worker must pay rent for the entire land.
The base text seems to impose a blanket rent obligation.
2
Distinguish the correct interpretation
The commentator warns that the apparent wording is misleading. The rent is not for the whole land but only for the landowner's share. The worker already owns a share of the crop, so he does not need to pay rent for his own portion of the land.
Correction: 'if he said in his share it would be more appropriate'.
3
Understand the dalil (istihsan)
The reasoning for not uprooting the crop is istihsan: uprooting causes harm (darar) to both parties. Preserving the crop by allowing it to ripen is preferred. However, this continued use of the land requires compensation to the landowner.
Istihsan overrides strict contract termination.
4
Apply the exception: worker's death
If the worker dies before ripening, no rent is owed. The contract is preserved only enough to let the crop mature, but the worker is not liable because the lease element is not continued against him or his heirs.
Death case is distinguished: no rent needed.
5
Examine additional sub-rulings
The passage also covers: spending without judge's order is voluntary; landowner cannot take crop as greens unilaterally; absent worker loses access until paying expenses; disputes over expenses are decided by the worker's oath.
These are all based on the same principle of avoiding harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن مضت المدة والزرع لم يدرك فعلى الزارع أجر مثل أرضه حتى يدرك) يعني يجب على العامل أجر مثل أرض الآخر حتى يستحصد، وظاهر العبارة أنه يجب الأجرة وليس كذلك فلو قال في نصيبه لكان أولى وأسلم لأن العقد قد انتهى بمضي المدة وفي القلع ضرر فبقيناه بأجر المثل إلى أن يستحصد فيجب على غير صاحب الأرض بحصته من الأجرة لأنه استوفى منفعة الأرض بقدره بخلاف ما لو مات قبل ادراك الزرع حيث يترك إلى الحصاد ولا يجب على المزارع شيء لأنا أبقينا عقد الأجارة هنا استحساناً فأمكن استمرار العامل على ما كان من العمل، أما هنا لا يمكن إلا بانقضاء المدة فتعين ايجاب أجر المثل بالإيفاء وكان العمل ونفقة الزرع وموته بالحفظ وكري الأنهار عليهما بخلاف ما إذا مات قبل الإدراك حيث يكون الكل على العامل ولو أنفق أحدهما على الزرع بغير أمر القاضي وبغير أمر صاحبه فهو متطوع لأنه لا ولاية له عليه وهو غير مضطر إلى ذلك لأنه يمكنه أن ينفق بأمر القاضي فصار نظير ترميم الدار المشترك. ولو أراد رب الأرض أن يأخذ الزرع بقلاً ليس له لما فيه من الاضطرار بالآخر، ولو أراد الزارع أن يأخذه بقلاً قيل لصاحب الأرض اقلع الزرع إن شئت فيكون بينكما أو اعطه قيمة نصيبه أو أنفق أنت على الزرع وارجع عليه بما أنفقت عليه دفعاً للضرر عنه قال : ولا يضمن المزارع أجر مثل الأرض لأنه لما رضي بإبطال حقه لم تبق الاجارة بينهما. ولو غاب المزارع بعد ما زرع فأنفق رب الأرض إلى الأدراك بأمر القاضي رجع ولا سبيل للزارع على الزرع حتى يعطيه النفقة كلها لأن الزارع لو كان حاضراً كان الكل عليه فكذا لو غاب ولو اختلفا في النفقة فالقول قول الزارع مع يمينه لأنه ينكر وإذا انقضت المدة قبل الإدراك فمن أنفق منهما بغير إذن القاضي فهو متطوع، وإن أنفق بأمر القاضي رجع بنصف ما أنفق.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'If the period passes and the crop has not yet ripened, then the sharecropper must pay the equivalent rent of his land until it ripens.' Meaning: The worker must pay the equivalent rent of the other's land until the harvest is complete. The apparent wording indicates that the rent is obligatory, but it is not so. If he said 'in his share' it would be more appropriate and safer. Because the contract has ended with the expiry of the period, and in uprooting there is harm, so we keep it with equivalent rent until harvest. Thus it is obligatory on the one who is not the owner of the land to pay his share of the rent because he utilized the benefit of the land to that extent. Unlike if he died before the crop ripens, where it is left until harvest and nothing is owed by the sharecropper, because we preserved the lease contract here by istihsan, so it became possible for the worker to continue with the work he was doing. Here it is not possible except with the expiry of the period, so it was determined to impose equivalent rent for the benefit. And the work, expenses of the crop, its preservation, and digging canals are upon both. Unlike if he died before ripening, where everything is on the worker. If one of them spends on the crop without the judge's order and without the partner's order, he is a volunteer because he has no authority over it and he is not compelled to that because he can spend by the judge's order. So it becomes analogous to repairing a shared house. If the landowner wants to take the crop as greens, he does not have that right because it causes compulsion to the other. If the sharecropper wants to take it as greens, it is said to the landowner: Uproot the crop if you wish, so it will be between you, or give him the value of his share, or you spend on the crop and then claim back from him what you spent, to remove harm from him. He said: The sharecropper is not liable for the equivalent rent of the land, because since he consented to waive his right, the lease does not remain between them. If the sharecropper goes absent after planting, and the landowner spends until ripening by the judge's order, he recovers and the sharecropper has no access to the crop until he pays all the expenses, because if the sharecropper were present, everything would be on him, so also if he is absent. If they dispute about the expenses, the statement of the sharecropper is taken with his oath because he is denying. When the period expires before ripening, whoever spends without the judge's permission is a volunteer; if he spends by the judge's order, he recovers half of what he spent.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq dealing with the situation when the sharecropping (muzara'ah) term ends but the crop is not yet ripe. The ruling is that the worker (muzari') must pay an equivalent rent (ujrat al-mithl) for the land until harvest, but this rent is only for the share of the landowner, not for the worker's own share. The author corrects a potential misinterpretation: the obligation is not an absolute rent but proportionate to the landowner's share. The rationale is that continuing the lease by istihsan (juristic preference) is better than uprooting the crop which causes harm. However, if the worker dies before ripening, no rent is owed because the contract is preserved only out of necessity for the crop, not as a lease. Various sub-rulings follow: spending without a judge's order makes one a volunteer; the landowner cannot take the crop as greens unilaterally; the absent worker loses access to the crop until covering expenses.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market rent for the land's use, determined by similar properties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the muzara'ah term expires before the crop ripens, what must the worker do?
A) Uproot the crop immediately
B) Pay equivalent rent for the landowner's share until harvest
C) Give half the crop to the landowner
D) Leave the land without any compensation

Key Takeaway
When the muzara'ah term ends before the crop ripens, the worker must pay ujrat al-mithl for the landowner's proportionate share, not for the whole land, by istihsan to avoid waste.

Expenses of Crop and Invalid Conditions in Muzara'ah
Explains shared expenses and that stipulating them on worker invalidates contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stipulating post-harvest expenses on the worker in a muzara'ah contract and distinguish the apparent narration from Abu Yusuf's view.

Core Idea
Stipulating post-harvest work on the worker invalidates the contract per the apparent narration, but custom can validate it per Abu Yusuf.

In a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract, the expenses of harvesting and related work are normally shared according to ownership. But what happens if the parties stipulate that all such post-harvest work falls solely on the worker? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute: while the dominant transmission (zahir al-riwayah) declares the contract invalid due to an extraneous condition, a narration from Abu Yusuf upholds it on grounds of custom (ta'amul). Understanding this tension is key to knowing which ruling to apply in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule for crop expenses
The passage begins by establishing that post-harvest work like harvesting, threshing, and winnowing is shared by landowner and worker according to their ownership shares.
This default applies both during and after the muzara'ah period.
2
Recognize the invalidating condition
The author then states that if the parties stipulate these expenses solely on the worker, the contract becomes fasid (invalid). The reason given is that such a condition is not required by the contract's nature.
The condition is considered extraneous, like stipulating carrying and grinding.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
The passage introduces a counter-narration from Abu Yusuf, who holds the contract valid even with such conditions, relying on widespread custom (ta'amul). The scholars of Balkh and Shams al-A'imma preferred this view.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, not a madhhab difference.
4
Assess the tarjih (preference) and mufta bihi
The passage indicates that Shams al-A'imma chose Abu Yusuf's narration as 'the most correct in our lands', and fatwa in certain regions follows this due to custom.
Thus the operative ruling (mufta bihi) may vary by locality based on prevailing practice.
5
Apply the principle to additional tasks
The passage expands on other tasks (picking fruit, separating dates, etc.) that are always shared unless custom dictates otherwise. It also cites that any work increasing the crop is obligatory on the sharecropper whether stipulated or not.
This shows the scope of default obligations in muzara'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ونفقة الزرع عليهما بقدر حقوقهما كاجرة الحصاد والرفاع والدياس والتذرية) تجب عليهما نفقة الزرع على قدر ملكهما بعد انقضاء مدة المزارعة . كما يجب عليهما أجرة الحصاد والرفاع والدياسة والتذرية مطلقاً من غير قيد بانقضاء مدة المزارعة، أما نفقة الزرع بعد انقضاء المدة فلما بينا، وأما وجوب الحصاد دوما ذكر فلأن عقد المزارعة يوجب على العامل عملاً يحتاج إليه إلى انتهاء الزرع ليزداد الزرع بذلك فيبقى ذلك باشتراك بينهما يجب عليهما قال رحمه الله : (فإن شرطاه على العامل فسدت) يعني شرطا العمل الذي يكون بعد انتهاء الزرع كالحاصد وما ذكرناه على العامل أو النفقة فسدت لأنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد. وإنما قلنا ذلك لأن العقد يقتضي عمل المزارع وهذه الأشياء ليست أفعال المزارعة فكانت أجنبية فيكون شرطها مفسداً كشرط الحمل والطحن على العامل. من قال في الذخيرة وهو ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي يوسف أنها تصح مع اشتراط ذلك على العامل ومشايخ بلخ كانوا يفتون بهذه الرواية ويزيدون على هذا ويقولون: ويجوز شرط التنقية والحمل إلى منزله على العامل لأن المزارعة على هذه الشروط متعاملة بین الناس ويجوز ترك القياس بالتعامل واختار شمس الأئمة رواية أبي يوسف وقال : وهو الأصح في ديارنا . ولو شرط الجذاذ على العامل والحصاد على غير العامل لا يجوز الإجماع لعدم التعامل، ولو أراد فصل الفصيل أوجد التمر بسراً أو التقاطه الرطب كان ذلك كله عليهما. وفي الأصل: وإذا أدرك الباذنجان أو البطيخ فالتقاط ذلك عليهما والحمل والبيع عليهما وكذا الحصاد عليهما اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : وكل عمل يزيد في الزرع ولا بد للمزارع منه يجب على المزارع شرط عليه ذلك أو لم يشرط عليه ذلك كالسفر وغيره اهـ. والله أعلم.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And the expenses of the crop are upon both according to their shares, like the hire of harvesting, winnowing, threshing, and winnowing.' They are obligatory upon both proportionate to their ownership after the expiry of the muzara'ah period. As the hire of harvesting, winnowing, threshing, and winnowing is obligatory upon both absolutely, without any condition of expiry of the muzara'ah period. As for the expenses of the crop after expiry of the period, it is as we stated. As for the obligation of harvesting always, it is because the contract of muzara'ah imposes upon the worker work that is needed until the completion of the crop, so that the crop increases thereby. So that remains shared between them, obligatory upon both. He said: 'If they stipulate both upon the worker, the contract is invalid.' Meaning they stipulate the work that occurs after the completion of the crop, like the harvester and what we mentioned, upon the worker, or the expenses, then it is invalid because it is a condition that the contract does not require. We only say that because the contract requires the work of the sharecropper, and these things are not part of the sharecropper's work, so they are extraneous. Thus stipulating them is invalidating, like stipulating carrying and grinding upon the worker. From who said in al-Dhakhirah, and it is the apparent narration. And from Abu Yusuf that it is valid with stipulating that upon the worker, and the scholars of Balkh used to give fatwa according to this narration and added to it, saying: It is permissible to stipulate cleaning and carrying to his home upon the worker, because muzara'ah with these conditions is practiced among people, and it is permissible to leave analogy due to custom. And Shams al-A'imma chose the narration of Abu Yusuf and said: It is the most correct in our lands. If he stipulates picking dates on the worker and harvesting on someone else, it is not permissible by consensus due to lack of custom. If he wants to separate the young branch, or turn dates into ripe dates, or pick wet dates, all that is upon both. In al-Asl: When eggplants or watermelons ripen, picking them is upon both, and carrying and selling are upon both, and likewise harvesting is upon both. End quote. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Every work that increases the crop and is necessary for the sharecropper is obligatory upon the sharecropper, whether he stipulated it or not, like traveling, etc. End quote. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on muzara'ah. It addresses two main issues: (1) Expenses of the crop (like harvesting, threshing, winnowing) are shared by the landowner and worker according to their ownership shares, both before and after the contract period. The reasoning is that such work is necessary for the crop to reach completion, and the benefit is shared. (2) If they stipulate that these post-harvest activities or expenses are solely on the worker, the contract becomes invalid (fasid) according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). This is because the contract only requires the worker's labor of planting and tending, not extraneous work. Stipulating such extra conditions is like stipulating carrying and grinding, which is not part of the muzara'ah. However, there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that such conditions are valid, and the scholars of Balkh and Shams al-A'imma preferred this view, considering the widespread custom (ta'amul) of people. They also allow stipulating cleaning and transport. But stipulating picking dates on the worker while harvesting on someone else is invalid by consensus due to lack of custom. The passage then lists various tasks that are always shared, like picking eggplant, watermelon, etc. Finally, it cites al-Tatarkhaniyyah that any work that increases the crop and is necessary for the sharecropper is obligatory on him whether stipulated or not.

Key Terms
التعامل (al-ta'amul): Common practice among people; customary usage in commercial transactions.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The dominant transmission from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the parties stipulate that harvesting costs are solely on the worker?
A) The contract remains valid unconditionally
B) The contract is invalid per zahir al-riwayah
C) The contract is valid only if the landowner pays
D) The worker must refund the landowner

Key Takeaway
The validity of a muzara'ah contract containing conditions depends on whether the condition is extraneous to the contract's purpose; custom can override analogy.

Definition and Legal Description of Musaqat
Defines musaqat and explains each term of the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of musaqat and explain each element of the contract to distinguish it from sale, lease, and muzara'ah.

Core Idea
Musaqat is a contract for tree care with shared fruit, distinct from sale, lease, and muzara'ah.

Musaqat is a permissible contract for the care of fruit trees, where the owner hands over the trees to a worker who tends them in exchange for a share of the fruit. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a precise definition and parses its terms to show what musaqat includes and excludes. Understanding this definition is key to correctly applying the rulings of musaqat and distinguishing it from similar contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus and differentiae
The definition is structured as a genus (mu'āqadah) followed by three differentiae. Identify each component.
The genus is 'contract', and the three differentiae are: hand over trees, to someone who works in them, and on condition that the fruit is shared.
2
Analyze the exclusion of sale
Explain why 'handing over trees' excludes sale (bay'). In sale, ownership is transferred (tamlik), not just handed over for work.
3
Analyze the exclusion of lease
Explain why 'to someone who works in them' excludes lease (ijarah). Ijarah is for benefit, not necessarily for labor that increases the fruit.
4
Analyze the exclusion of muzara'ah
Explain why 'on condition that the fruit is between them' excludes muzara'ah. Muzara'ah involves land, not trees.
5
General rule: includes partners and strangers
Note that the phrasing 'whoever works' is general, covering partners and strangers. Review the fatwa on co-owners to see an invalid application.
The fatwa shows that when co-owners enter a similar arrangement without proper sharing, it is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المساقاة هي معاقدة دفع الأشجار إلى من يعمل فيها على أن الثمرة بينهما. قال: كتاب المساقاة من المساقاة معاقدة في غاية البيان: كان من حق الوضع أن يقدم كتاب المساقاة على كتاب المزارعة لأن المساقاة جائزة بلا خلاف ولهذا قدم الطحاوي في مختصره كتاب المساقاة على كتاب المزارعة إلا أن المزارعة لما كانت كثيرة الوقوع في عامة البلاد كانت الحاجة إليها أكثر فقدمت على المساقاة.اهـ. ولك أن تقول: وجه المناسبة أن في كل منهما دفعاً إلا أن في المزارعة دفع الأرض وهي الأصل وفي المساقاة المقصود دفع الأشجار وهي فرع فقدم الأصل وهو دفع الأرض. وهي في اللغة مفاعلة من السقي وسبب جوازها حاجة الناس إليها. وركنها الإيجاب والقبول والارتباط ودليلها ما تقدم في المزارعة، وشرطها كون العاقد والساقي من أهل العقد وشرط صحتها كون الثمرة تزيد بالعمل، وصفتها أنها جائزة، وحكمها وجوب الشركة في الخارج وعند الفقهاء ما سنذكره. قال رحمه الله: (هي دفع الأشجار إلى من يعمل فيها على أن الثمرة بينهما فقوله «معاقدة» جنس وقوله «دفع الأشجار» أخرج البيع لأنه عقد تمليك العين لا دفعها، وقوله إلى من يعمل فيها» أخرج الإجارة لأنها وإن كانت فيها دفع للانتفاع لا ليعمل فيها. وقوله على أن الثمرة بينهما» أخرج المزارعة. وأطلق من يعمل فشمل الشريك وغيره ولو زاد الأجنبي ليعمل فيها الخ لكان أولى لأنه لو دفع أحدهما للآخر وهما مالكان لا قال يصح . في فتاوى الفضلي: إذا كان النخل بين اثنين فدفع أحدهما لصاحبه معاملة على أن يقوم عليه ويسقيه ومهما خرج فهو بينهما أثلاثاً ثلثه للدافع وثلثاه للعامل فهذه المعاملة فاسدة، ولو كان مكانها مزارعة بأن كانت أرض بين اثنين ودفعها أحدهما لصاحبه مزارعة على أن الخارج ثلثه للدافع وثلثاه للعامل جاز على أصح الروايتين اهـ.
The book of Musaqat: It is a contract of handing over trees to someone who works on them on the condition that the fruit is shared between them. He said: The book of Musaqat from musaqat is a contract in utmost clarity: It was proper to place the book of Musaqat before the book of Muzara'ah because Musaqat is permissible without dispute, and hence al-Tahawi in his Mukhtasar placed the book of Musaqat before the book of Muzara'ah, except that since Muzara'ah occurs frequently in most lands, the need for it is greater, so it was placed before Musaqat. And you may say: The aspect of appropriateness is that in each there is a handing over, but in Muzara'ah it is handing over land, which is the principal, and in Musaqat the objective is handing over trees, which are subsidiary, so the principal (handing over land) was placed first. Linguistically, it is a mutual form from 'irrigation', and the reason for its permissibility is people's need for it. Its pillar is offer and acceptance and linkage, and its evidence is what preceded in Muzara'ah. Its condition is that the contracting party and the irrigator be from the people of contract, and the condition of its validity is that the fruit increases by labor. Its description is that it is permissible, and its ruling is the obligation of partnership in the produce, and according to the jurists, what we will mention. He (the author) said: (It is the handing over of trees to someone who works on them on condition that the fruit is between them). So his statement 'contract' is a genus, and his statement 'handing over trees' excludes sale because it is a contract of transferring ownership of the object, not its handing over. His statement 'to someone who works in them' excludes lease because although it involves handing over for benefit, not for working in them. His statement 'on condition that the fruit is between them' excludes Muzara'ah. And he said 'whoever works' generally, so it includes the partner and others. And if he had added 'the stranger to work in them to the end', it would have been better, because if one of them handed over to the other while both are owners, it is not said to be valid. In Fatawa al-Fadli: If date-palms are between two, and one hands over to his partner a mu'amalah on the basis that he takes care of them and irrigates them, and whatever comes out is between them in thirds: one third for the giver and two thirds for the worker, then this mu'amalah is invalid. And if instead it were a muzara'ah such that land is between two, and one hands it over to his partner as muzara'ah on the basis that the produce is one third for the giver and two thirds for the worker, it is valid according to the more correct of the two narrations.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the contract of Musaqat (sharecropping of trees). The author begins by establishing that Musaqat is a contract of handing over trees to a worker with the fruit shared between the owner and the worker. The commentary then discusses the placement of this chapter in the book, noting that although Musaqat is unanimously permissible, Muzara'ah is placed first due to its greater frequency and need. Linguistically, 'Musaqat' is derived from 'saqa' (to irrigate). The reason for its permissibility is the general need for such contracts. The pillar (rukn) is offer and acceptance coupled with the linkage to the subject matter. The evidence for its validity is the same as for Muzara'ah, which is based on the Sunnah and consensus. The conditions include that both parties be legally capable (balanced and sane), and that the fruit actually increases through the worker's labor. The contract is classified as permissible (ja'iz), not obligatory. The commentary then parses the definition phrase by phrase: 'contract' is a general category; 'handing over trees' excludes sale (which transfers ownership, not just possession for work); 'to someone who works in them' excludes lease (which is for benefit, not necessarily labor); 'on condition that the fruit is between them' excludes Muzara'ah (which involves land). The generality 'whoever works' includes both partners and strangers. A fatwa from Fatawa al-Fadli illustrates a case: if two co-owners of date-palms, one hands over his share to the other to tend and irrigate, with the fruit divided in thirds (one for the giver, two for the worker), this contract is invalid because it resembles a forbidden mu'amalah. However, if it were a Muzara'ah on land with the same share division, it would be valid according to the more reliable narration, because Muzara'ah is permissible according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Key Terms
المساقاة (al-musāqāh): A contract to hand over trees to a worker for tending, with the fruit shared between owner and worker.
معاقدة (mu‘āqadah): A mutual contract or agreement involving an exchange.
دفع (daf‘): The act of handing over possession of the trees to the worker, not transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the definition of musaqat, what does the phrase 'دفع الأشجار' (handing over trees) exclude?
A) Lease (ijarah)
B) Sale (bay')
C) Gift (hibah)
D) Muzara'ah

Key Takeaway
Musaqat is a contract for tree care with shared fruit, distinct from sale (ownership transfer), lease (fixed benefit), and muzara'ah (land).

Musaqat and Muzara'ah: The Four Differences
Explains the similarity and four differences between musaqat and muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four differences between musaqat and muzara'ah according to the Hanafi school and explain why the period may be unspecified in musaqat by istihsan.

Core Idea
Musaqat is like muzara'ah in conditions but differs in compulsion, rent, third-party claims, and duration flexibility.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq compares two important agricultural contracts: musaqat (watering/tending trees for a share of fruit) and muzara'ah (sharecropping on land). The author notes that musaqat is 'like muzara'ah' but then specifies four key differences. Understanding these differences is essential for correctly applying Hanafi contract law to orchards and vineyards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
Read the phrase 'وهي كالمزارعة' and the commentary. Determine the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions regarding the permissibility of musaqat.
Imam does not permit it; Sahibayn permit it. The mufta bihi is the position of Sahibayn.
2
List the four differences
The text enumerates four exceptions where musaqat differs from muzara'ah. Extract them: (1) compulsion if one refuses, (2) no rent after period ends, (3) worker's compensation if trees are claimed, (4) duration specification via istihsan.
Memorize these four to apply in practice.
3
Examine the fourth difference in detail
The passage elaborates on duration: if no period is set, musaqat is valid by istihsan because fruit ripening time is known. Compare with cases involving saplings, reeds, and absolute terms to understand the boundaries.
Focus on the distinction between date-palms (known ripening) and reeds (uncertain).
4
Apply the rules to hypotheticals
Consider scenarios: saplings not yet fruiting, reeds with absolute terms, palms with specified period but no fruit. Determine validity based on the criteria given.
This develops practical fatwa skills.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وهي كالمزارعة) يعني لا يجوز عند الإمام ويجوز عندهما، وشرطها عندهما شروط المزارعة في جميع ما ذكرنا إلا في أربعة أشياء: أحدها إذا امتنع أحدهما يجبر لأنه لا ضرر عليه في المضي بخلاف المزارعة على ما تقدم. الثاني إذا انقضت المدة تترك بلا أجرة على ما تبين بخلاف المزارعة الثالث إذا استحق النخل يرجع العامل بأجرة مثله والزارع بقيمة الزرع والرابع في بيان المدة فإذا لم يبين المدة فيها يجوز استحساناً لأن التيقن وقت إدراك الثمرة معلوم وقل ما يتفاوت فيه فيدخل ما هو المتيقن به، وإدراك البذر في أصول الرطبة في هذا بمنزلة إدراك الثمار لأن لها نهاية معلومة فلا يشترط فيها بيان المدة بخلاف الزرع لأن ابتداء يختلف والانتهاء ينبني عليه فتدخله الجهالة الفاحشة، وبخلاف ما إذا دفع إليه غرساً قد نبت ولم يثمر بعد معاملة حيث لا يجوز إلا ببيان المدة لأنه يتفاوت بقوة الأرض وضعفها تفاوتاً فاحشاً فلا يمكن صرفه إلى أول ثمر يخرج منه، وبخلاف ما إذا دفع نخلاً أو أصول رطبة على أن يقيم عليها حتى يذهب أصولها وثبتها لأنه لا يعلم متى ينقطع النخل أو الرطب لأن الرطب ثمر ما دامت أصولها فتكون مجهولة فتفسد المساقاة . وكذا إذا أطلق في الرطبة ولم يرد في قوله حتى يذهب بخلاف ما إذا أطلق في النخل حيث يجوز وينصرف إلى أول ثمرة تخرج منه. والفرق أن ثمر النخل لإدراكه وقت معلوم فينصرف إليه ولا يعرف في الرطبة أول جزء منه حتى لو عرف جاز لعدم الجهالة. ولو أطلق في النخل ولم يثمر في تلك السنة انقطعت المعاملة فيها لانتهاء مدتها، فإن سمى فيها مدة يعلم أن الثمرة لا تخرج في المدة فسدت المساقاة لفوات المقصود وهو الشركة في الثمار، وإن ذكرا مدة يحتمل الطلوع فيها جازت لعدم التيقن بفوات المقصود . ثم إن خرج في الوقت المسمى فهو على الشركة لصحة العقد، وإن تأخر فللعامل أجر مثله لفساد العقد لأنه تبين الخطأ المدة فصار كما لو علم ذلك ابتداء بخلاف ما إذا لم يخرج أصلاً لأن الذهاب بآفة سماوية فلا يتبين أن العقد كان فاسداً فبقي العقد صحيحاً، ولا شيء لكل واحد منهما على صاحبه.
He (the author) said: (It is like muzara'ah) meaning it is not permissible according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and is permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And its conditions according to the two are the conditions of muzara'ah in all that we mentioned, except in four things: First, if one of them refuses, he is compelled because there is no harm to him in proceeding, unlike muzara'ah as previously mentioned. Second, if the period expires, it is left without rent as is evident, unlike muzara'ah. Third, if the date-palms are claimed (by a third party), the worker gets the equivalent rent, and the cultivator gets the value of the crop. Fourth, regarding the specification of the period: if the period is not specified, it is permissible by istihsan because the time of ripening of the fruit is known and it hardly varies, so what is certain is included. And the growth of seeds in the roots of reeds is like ripening of fruits because it has a known end, so specifying the period is not required, unlike crops (agriculture) because its beginning varies and the end depends on it, so gross uncertainty enters. And unlike the case where he hands over to him a sapling that has grown but not yet fruited as a mu'amalah, where it is not permissible except with a specified period because it varies greatly with the strength and weakness of the land, so it cannot be referred to the first fruit that emerges from it. And unlike the case where he hands over date-palms or roots of reeds on the condition that he stays on them until their roots and stems disappear, because it is not known when the date-palms or reeds will end, since reeds bear fruit as long as their roots exist, so it is unknown, and thus the musaqat is invalid. Likewise, if it is absolute regarding reeds and he does not mean by his statement 'until it disappears', unlike the case if it is absolute regarding date-palms, where it is permissible and is referred to the first fruit that emerges from them. The difference is that the fruit of date-palms has a known time for ripening, so it is referred to that, but the first part of reeds is not known, so if it is known, it is permissible due to the absence of uncertainty. And if it is absolute regarding date-palms and it did not bear fruit in that year, the mu'amalah is terminated because its period has ended. If they specify a period in which it is known that the fruit will not emerge, the musaqat is invalid due to the loss of the objective, which is partnership in the fruits. If they mention a period in which emergence is probable, it is permissible because the loss of the objective is not certain. Then if fruit emerges in the specified time, it is on partnership due to the validity of the contract. If it is delayed, the worker gets an equivalent rent due to the invalidity of the contract, because it becomes clear that the period was wrong, so it is as if they knew that initially, unlike the case where it does not emerge at all because the loss is due to a heavenly affliction, so it does not become clear that the contract was invalid, so the contract remains valid, and neither owes anything to the other.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a comparison between musaqat and muzara'ah, focusing on an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that musaqat is 'like muzara'ah', which the commentary explains means that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, musaqat is not permissible (like his view on muzara'ah) while according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible. However, the conditions for musaqat according to the two companions are the same as for muzara'ah with four exceptions. First, if one party refuses to proceed, he is compelled in musaqat because there is no harm; in muzara'ah, compulsion is not applied. Second, at the end of the period, the land in musaqat is left without any rental claim, whereas in muzara'ah, a rental may be due. Third, if a third party proves ownership of the trees, the worker gets the market rate for his labor, while in muzara'ah, the cultivator gets the value of the crop. Fourth, regarding specification of duration: in musaqat, if no period is specified, the contract is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because the time of ripening is generally known and not highly variable. The commentary then elaborates on the fourth difference with various cases. For example, if saplings that have not yet fruited are handed over, a period must be specified because the fruiting time varies. If date-palms or reeds are handed over with the condition that the worker stays until the roots disappear, it is invalid due to uncertainty. If the period is unspecified for date-palms, it is understood as the first fruit, but for reeds it is not valid unless the first part is known. If a period is specified during which fruit is expected but does not appear, different rulings apply depending on whether the delay is due to natural causes or not.

Key Terms
المزارعة (al-muzāra‘ah): A contract of sharecropping on land, where one party provides land and the other works, and the crop is shared.
المساقاة (al-musāqāt): A contract to tend fruit-bearing trees for a share of the fruit.
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference used to allow musaqat without a fixed period due to the known ripening time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fourth difference between musaqat and muzara'ah?
A) The worker is compelled to proceed if one party refuses
B) If the trees are claimed by a third party, the worker gets equivalent rent
C) The period may be unspecified in musaqat by istihsan
D) At the end of the period, the land is left without rent

Key Takeaway
Musaqat shares conditions with muzara'ah but has four distinct rules regarding compulsion, rent, third-party claims, and duration specification.

Musaqat on Plants: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Eligible Crops
Ruling on plant eligibility for musaqat with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which plants musaqat is valid for, explain the evidence from the Khaybar hadith, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i new opinion.

Core Idea
In musaqat, any fruit-bearing plant that requires labor and yields a known crop qualifies; it is not limited to dates and grapes.

The Hanafi school extends musaqat to vines, trees, reeds, and eggplant roots, while Imam al-Shafi'i in his new opinion restricts it to vines and date-palms. This lesson unpacks the evidence—the hadith of the Prophet's musaqat at Khaybar—and the underlying rationale that drives the Hanafi view. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to reason by analogy (qiyas) and apply the principle of istihsan in contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the matn declares musaqat valid for vines, trees, reeds, and eggplant roots. This is the Hanafi ruling: it covers all such plants.
The Hanafi school generalizes to any plant that produces a crop requiring labor.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Al-Shafi'i in his new opinion restricts musaqat to vines and date-palms only. Note the ikhtilaf.
This is the key point of contention.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i likely relies on a strict reading of the Khaybar hadith or the principle of gharar. The text does not detail his proof, but the context suggests a narrower analogy.
The Hanafi response will address this.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet made musaqat with the people of Khaybar for half the fruit. The hadith mentions fruits generally, not just dates. Hanafis use this plus istihsan to extend to all similar plants.
The wajh al-dalalah: the Prophet's practice indicates permissibility for fruits in general.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow musaqat on mangoes, lemons, and reeds; Shafi'is do not. This affects farmers and landowners in their contractual options.
The difference is significant in agricultural economies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وتصح في الكرم والشجر والرطب وأصول الباذنجان) وقال الشافعي أن رحمه الله تعالى في الجديد لا تجوز إلا في الكرم والنخل ولنا ما روي عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دفع إلى أهل خيبر المساقاة على أن لهم الشطر من الثمر. وفي الخلاصة : وإن ذكرا مدة قد يخرج وقد لا يخرج فهي موقوفة إن أخرجت صحت، وإن لم تخرج فسدت. وهذا إذا خرجت في المدة المضروبة ما يرغب في مثله، فإن أخرجت في شيء لا يرغب في مثله فهي فاسدة اهـ. وفي المحيط : ولو دفع إليه رطبه ثابتة في الأرض وقد انتهى جوازها لكن بذرها لم يخرج ليقوم ليخرج البذر على أن البذر بينهما نصفان ولم يسميا وقتاً جاز لأنه جعل الأجرة بعض ما يخرج من عمله، ولو شرطا أن الرطبة بينهما نصفان لم تجز لأنه استأجره ببعض ما أوجد قبل عمله مقصوداً. وفي جامع الفتاوى : ولو دفع أرضاً معاملة خمسمائة سنة لم يجز، وإن شرط مائة سنة وهو ابن عشرين سنة جاز، وإن كان أكثر من عشرين سنة لم يجز اهـ.
He (the author) said: (And it is valid for the vine, trees, reeds, and roots of eggplant). And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said in the new (opinion) that it is not valid except for vines and date-palms. And we have what was narrated from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, handed over to the people of Khaybar the musaqat on the condition that they have half of the fruit. And in al-Khulasa: If they mention a period in which it may emerge and may not emerge, it is suspended: if it emerges, it becomes valid; if it does not emerge, it becomes invalid. This is if it emerges in the stipulated period something that is desirable in its like; if it emerges something that is not desirable in its like, it is invalid. In al-Muhit: If he hands over to him his reeds fixed in the ground, and their bearing has ended but their seeds have not emerged, to stand and bring out the seeds, on condition that the seeds are half and half between them, and they did not specify a time, it is valid because he made the fee a portion of what emerges from his work. If they stipulate that the reeds are half and half between them, it is not valid because he hired him with a portion of what was created before his work intentionally. And in Jami' al-Fatawa: If he hands over land as a mu'amalah for five hundred years, it is not valid. If they stipulate one hundred years and he is twenty years old, it is valid. If it is more than twenty years, it is not valid.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the types of plants for which musaqat is valid, and it includes an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. The matn states that musaqat is valid for vines (grapevines), trees (fruit trees), reeds (a type of plant used for fodder or building), and the roots of eggplant. Al-Shafi'i, in his new opinion, restricts it to only vines and date-palms. The Hanafi evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made a musaqat contract with the people of Khaybar for half the fruit, which includes various fruits, not just dates and grapes. The passage then shifts to a discussion of duration and conditions from other works. Al-Khulasa states that if the period is such that fruit may or may not emerge, the contract is suspended: if fruit emerges, it becomes valid; if not, it becomes invalid. This is only if the fruit that emerges is of desirable quality; if it is not desirable, the contract is invalid from the start. Al-Muhit discusses a case where reeds are handed over after their bearing has ceased, but seeds have not yet emerged, and the agreement is to share the seeds equally. If no time is specified, it is valid because the worker's fee is a portion of what his labor produces. But if they stipulate that the reeds themselves (the plants) are shared equally, it is not valid because that would be hiring him with something that existed before his work. Jami' al-Fatawa addresses extremely long durations: a contract for 500 years is invalid; for 100 years, if the worker is 20 years old (so it is within his expected lifespan), it is valid; longer than that is invalid due to uncertainty.

Key Terms
الكرم (al-karm): The grapevine; a trellised vine that produces grapes.
الرطب (al-ratab): A type of reed or rush that grows in wet areas, used for fodder; its seeds are also harvested.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the Hanafi position that musaqat is valid on more than just dates and grapes?
A) The practice of the people of Khaybar
B) A hadith from Ibn Umar about the Prophet making musaqat on various fruits
C) The principle of istihsan
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits musaqat on any plant that yields a crop through labor, supported by the Khaybar hadith and istihsan.

Duration and Special Conditions in Musaqat Contracts
Rulings on duration and special conditions in musaqat contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on uncertain duration, crop quality, sharing of seeds, and the maximum contract period based on the worker's lifespan.

Core Idea
A musaqat contract must have a certain term; if the term is uncertain, the contract is suspended; if the crop is worthless, it is invalid; sharing seeds is valid but sharing existing plants is not; and the term cannot exceed the worker's expected lifespan.

Beyond the dispute over eligible plants, the Hanafi school provides detailed rules on the duration and conditions of musaqat contracts. This lesson covers three key scenarios: uncertain periods, sharing of seeds from reeds, and extremely long-term contracts. Understanding these conditions ensures that the contract is free from gharar (uncertainty) and is equitable to both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first case from al-Khulasa
A contract with a period where fruit may or may not emerge. The contract is suspended: if fruit emerges, it becomes valid; if not, invalid. Also, the fruit must be desirable.
This deals with uncertainty in the term and quality.
2
Identify the second case from al-Muhit
Reeds with ended bearing but seeds not yet emerged. Two sub-cases: sharing seeds without specifying time is valid (fee is from the produce of labor); sharing existing reeds is invalid (fee is from pre-existing property).
The principle: the worker's compensation must be from his labor's produce.
3
Identify the third case from Jami' al-Fatawa
Extremely long-term mu'amalah (here musaqat). A term of 500 years is invalid; 100 years is valid if the worker is 20 years old; if the term is more than 20 years (relative to the worker's age?), it is invalid.
The rule: the term must be within the worker's expected lifespan.
4
Extract the underlying principles
The contract must avoid gharar (uncertainty). The term must be reasonable. The worker's share must be from the produce of his labor.
These principles appear in other fiqh chapters as well.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
For example, a contract for 50 years with a 30-year-old worker is valid; one for 100 years with a 30-year-old is invalid because it exceeds expected lifespan.
This shows the condition regarding the worker's age.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وتصح في الكرم والشجر والرطب وأصول الباذنجان) وقال الشافعي أن رحمه الله تعالى في الجديد لا تجوز إلا في الكرم والنخل ولنا ما روي عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دفع إلى أهل خيبر المساقاة على أن لهم الشطر من الثمر. وفي الخلاصة : وإن ذكرا مدة قد يخرج وقد لا يخرج فهي موقوفة إن أخرجت صحت، وإن لم تخرج فسدت. وهذا إذا خرجت في المدة المضروبة ما يرغب في مثله، فإن أخرجت في شيء لا يرغب في مثله فهي فاسدة اهـ. وفي المحيط : ولو دفع إليه رطبه ثابتة في الأرض وقد انتهى جوازها لكن بذرها لم يخرج ليقوم ليخرج البذر على أن البذر بينهما نصفان ولم يسميا وقتاً جاز لأنه جعل الأجرة بعض ما يخرج من عمله، ولو شرطا أن الرطبة بينهما نصفان لم تجز لأنه استأجره ببعض ما أوجد قبل عمله مقصوداً. وفي جامع الفتاوى : ولو دفع أرضاً معاملة خمسمائة سنة لم يجز، وإن شرط مائة سنة وهو ابن عشرين سنة جاز، وإن كان أكثر من عشرين سنة لم يجز اهـ.

And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said in the new (opinion) that it is not valid except for vines and date-palms. This is if it emerges in the stipulated period something that is desirable in its like; if it emerges something that is not desirable in its like, it is invalid. Key Terms
المدة (al-mudda): The period or term of the contract.
موقوفة (mawqufa): Suspended; the contract's validity depends on a future event.
الرطب (al-ratab): A type of reed or rush that grows in wet areas, used for fodder; its seeds are also harvested.

Checkpoint
According to Jami' al-Fatawa, a musaqat contract for 500 years is:
A) Valid if both parties agree.
B) Invalid due to extreme uncertainty.
C) Valid for trees but not for vines.
D) Valid if the worker is under 20 years old.

Key Takeaway
The term of a musaqat contract must be certain and within the worker's expected lifespan; sharing of seeds from existing plants is valid, but sharing the plants themselves is not.

The Scope of Musaqah: A Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute and Duration Conditions
Commentary on validity and duration conditions of musaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on valid trees for musaqah, explain the duration conditions, and evaluate the Shafi'i restriction with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Musaqah is valid on all fruit-bearing trees; a general proof cannot be restricted by opinion.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling that musaqah is valid on vines, trees, rutab (fresh dates), and eggplant roots. It then navigates the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who restricts it to vines and date palms in his new opinion. The commentary also provides detailed guidance on duration conditions – when a term must be specified and when it can be left open, using istihsan. Understanding this ruling is essential for structuring valid agricultural partnerships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on trees
The matn states musaqah is valid on vines, trees (all fruit trees), rutab, and eggplant roots. This is the comprehensive Hanafi view.
Rutab are fresh dates; eggplant roots are treated like fruit trees due to a known end of fruiting.
2
Analyse the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i (new opinion) restricts musaqah to vines and date palms only.
The commentator refutes this using the general hadith of Khaybar.
3
Examine the proof: Khaybar hadith
The Prophet made a contract with the people of Khaybar 'on what comes out of fruit' – the word 'fruit' is general (amm) and cannot be restricted without evidence.
Hanafi usul: an absolute text cannot be limited by opinion; restriction requires a specific dalil.
4
Work through duration conditions
The text explains when duration must be specified: for new saplings, indeterminate life (rutab roots), or extremely long terms. For trees with known ripening times (like dates), istihsan allows leaving duration unspecified.
The key distinction is between crops (cereals) where timing varies greatly, and trees with a fixed fruiting season.
5
Apply the practical implications
Under Hanafi, musaqah can be on any fruit tree; under Shafi'i (new), only vines and palms. This affects what contracts are valid in different regions.
The burden of proof lies on the one restricting the general rule.
