كتاب المساقاة
وتصح في الكرم والشجر والرطب وأصول الباذنجان فإن دفع نخلا فيه ثمرة مساقاة
أحدهما يجبر لأنه لا ضرر عليه في المضي بخلاف المزارعة على ما تقدم. الثاني إذا انقضت المدة تترك بلا أجرة على ما تبين بخلاف المزارعة الثالث إذا استحق النخل يرجع العامل بأجرة مثله والزارع بقيمة الزرع والرابع في بيان المدة فإذا لم يبين المدة فيها يجوز استحساناً لأن التيقن وقت إدراك الثمرة معلوم وقل ما يتفاوت فيه فيدخل ما هو المتيقن به، وإدراك البذر في أصول الرطبة في هذا بمنزلة إدراك الثمار لأن لها نهاية معلومة فلا يشترط فيها بيان المدة بخلاف الزرع لأن ابتداء يختلف والانتهاء ينبني عليه فتدخله الجهالة الفاحشة، وبخلاف ما إذا دفع إليه غرساً قد نبت ولم يثمر بعد معاملة حيث لا يجوز إلا ببيان المدة لأنه يتفاوت بقوة الأرض وضعفها تفاوتاً فاحشاً فلا يمكن صرفه إلى أول ثمر يخرج منه، وبخلاف ما إذا دفع نخلاً أو أصول رطبة على أن يقيم عليها حتى يذهب أصولها وثبتها لأنه لا يعلم متى ينقطع النخل أو الرطب لأن الرطب ثمر ما دامت أصولها فتكون مجهولة فتفسد المساقاة . وكذا إذا أطلق في الرطبة ولم يرد في قوله حتى يذهب بخلاف ما إذا أطلق في النخل حيث يجوز وينصرف إلى أول ثمرة تخرج منه. والفرق أن ثمر النخل لإدراكه وقت معلوم فينصرف إليه ولا يعرف في الرطبة أول جزء منه حتى لو عرف جاز لعدم الجهالة. ولو أطلق في النخل ولم يثمر في تلك السنة انقطعت المعاملة فيها لانتهاء مدتها، فإن سمى فيها مدة يعلم أن الثمرة لا تخرج في المدة فسدت المساقاة لفوات المقصود وهو الشركة في الثمار، وإن ذكرا مدة يحتمل الطلوع فيها جازت لعدم التيقن بفوات المقصود . ثم إن خرج في الوقت المسمى فهو على الشركة لصحة العقد، وإن تأخر فللعامل أجر مثله لفساد العقد لأنه تبين الخطأ المدة فصار كما لو علم ذلك ابتداء بخلاف ما إذا لم يخرج أصلاً لأن الذهاب بآفة سماوية فلا يتبين أن العقد كان فاسداً فبقي العقد صحيحاً، ولا شيء لكل واحد منهما على صاحبه. المدة وفي الخلاصة : وإن ذكرا مدة قد يخرج وقد لا يخرج فهي موقوفة إن أخرجت في صحت، وإن لم تخرج فسدت. وهذا إذا خرجت في المدة المضروبة ما يرغب في مثله، فإن أخرجت في شيء لا يرغب في مثله فهي فاسدة اهـ. وفي المحيط : ولو دفع إليه رطبه ثابتة في الأرض وقد انتهى جوازها لكن بذرها لم يخرج ليقوم ليخرج البذر على أن البذر بينهما نصفان ولم يسميا وقتاً جاز لأنه جعل الأجرة بعض ما يخرج من عمله، ولو شرطا أن الرطبة بينهما نصفان لم تجز لأنه استأجره ببعض ما أوجد قبل عمله مقصوداً. وفي جامع الفتاوى : ولو دفع أرضاً معاملة خمسمائة سنة لم يجز، وإن شرط مائة سنة وهو ابن عشرين سنة جاز، وإن كان أكثر من عشرين سنة لم يجز اهـ.
في
قال رحمه الله : ( وتصح في الكرم والشجر والرطب وأصول الباذنجان) وقال الشافعي أن رحمه الله تعالى في الجديد لا تجوز إلا في الكرم والنخل ولنا ما روي عن ابن عمر
كتاب المساقاة
والثمر يزيد بالعمل صحت وإن انتهت لا كالمزارعة فإذا فسدت فللعامل أجر مثله
النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عامل أهل خيبر على ما يخرج من ثمر. وهذا مطلق فلا يجوز قصره على بعض الأشجار دون بعض لأنه تقييد فلا يجوز بالرأي. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : دفع كرماً معاملة وفيه أشجار لا تحتاج إلى عمل سوى الحفظ، فإن كان بحال لو لم تحفظ يذهب ثمرها قبل الإدراك لا تجوز المعاملة في تلك الأشجار ولا نصيب للعامل فيها. وفي التجريد: رجل دفع نخلاً إلى رجلين معاملة على أن لأحدهم السدس وللآخر النصف ولرب الأرض الثلث فهي جائزة، ولو شرطوا الصاحب النخل الثلث وللآخر الثلثان وللثالث أجر مائة على العامل فهذا فاسد، والخارج كله لرب النخل ويرجع العامل الذي شرط له الثلثان على رب النخل ولرب النخل الثلثان وللثالث الثلث فهي جائزة. وفي جامع الفتاوى لو دفع إلى رجلين جاز عند أبي يوسف ولا يجوز عند الإمام. وفي شرح الطحاوي ولو أن رجلاً دفع أرضه معاملة على أن يغرس العامل فيها أغراساً والغراس يكون بينهما فهذا يجوز ، فإذا انقضت المدة فلرب الأرض أن يطالبه بقلع الأشجار وليس له أن يتملكها بغير رضا المستأجر إذا لم يضر القلع بالأرض، فإن كان يضرها ضرراً فاحشاً فله أن يتملكها بغير رضاه. وفي الفتاوى العتابية : إذا دفع أرضه للغرس على أن الغراس بينهما، فإن كان الغراس من جانب صاحب الأرض فغرس فالغراس كله لصاحب الأرض، وإن كان للعامل وقال له اغرسها فالغراس لصاحب الأرض وللعامل عليه قيمتها اهـ. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : لو غرس حافتي نهر فقال رجل غرست لي لأنك كنت خادمي وفي عيالي وقال الغارس لنفسي، فإن عرف أن الغارس كان وقت الغراس في عياله يعمل له مثل هذا العمل فالشجر ،له وإن لم يعرف ذلك فللغارس ذلك اهـ.
Chapter of Musaqah. And it is valid on vines, trees, rutab, and eggplant roots. If he gives a date palm with fruit as musaqah... one of them is forced because there is no harm in proceeding, unlike muzara'ah as previously mentioned. Second: when the term ends, it is left without rent as clarified, unlike muzara'ah. Third: if the palm is claimed (by another), the worker gets his equivalent wage and the farmer (in muzara'ah) gets the value of the crop. Fourth: concerning the statement of the term: if the term is not specified, it is permissible by istihsan because the known time of fruit ripening is known and rarely varies, so it is included as the certain time. The ripening of seeds in the roots of rutab is like the ripening of fruits because they have a known end, so specifying the term is not required, unlike crops because the beginning varies and the end depends on it, so gross uncertainty enters. And unlike if he gives him a sapling that has grown but not yet fruited as a transaction, it is not permissible without specifying the term because it varies greatly by the strength and weakness of the soil, so it cannot be directed to the first fruit from it. And unlike if he gives palm or rutab roots on condition that he tends them until their roots and shoots die, because it is not known when the palm or rutab will cease, because rutab is fruit as long as its roots exist, so it is uncertain and the musaqah becomes invalid. Similarly if he is absolute in rutab and does not intend in his statement 'until it dies', unlike if he is absolute in palm, where it is permissible and is directed to the first fruit that comes from it. The difference is that palm fruit has a known time of ripening so it is directed to it, but in rutab the first part is not known; if it were known it would be permissible due to the absence of uncertainty. If he is absolute in palm and it does not fruit that year, the transaction ends because its term expires. If they specify a term known that the fruit will not come out in that term, the musaqah is invalid due to the loss of the objective, which is partnership in fruits. If they mention a term in which fruiting is possible, it is permissible due to the lack of certainty that the objective is lost. Then if the fruit appears in the specified time, it is on partnership due to the validity of the contract. If it is delayed, the worker has his equivalent wage due to the invalidity of the contract because the error in the term becomes clear, so it is as if they knew that initially, unlike if no fruit appears at all because the loss is by a heavenly affliction, so it does not become clear that the contract was invalid, so the contract remains valid, and nothing is owed by either to the other. (Regarding the term) In al-Khulasa: If they mention a term in which fruit may or may not appear, it is suspended: if fruit appears, it is valid; if not, it is invalid. This is if what appears in the stipulated term is something desirable; if an undesirable amount appears, the contract is invalid. End quote. In al-Muhit: If he gives him rutab fixed in the ground whose fruiting has ended but its seeds have not come out to grow, on condition that the seeds are half and half between them and they do not specify a time, it is permissible because he made the wage part of what comes out of his work. If they stipulate that the rutab be half and half between them, it is not permissible because he hires him with part of what existed before his work intentionally. In Jami' al-Fatawa: If he gives land as a transaction for five hundred years, it is invalid. If he stipulates one hundred years and he is twenty years old, it is permissible. If it is more than twenty years, it is invalid. End quote. In (the commentary): He (the author) said: (And it is valid on vines, trees, rutab, and eggplant roots) and al-Shafi'i - may Allah have mercy on him - said in his new opinion: it is only valid on vines and date palms. And we have the narration from Ibn Umar... (Page 300) Chapter of Musaqah: And the fruit increases with work, so it is valid, and if it ends (ripens) it is not like muzara'ah. If it becomes invalid, the worker has his equivalent wage. The Prophet (peace be upon him) contracted with the people of Khaybar on what comes out of fruit. This is unconditional, so it is not permissible to restrict it to some trees and not others because that would be a restriction not allowed by opinion. In Fatawa of Abu al-Layth: He gave a vineyard as a transaction and in it were trees that need no work except preservation; if they were such that if not preserved their fruit would be lost before ripening, the transaction is not valid regarding those trees and the worker has no share in them. In al-Tajrid: A man gave date palms to two men as a transaction on condition that one gets one-sixth, the other half, and the landowner one-third: it is valid. If they stipulate that the owner of the palms gets one-third, the other two-thirds, and a third party gets a wage of one hundred from the worker, that is invalid; all produce goes to the palm owner, and the worker who was stipulated two-thirds claims from the palm owner, and the palm owner has two-thirds and the third party has one-third, so it is valid. In Jami' al-Fatawa: If he gives to two men, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf and not valid according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). In Sharh al-Tahawi: If a man gives his land as a transaction on condition that the worker plant trees and the trees are between them, that is valid. When the term ends, the landowner may demand the removal of the trees and may not own them without the tenant's consent if removal does not damage the land; if it causes gross damage, he may own them without his consent. In al-Atabiyyah: If he gives his land for planting on condition that the trees are between them, then if the planting was from the landowner's side, the trees belong entirely to the landowner; if from the worker and he said 'plant it', the trees belong to the landowner and the worker has their value against him. End quote. In Fatawa of Abu al-Layth: If someone planted the banks of a river and one man said 'You planted for me because you were my servant and in my household' and the planter said 'for myself'; if it is known that at the time of planting the planter was in his household working for him in such work, the trees are for the owner; if not known, they are for the planter. End quote.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn statement that musaqah is valid on vines, trees, rutab (fresh dates), and eggplant roots. The commentator first explains branches: if a palm with fruit is given, the worker is forced to continue because no harm; after term, not rent; if palm claimed, worker gets equivalent wage. Then the key issue: when duration is not specified, istihsan allows it because the time of ripening is known for these trees, unlike crops. He differentiates between trees with known ripening times (palm) and those without (rutab). He discusses the effect if the term is specified and fruit appears or not. Then he quotes fatwas from al-Khulasa, al-Muhit, and Jami' al-Fatawa about extremely long terms. The commentator then presents the matn again and the disagreement with al-Shafi'i, who restricts musaqah to vines and palms. The Hanafi proof is the Prophet's practice at Khaybar, which is general and cannot be restricted by opinion. He then includes several fatwas: Abu al-Layth on trees needing only preservation, al-Tajrid on multiple workers with different shares, Jami' al-Fatawa on difference between Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa, Sharh al-Tahawi on planting trees with share, al-Atabiyyah on who owns trees if planted by worker, and Abu al-Layth on a dispute about planting on riverbanks. These illustrate practical applications of the general principle that musaqah is valid on all fruit-bearing trees.

Key Terms
المساقاة (al-musaqah): A contract of partnership in fruit trees where one party provides the trees and land, and the other works on them in exchange for a share of the fruit.
الكرم (al-karm): Vineyard or grapevines.
الشجر (al-shajar): Trees in general, here referring to fruit-bearing trees.
الرطب (al-rutab): Fresh dates still on the palm, or the palm itself bearing rutab.
أصول الباذنجان (usul al-badhinjan): Eggplant roots, here meaning the plants that bear fruit annually.
المزارعة (al-muzara'ah): Sharecropping contract for land cultivation, similar to musaqah but for annual crops.
الأجرة (al-ujrah): Wage or rent; in this context, the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) for the worker if contract is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for allowing musaqah on all fruit trees?
A) Qiyas on palm trees.
B) The Prophet's contract with the people of Khaibar on what comes out of fruit.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) The general custom of Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Musaqah is valid on all fruit-bearing trees according to the Hanafi school, based on the general Khaybar hadith; the duration may be left unspecified for trees with known fruiting seasons.

Musaqah on Trees with Existing Fruit and Consequences of Invalidity
Ruling on musaqah when tree already has fruit and compensation if contract invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of musaqah when the tree already has fruit, and determine the compensation due if the contract is invalid.

Core Idea
Musaqah on a fruit-bearing tree is valid if fruit increases with work, but invalid contract gives worker equivalent wage.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on musaqah contracts where the tree already bears fruit. The key principle is that the contract is valid only as long as the worker's labor adds value. Once the fruit ripens fully, the contract ends. If the contract is invalid from the start, the worker is entitled to a fair market wage, treating the arrangement akin to an invalid hire contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The contract is valid if the fruit increases with work; after the fruit reaches full ripeness, the contract does not continue like muzara'ah.
The text explicitly states: 'so if it were permissible after ripening, he would be entitled without work'.
2
Understand the rationale
The worker is only entitled through work; after ripening no work is needed, so the contract cannot continue.
This is based on the principle that entitlement without work is not legislated.
3
Distinguish from muzara'ah
In muzara'ah, a contract may continue even after the crop is ready? But here the text says it is not like muzara'ah, indicating a difference in ruling.
Muzara'ah is sharecropping on land; musaqah is on trees; the difference arises from the nature of the work.
4
Apply the compensation rule
If the musaqah contract becomes invalid, the worker gets ajr al-mithl (fair wage) because the contract is akin to ijarah (hire).
The analogy is to invalid muzara'ah where the worker also gets ajr al-mithl.
5
Note the analogy to ijarah
The contract is not a pure ijarah but shares its compensation rules when invalid.
This is based on the principle that the worker's labor must be compensated fairly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن دفع نخلا فيه ثمرة مساقاة والثمر يزيد بالعمل صحت وإن انتهت لا كالمزارعة) لأن العامل لا يستحق إلا بالعمل ولا أثر للعمل بعد التناهي فلو جاز بعد الإدراك لا يستحق إلا بلا عمل ولم يرد به الشرع، ولا يجوز الحاقه بما قبل التناهي لأن جوازه قبل التناهي للحاجة على خلاف القياس ولا حاجة إلى مثله فبقي على الأصل. قال رحمه الله : (فإذا فسدت فللعامل أجر مثله لأنها في معنى الإجارة كالمزارعة إذا فسدت وقد تقدم بيانه.
He (the author) said: (If he gives a date palm that has fruit as musaqah, and the fruit increases with work, the contract is valid; if the fruit reaches completion (ripens), it is not like muzara'ah.) Because the worker is only entitled through work, and there is no effect of work after completion; so if it were permissible after ripening, he would be entitled without work, and such has not been legislated. And it is not to be analogized to before completion, because its permissibility before completion is due to necessity, contrary to analogy, and there is no such need after, so it remains on the original principle. He (the author) said: (If it becomes invalid, then the worker has his equivalent wage) because it is akin to a hiring (ijarah), like muzara'ah when it becomes invalid, and its explanation has preceded.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage explains two connected matn statements. First, if a date palm already has fruit at the time of the musaqah contract, the contract is valid because the fruit increases with the worker's labor. The clarification: if the fruit reaches full ripeness (tamr) during the contract period, the contract does not continue like muzara'ah (which might allow continuation for ripening) because after ripening no work is needed, and entitlement without work is against Islamic law. The validity before ripening is an exception to analogy due to need. Second, if the musaqah contract becomes invalid (e.g., due to a defect), the worker is entitled to the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl), similar to an invalid muzara'ah, because the contract is analogous to hire (ijarah).

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage for the worker's labor, determined by what similar workers earn.
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract of hire or lease; musaqah is considered akin to ijarah for compensation purposes when invalid.
التناهي (al-tanahi): Completion, here meaning the fruit reaching full ripeness (tamr) where no further work is needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider musaqah on a tree with fruit valid?
A) Because the fruit is already ripe for harvest.
B) Because the fruit increases with the worker's labor.
C) Because it is a form of sale.
D) Because the owner cannot take it back.

Key Takeaway
The validity of musaqah on a fruit-bearing tree depends on the fruit's potential to increase with work; upon ripening, the contract ends, and if invalid, the worker receives fair wage.

Termination of Musaqah by Death and Rights of Heirs
Ruling that musaqah is voided by death and the worker's right to continue until harvest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that musaqah is voided by death and explain the istihsan exception allowing the worker to continue tending unripe fruit to avoid harm.

Core Idea
Musaqah invalid by death, but istihsan lets worker continue to avoid harm.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the effect of death on a musaqah contract. The basic ruling is that the contract becomes void (batil) upon the death of either party, based on analogy to ijarah. However, if the fruit is unripe, the worker is allowed to continue tending it by istihsan to prevent loss, and the heirs cannot prevent him. The passage also discusses the heirs' options if the worker agrees to bear the risk of loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The matn states 'And it becomes invalid by death'. Identify that the default ruling is batil and the proof is qiyas to ijarah (hire).
The author says 'because it is akin to hire'.
2
Understand the istihsan exception
Note that by istihsan (juristic preference), the worker may continue tending the fruit until it ripens. This overrides the strict qiyas to avoid harm (darar) to the worker.
The text says 'to avoid harm to him'.
3
Analyze the heirs' rights when worker assumes risk
If the worker agrees to bear the potential loss (if the fruit perishes), the heirs have three options: divide the unripe fruit per the contract share, pay the value of the worker's share, or spend to ripen the fruit and claim reimbursement from the worker.
This is a secondary scenario, not the default.
4
Note the ishkal (difficulty)
The commentator flags a textual issue in the source regarding the worker's recourse, indicating that later scholars noted an ambiguity.
The phrase 'there is an issue (ishkal) in his recourse'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وتبطل بالموت) لأنها في معنى الإجارة كالمزارعة فإن مات رب الأرض والخارج بسراً فللعامل أن يقوم عليه كما كان يقوم عليه قبل ذلك إلا أن تدرك الثمرة، وليس لورثته أن يمنعوه من ذلك استحساناً كما في المزراعة لأن في منعه إلحاق الضرر به فيبقى العقد دفعاً للضرر عنه ولا ضرر على الورثة. ولو التزم العامل الضرر يخير أن ورثة الآخر أن بين يقسموا البسر على الشرط وبين أن يعطوه قيمة نصيبه من البسر وبين ينفقوا على البسر حتى يدرك فيرجعون على المعامل بحصته من الثمر لأنه ليس له إلحاق الضرر به كما في المزارعة ; هكذا ذكر صاحب الهداية وغيره وفي رجوعه في حصته إشكال،
He (the author) said: (And it becomes invalid by death) because it is akin to hire, like muzara'ah. If the owner of the land dies and the fruit (appearing) is unripe (busr), the worker has the right to tend it as he used to before, until the fruit ripens, and his heirs cannot prevent him from that by istihsan, as in muzara'ah, because preventing him would cause him harm, so the contract remains to avoid harm to him, and there is no harm to the heirs. If the worker assumes the (potential) harm, the heirs of the other (the deceased owner) have the choice between dividing the unripe fruit according to the condition, giving him the value of his share of the unripe fruit, or spending on the unripe fruit until it ripens and then claiming from the worker his share of the fruit, because he (the deceased) has no right to cause him harm, as in muzara'ah. Thus mentioned by the author of al-Hidayah and others, but there is an issue (ishkal) in his recourse regarding his share.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage explains the matn statement that musaqah is voided by the death of either party, because it is analogous to hire (ijarah). However, by istihsan, the worker is allowed to continue tending the fruit (busr - unripe dates) until they ripen, to prevent loss to him. The heirs of the deceased owner cannot prevent this if it would cause harm to the worker. If the worker agrees to bear the loss (i.e., if the fruit perishes), the heirs have three options: (1) divide the unripe fruit as per the contract share, (2) pay the worker the value of his share of the unripe fruit, or (3) themselves spend money to ripen the fruit and then claim their share from the worker. The commentator notes that there is a difficulty (ishkal) in the wording regarding the worker's recourse, possibly referring to a textual issue in the source.

Key Terms
البسر (al-busr): Unripe dates; here the fruit that is not yet fully ripe at the time of death.
الإستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; here used to allow the worker to continue tending the fruit despite the contract being voided, to avoid harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school allow the worker to continue tending the fruit after the death of the landowner?
A) Because the contract is still valid after death.
B) By istihsan to avoid harm to the worker.
C) Because the fruit belongs to the worker.
D) Because the heirs are obligated to hire him.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that musaqah is voided by death, but by istihsan the worker may continue to tend the fruit until ripe to avoid harm, with the heirs having options if the worker bears the loss.

The Core Condition of Musaqah: Fruit Must Increase by Work
Opening of Kitab al-Musaqah with matn and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the essential condition for a valid musaqah contract and explain the Prophetic proof, and identify when the contract becomes fasid and the worker's entitlement.

Core Idea
Musaqah is valid only if the fruit increases through the worker's labor; otherwise it is invalid.

This lesson opens the Book of Musaqah from al-Bahr al-Raiq. The matn concisely states the key condition: the contract is valid only when the fruit is capable of increase by work. The commentary expands with the Prophetic precedent and several fatwa examples illustrating when the condition is met or broken. Understanding this foundational rule will help you distinguish valid musaqah from invalid arrangements and know the legal consequences of a fasid contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling in the matn
Read the matn: 'والثمر يزيد بالعمل صحت' — the contract is valid if the fruit increases through work. This is the central condition.
If the fruit is already ripe or does not require work, the contract is not valid.
2
Locate the Prophetic proof
The matn cites the action of the Prophet ﷺ with the people of Khaybar. This proof is absolute and cannot be restricted to only some trees.
The proof is from Sunnah ahad (zanni thubut) but its dalala is qati regarding permissibility.
3
Understand the term 'absolute' (mutlaq)
The commentary explains that the proof is mutlaq, so we cannot restrict it to specific types of trees by opinion (ra'y). It applies to all fruit trees capable of increase through work.
Restriction would be taqyid without dalil, which is not permissible.
4
Analyze the fatwa examples
The passage provides multiple fatwa scenarios: trees needing no work, multiple workers, planting on land (ghirs). For each, determine if the condition of work increasing fruit is met.
For example, if trees only need preservation and fruit would perish without it, the contract is invalid because work does not increase fruit but merely prevents loss.
5
Summarize the consequences of fasid musaqah
If the contract is fasid (invalid due to missing condition), the worker receives ujr al-mithl (standard wage) for the work done, not the agreed share. All produce belongs to the tree owner.
This is the general rule for fasid contracts in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المساقاة
والثمر يزيد بالعمل صحت وإن انتهت لا كالمزارعة فإذا فسدت فللعامل أجر مثله
النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عامل أهل خيبر على ما يخرج من ثمر. وهذا مطلق فلا يجوز قصره على بعض الأشجار دون بعض لأنه تقييد فلا يجوز بالرأي. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : دفع كرماً معاملة وفيه أشجار لا تحتاج إلى عمل سوى الحفظ، فإن كان بحال لو لم تحفظ يذهب ثمرها قبل الإدراك لا تجوز المعاملة في تلك الأشجار ولا نصيب للعامل فيها. وفي التجريد: رجل دفع نخلاً إلى رجلين معاملة على أن لأحدهم السدس وللآخر النصف ولرب الأرض الثلث فهي جائزة، ولو شرطوا الصاحب النخل الثلث وللآخر الثلثان وللثالث أجر مائة على العامل فهذا فاسد، والخارج كله لرب النخل ويرجع العامل الذي شرط له الثلثان على رب النخل ولرب النخل الثلثان وللثالث الثلث فهي جائزة. وفي جامع الفتاوى لو دفع إلى رجلين جاز عند أبي يوسف ولا يجوز عند الإمام. وفي شرح الطحاوي ولو أن رجلاً دفع أرضه معاملة على أن يغرس العامل فيها أغراساً والغراس يكون بينهما فهذا يجوز ، فإذا انقضت المدة فلرب الأرض أن يطالبه بقلع الأشجار وليس له أن يتملكها بغير رضا المستأجر إذا لم يضر القلع بالأرض، فإن كان يضرها ضرراً فاحشاً فله أن يتملكها بغير رضاه. وفي الفتاوى العتابية : إذا دفع أرضه للغرس على أن الغراس بينهما، فإن كان الغراس من جانب صاحب الأرض فغرس فالغراس كله لصاحب الأرض، وإن كان للعامل وقال له اغرسها فالغراس لصاحب الأرض وللعامل عليه قيمتها اهـ. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : لو غرس حافتي نهر فقال رجل غرست لي لأنك كنت خادمي وفي عيالي وقال الغارس لنفسي، فإن عرف أن الغارس كان وقت الغراس في عياله يعمل له مثل هذا العمل فالشجر ،له وإن لم يعرف ذلك فللغارس ذلك اهـ .
Book of Musaqah. And the fruit increases with work, it is valid; and if it ends, it is not like mazar'a. So if it becomes invalid, the worker gets his like wage. The Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم contracted with the people of Khaybar on what comes out of fruit. And this is absolute, so it is not permissible to restrict it to some trees without others because that is a restriction and it is not permissible by opinion. In Fatawa Abi al-Layth: He gave a vineyard as mu'amala, and in it there are trees that do not need work except preservation; if it is such that if not preserved, its fruit would perish before ripening, the mu'amala is not valid in those trees and no share for the worker. In al-Tajrid: A man gave palm trees to two men as mu'amala on condition that one gets one-sixth, the other half, and the landowner one-third; it is valid. If they stipulated that the owner of the palms gets one-third, another gets two-thirds, and a third gets a wage of one hundred on the worker, this is invalid, and all the produce is for the owner of the palms, and the worker who was stipulated two-thirds has recourse against the owner of the palms, and the owner of the palms gets two-thirds, and the third gets one-third; it is valid. In Jami' al-Fatawa: If he gave to two men, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf and not valid according to Imam. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If a man gave his land as mu'amala for the worker to plant trees, and the trees are between them, this is permissible. When the term ends, the landowner may demand the uprooting of the trees, and he may not own them without the lessee's consent if uprooting does not harm the land. If it harms it excessively, he may own them without his consent. In al-Fatawa al-'Atabiyya: If he gave his land for planting on condition that the trees are between them, if the planting is from the side of the landowner and he plants, the trees are entirely for the landowner. If it is for the worker and he said to him 'plant them', the trees are for the landowner and the worker has against him their value. In Fatawa Abi al-Layth: If he planted the banks of a river, and one man said 'you planted for me because you were my servant and in my household', and the planter said 'for myself', if it is known that the planter at the time of planting was in his household working such work for him, the trees are for him; if that is not known, then for the planter.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq opens the Book of Musaqah. It begins with the matn stating the core ruling: Musaqah (irrigation contract for trees) is valid when the fruit increases through the worker's labor. If the fruit has already ripened and no further work is needed, the contract is invalid—unlike mazar'a (sharecropping of land) where the contract can continue even after the crop is ripe? Actually the text says it is not like mazar'a, meaning that in mazar'a the contract may be valid even after the crop is ripe under certain conditions? The commentary then provides the proof from the Prophet's ﷺ treatment of the people of Khaybar, which is a general contract, so it cannot be restricted to only some trees. Then various fatwa examples are given: trees that don't need work but only preservation; if their fruit would perish without preservation, the contract is invalid for those trees. Multiple workers: if shares are stipulated, it may be valid or invalid depending on the shares. There is also a difference of opinion between Abu Yusuf and Imam Abu Hanifa regarding giving to two workers. The passage then discusses cases of planting on land (ghirs) which is similar to musaqah. In all cases, the key is that the worker must perform work that increases the fruit for the contract to be valid. If the contract becomes fasid (invalid) for any reason, the worker receives ujr al-mithl (like wage) for his work.

Key Terms
مساقاة (musaqah): A contract where a worker tends to fruit-bearing trees and receives a share of the produce.
مزارعة (mazar'a): A contract where a worker cultivates land and receives a share of the crop.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The standard market wage for similar work in a fasid contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following makes a musaqah contract invalid (fasid)?
A) The fruit increases through the worker's labor.
B) The contract includes trees that only require preservation, and the fruit would perish without it.
C) The shares are clearly specified as fractions.
D) The worker is given a share of the fruit.

Key Takeaway
A musaqah contract is valid only when the fruit is capable of increase through the worker's labor; if the fruit is already ripe or work does not increase yield, the contract is invalid and the worker receives ujr al-mithl.

Ruling on Fasid Musaqah: Worker Gets Ujr al-Mithl
Matn stating the consequence of a corrupt musaqah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on compensation when a musaqah contract becomes fasid and explain the analogy (qiyas) to ijarah.

Core Idea
In a fasid musaqah, the worker gets ujr al-mithl, not the agreed share.

This lesson addresses a critical principle in Hanafi muamalat: what happens when a valid-looking contract turns out to be fasid? The matn rules that the worker still deserves compensation, but at the standard market rate (ujr al-mithl), not the agreed share. This ruling is derived by analogy to ijarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type and status
Musaqah is a contract for tending trees in exchange for a share of fruit. Here it is ruled fasid (invalid).
2
State the ruling for the worker
The matn says: 'فإذا فسدت فللعامل أجر مثله' — the worker gets ujr al-mithl, not the agreed share.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The text explains: لأنها في معنى الإجارة — musaqah is in the meaning of ijarah because the worker provides labor. So the ruling follows that of a fasid ijarah: ujr al-mithl.
4
Apply the general principle
In Hanafi law, when a contract of service is fasid, the worker is entitled to ujr al-mithl for work actually done. This protects the worker from loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإذا فسدت فللعامل أجر مثله) لأنها في معنى الإجارة كالمزارعة إذا فسدت وقد تقدم بيانه.
He (the author) said: (If it becomes invalid, then the worker gets his like wage) because it is in the meaning of ijarah like mazar'a if it becomes invalid, and its explanation has preceded.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This is a short matn and its commentary. The matn clarifies that if a musaqah contract becomes fasid (invalid), the worker is entitled to ujr al-mithl (like wage) for his work, not the agreed share. The reason given is that musaqah is in the nature of ijarah (hire) because the worker provides labor. This is analogous to mazar'a (sharecropping) when it becomes fasid. The commentator notes that this has been explained earlier (presumably in the book). The ruling is straightforward: the worker does not lose his right to compensation; he gets the market value of his labor.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The standard wage for similar work in the market.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid musaqah contract, what is the worker entitled to?
A) The agreed share of fruit.
B) Nothing.
C) Ujr al-mithl (like wage).
D) The entire crop.

Key Takeaway
In a fasid musaqah, the worker is entitled to ujr al-mithl (standard wage) for labor performed, not the agreed share.

Dissolution of Musaqah by Excuse
Matn and commentary on termination of musaqah by excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a musaqah contract may be dissolved by excuse and apply the analogy to ijarah.

Core Idea
Musaqah is dissolved by excuse because it resembles ijarah, which is terminable.

A musaqah (sharecropping of trees) is not an absolutely binding contract. The Hanafi school permits its dissolution (faskh) when a valid excuse ('udhr) arises, such as the worker becoming a thief or falling ill. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof through analogy (qiyas) to ijarah, and a difference of opinion within the school regarding a healthy worker's right to leave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The matn states 'وتفسخ بالعذر' (it is dissolved by excuse). Determine that this is a permissibility (jawaz) to rescind, not an obligation. Note that the excuse must be genuine and material.
The ruling applies to musaqah, analogous to mazar'a.
2
Examine the examples of valid excuses
The text gives two examples: the worker being a thief (steals fruit or palm leaves) or being sick and unable to work. These cause harm to the landowner or render performance impossible.
Other excuses may be analogized; only these are explicit in the passage.
3
Understand the proof: qiyas to ijarah
The commentary states 'لأنها في معنى الإجارة' (because it is in the meaning of ijarah). Since ijarah (hire) can be dissolved by excuse, musaqah follows the same rule due to shared illa (effective cause): both involve compensation for work and are not fully binding like a sale.
This is a clear qiyas jali (manifest analogy).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on healthy worker
The text reports two opinions: (1) a healthy worker may leave work before starting, (2) he may not. The phrase 'بالاتفاق' (by agreement) suggests the disagreement is unresolved in this passage.
This ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school; no tarjih is given.
5
Place the ruling in the broader framework
The author introduces a classification of mazar'a (and by analogy musaqah) into three categories: death, dissolution due to debt, and expiry of term. This helps organize the rules of termination.
The text is cut off before fully explaining the debt-related scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وتفسخ بالعذر كالمزارعة بأن يكون العامل سارقاً أو مريضاً لا يقدر على العمل لأنها في معنى الإجارة وقد بينا أنها تفسخ بالأعذار وكونه سارقاً عذر ظاهر لأنه يسرق الثمر والسعف ويحلق الآخر الضرر ولو أراد العامل ترك العمل في الصحيح، وقيل يمكن وقيل لا يمكن بالاتفاق . قال أصله أن المزارعة لازمة من جهة من لا بذر منه غير لازمة من جهة رب البذر ، ثم مسائله على ثلاثة أقسام : قسم في الموت، وقسم في فسخ قيله بالدين، وقسم في انقضاء المدة. وإذا أراد . من قبله البذر قبل العمل ليس له ذلك إلا أن يكون عليه دين لا وفاء إلا منه، فإن باعها بالدين لم يكن عليه من نفقة العامل شيء في حفر الأنهار وإصلاحها لأن المنافع لا تتقوم إلا العقد من رب الأرض أن يفسخ ا العقد وليس
He said: And it is dissolved by excuse like mazar'a, such as the worker being a thief or sick, unable to work, because it is in the meaning of ijarah, and we have explained that it is dissolved by excuses. And him being a thief is an obvious excuse because he steals fruit and palm leaves and causes harm to the other. And if the worker wants to leave work while healthy, it is said it is possible and it is said it is not possible by agreement. He said: The origin is that mazar'a is binding from the side of the one who does not have the seed, not binding from the side of the owner of the seed. Then its issues are three categories: a category in death, a category in dissolution due to debt, and a category in expiry of term. And if the one who has the seed wants [to terminate] before work, he may not unless he has a debt that can only be paid from it. If he sells it for the debt, there is no expense on him for the worker's work in digging canals and repairing them, because benefits are not valued except... the contract from the landowner that he dissolves the contract and not...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage covers the dissolution of musaqah by excuse ('udhr). The matn states that musaqah can be terminated by a valid excuse, analogous to mazar'a. Examples given: the worker being a thief (steals fruit) or being sick and unable to work. The commentary draws on the principle that musaqah is like ijarah (hire), and ijarah can be terminated by excuses. There is a discussion on whether a healthy worker can unilaterally leave work; there are two opinions, but the text does not resolve. The passage then shifts to the origin that mazar'a is binding only on the party who does not provide seed, not on the seed owner. Then it categorizes issues into three: death, dissolution due to debt, and expiry of term. The text then begins a discussion about a seed owner wanting to terminate before work, but the OCR cuts off. The incomplete part likely says that the seed owner cannot terminate except if he has a debt, and if he sells the crop for the debt, he does not owe the worker's expenses.

Key Terms
عذر ('udhr): A valid legal excuse such as theft or illness that justifies termination of the contract.
فسخ (faskh): Dissolution or rescission of a contract due to an excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for allowing dissolution of musaqah by excuse?
A) The Quranic verse on contracts.
B) Analogy to ijarah (qiyas).
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Public interest (maslahah).

Key Takeaway
Musaqah can be dissolved by a valid excuse because it is analogous to ijarah, which is terminable for similar reasons.

10 min
Voiding of Masaqah by Death and Rescission by Excuse (with Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Expense Recovery)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on expense recovery in Masaqah upon death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that Masaqah becomes void by death and rescinded by excuse, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over expense recovery when the owner dies, giving the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Masaqah voids by death; heirs recover half expenses from the worker's share, like Muzara'ah.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on Masaqah when the owner dies or an excuse arises. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states it becomes void by death and rescinded by excuse, analogous to Muzara'ah. The commentary then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: do the heirs recover all or half of their expenses from the worker's share? We will trace the arguments and settle on the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
State the ruling from the matn: Masaqah becomes void (batil) by death and is rescinded (munfasikh) by a valid excuse, just like Muzara'ah.
This establishes the analogy between Masaqah and Muzara'ah.
2
Understand the expense recovery problem
When the owner dies and the worker continues with the heirs' permission, the heirs may incur expenses on the trees. The question is: how much of those expenses can they recover from the worker's share of the produce?
The worker's entitlement is based on work; the work is all on him if he continues alone.
3
Analyze the logical argument for full recovery
Some argue that since the worker does all the work, the heirs should recover all their expenses from the worker's share. If they only recover his share, it implies the work is jointly owed, leading to the worker being entitled without working for part of the period – a contradiction.
This view is based on the premise that the worker's work is entirely his obligation.
4
Contrast with the transmitted texts
The relied-upon position comes from al-Kafi by al-Nasafi and al-Hakim al-Shahid: 'And they revert half of their expenses in the worker's share as in Muzara'ah.' Al-Tatarkhaniyyah also supports half-revert when the heirs spend under court order.
The half-revert is transmitted (manqul) and takes precedence over pure logic.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) prefers the half-revert as the transmitted narration, making it the operative ruling for fatwa.
Masaqah and Muzara'ah are of one category (bab wahid), so the same rule applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتبطل بالموت وتفسخ بالعذر كالمزارعة .
عليه بجميعه
لأن العامل إنما يستحق بالعمل وكان العمل كله عليه أن يرجعو وكان ينبغي ولهذا إذ اختار المضي أو لم يمت صاحبه كان العمل كله عليه فلو رجعوا عليه بحصته فقط يؤدي إلى أن العمل يجب عليهما حتى يستحق المؤنة بحصته فقط وهذا خلف لأنه يؤدي إلى استحقاق العامل بلا عمل في عمل بعض المدة، وهذا الإشكال وارد في المزارعة أيضاً؛ كذا في الشارح. وإجاب بعض الأفاضل بأن المعنى يرجعون في حصة العامل بجميع ما أنفقوا لا بحصته كما فهمه فيرد على هذا المجيب بأن المنقول في الكافي للعلامة النسفي. وفي الحاكم الشهيد ما نص عبارته ويرجعون بنصف نفقتهم في حصة العامل كما في المزارعة اهـ. فحمله غير صحيح. ونقل في التتارخانية في فصل الموت في المزارعة إذا أنفق ورثة رب النفقة مقدار بالحصة، وإذا أنفق رب الأرض بأمر القاضي يرجعون على المزارع بجميع الأرض بإذن القاضي يرجع بنصف النفقة .اهـ. ولا يخفى أن المعاملة والمزارعة من باب واحد فما قاله الشارح ظهر منقولاً .
And it becomes void by death and is rescinded by excuse, like Muzara'ah. It [the expense] falls on him entirely, because the worker only becomes entitled by work, and the work was all on him—they should revert [expenses] and it was fitting. Hence when he chooses to continue or his companion did not die, all the work is on him. If they revert upon him only his share, it leads to the work being obligatory on both, so that the sustenance is entitled only by his share, and this is contradictory because it leads to the worker being entitled without work in working part of the period. This problem also occurs in Muzara'ah; thus in the Sharh. Some virtuous ones answered that the meaning is they revert in the worker's share all that they spent, not his share as understood. This responder is rebutted because what is transmitted in al-Kafi by al-Allamah al-Nasafi and in al-Hakim al-Shahid is the text of his statement: 'And they revert half of their expenses in the worker's share as in Muzara'ah.' So his interpretation is incorrect. And it is transmitted in al-Tatarkhaniyyah in the chapter on death in Muzara'ah: When the heirs of the owner spend an amount according to the share, and when the landowner spends by the judge's order, they revert upon the sharecropper with all [expenses]? With the judge's permission he reverts half of the expenses. It is not hidden that Mu'amalah and Muzara'ah are of one category, so what the commentator said appears transmitted.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling of Masaqah (orchard tenancy) upon the death of one party and regarding rescission by excuse. The basic ruling from the matn is that Masaqah becomes void (batil) by death and is rescinded (tunfasakh) by excuse, just like Muzara'ah (crop-sharing tenancy). The commentary then delves into a detailed issue: when the owner dies, how do the heirs of the owner recover expenses they incurred on the trees? The commentator explains that if the worker continues, he owes all expenses because the work is entirely on him. If they only recover his share, it leads to a logical contradiction where the worker would be entitled without working for a part of the period. Some virtuous scholars (some afadil) interpreted that the heirs recover all their expenses from the worker's share, not just his portion. However, this interpretation is rejected because the transmitted text in al-Kafi and al-Hakim al-Shahid clearly states that they recover only half of their expenses from the worker's share, as in Muzara'ah. The Tatarkhaniyyah also supports this: when the landowner's heirs spend by court order, they revert half the expenses. The passage concludes that Mu'amalah (Masaqah) and Muzara'ah are of the same category, so what the commentator (al-Sharh) said is supported by transmission. The key takeaway is that Masaqah and Muzara'ah are analogous in the rulings of death and excuse, and the established Hanafi position is that expenses are shared equally unless otherwise specified.

Key Terms
المساقاة (al-musāqāh): A contract of sharecropping on fruit trees, where one party provides trees and the other works for a share of the produce.
المزارعة (al-muzāra‘ah): A contract of sharecropping on land, where one party provides land and the other works for a share of the crop.
الفسخ (al-faskh): The rescission of a contract due to an excuse, rendering it void ab initio or from the time of excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Masaqah contract, when the owner dies and the worker continues, how much of the expenses incurred by the heirs are recoverable from the worker's share according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) All expenses
B) Half of the expenses
C) No expenses can be recovered
D) Only the worker's share of expenses

Key Takeaway
Masaqah voids by death and is rescinded by excuse; the relied-upon Hanafi position is that heirs recover half expenses from the worker's share, based on transmitted texts.

Continuation of Masaqah After Worker's Death
Ruling on death of worker and comparisons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rights of the worker's heirs upon his death in a Masaqah contract and distinguish between khiyar in financial rights and khiyar al-shart regarding inheritability.

Core Idea
The worker's heirs may continue the Masaqah contract; their option to leave fruit on trees is a financial right that is inherited.

When a worker in a Masaqah contract dies, what happens to the arrangement? The Hanafi school grants his heirs the right to continue or terminate, while the landowner cannot impose his own choice. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its underlying reasoning, highlighting the distinction between inheritable options and non-inheritable stipulations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Consider the death of the worker in a Masaqah contract. The passage first states that his heirs may continue the contract on his behalf, and the landowner cannot force them out or require them to continue.
2
Determine the nature of the option
The option given to the heirs (to continue or leave the fruit on trees) is classified as a financial right (khiyar fi haqq mali) and is therefore inheritable. Contrast this with khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), which is not inheritable.
Only financial rights related to the subject matter of the contract pass to heirs.
3
Examine the post-term situation
If the contract term ends while the fruit is still green (busr), the worker (or his heirs) may stay on the trees until the fruit ripens, without paying rent. This is similar to Muzara'ah, but with a key difference: no rent is due because trees cannot be rented.
In Muzara'ah, the sharecropper must pay land rent after term because land can be rented.
4
Understand the talil (reasoning)
The reasoning ('illa) for the difference lies in the nature of the object: trees produce fruit that is not yet quantifiable at rental, whereas land's usufruct can be valued. Hence, after the term, all work falls on the worker in Masaqah, while in Muzara'ah work is shared because land rent compensates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مات العامل فلورثته أن يقيموا عليه وليس لرب الأرض أن ذلك لأن فيه النظر من الجانبين فإذا أرادوا أن يضربوه بسراً كان صاحب الأرض يمنعهم من بين الخيارات الثلاث التي ذكرناها، وإن ماتا جميعاً فالخيار لورثة العامل لقيامهم مقامه، وهذا خيار في حق مالي وهو ترك الثمار على الأشجار إلى وقت الإدراك فيورث بخلاف خيار الشرط فإن أبوا ورثة العامل أن يقيموا عليه كان الخيار في ذلك لورثة رب الأرض على ما ذكرنا، وإذا انقضت مدة العامل وكان الخارج بسراً أخضر فهو كالمزارعة إذا انقضت، مدتها فللعامل أن يقسم عليها إلى أن تنتهي الثمار كما أن ذلك للمزارع لكن هنا لا يجب على العامل أجرة حصته إلا أن يدرك لأن الشجر لا يجوز استئجاره بخلاف المزارعة حيث يجب على المزارع أجر مثل الأرض إلى أن يدرك الزرع لأن الأرض يجوز استئجارها. وكذا العمل كله على العامل هنا وفي المزارعة عليهما لأنه لما وجب أجر مثل الأرض بعد انتهاء المدة في المزارعة لا يستحق العمل عليه كما كان يستحق قبل انتهائها .
And if the worker dies, his heirs may continue [the contract] on his behalf, and the landowner does not have that right, because there is benefit from both sides. If they wish to leave the fruit unripe on the trees, the landowner prevents them from the three options we mentioned. If both die, the option is for the worker's heirs because they stand in his place. This is an option regarding wealth—leaving the fruit on the trees until ripening—so it is inherited, unlike the option of stipulation. If the worker's heirs refuse to continue, then the option in that lies with the landowner's heirs as we mentioned. When the worker's period expires and the fruit is unripe green, it is like Muzara'ah when its term expires: the worker may stay on it until the fruit finishes, just as that applies to the sharecropper. But here, no wage for his share is obligatory on the worker unless it ripens, because trees cannot be rented, unlike Muzara'ah where the sharecropper must pay the land's equivalent rent until the crop ripens, because land can be rented. Similarly, all the work is on the worker here, while in Muzara'ah it is on both, because when the equivalent rent of land becomes obligatory after the term in Muzara'ah, the work is not due on him as it was before the end of the term.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on the death of the worker in a Masaqah contract. When the worker dies, his heirs have the right to continue the contract in his place; the landowner cannot force them to stop or continue. If both parties die, the worker's heirs get the choice because they represent the worker. The option to leave unripe fruit on the trees is a financial right that is inherited, unlike the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) which is not inheritable. If the term expires while the fruit is still unripe (green), the worker may remain on the trees until the fruit is ripe, similar to a Muzara'ah worker after the term ends. However, a key difference is that in Masaqah, the worker does not owe rent for his share unless the fruit actually ripens, because trees cannot be rented (their usufruct is not quantifiable in the same way). In Muzara'ah, the sharecropper must pay the land's equivalent rent after the term ends because land can be rented. Consequently, after the term, all work falls on the worker in Masaqah, whereas in Muzara'ah it falls on both parties, because the obligation of land rent compensates for the work.

Key Terms
الخيار في حق مالي (al-khiyār fī ḥaqq mālī): An option related to a financial right, such as leaving fruit on the tree until ripening; it is inheritable.
البسر (al-busr): Unripe dates that are still green but have changed color from the initial stage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Masaqah contract, after the expiry of the term while the fruit is still green, does the worker owe rent for his share?
A) Yes, he must pay the landowner the equivalent rent
B) No, unless the fruit actually ripens
C) He must pay half the rent
D) The landowner pays him for staying

Key Takeaway
The worker's heirs may continue the Masaqah contract, and their option to leave fruit on trees is an inheritable financial right; after the term, the worker stays without rent until the fruit ripens, differing from Muzara'ah due to the nature of trees.

Rescission of Masaqah by Excuse and the Principle of Bindingness
Ruling on rescission by excuse and the binding principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid excuses for rescinding a Masaqah contract and explain why the contract is binding only on the party who does not provide the seed.

Core Idea
Masaqah is rescinded by valid excuses like theft or illness, and the seed-provider may rescind before work.

The passage opens with the ruling that Masaqah, like Muzara'ah, can be rescinded by a valid excuse, giving examples of the worker being a thief or sick. This is because the contract is akin to a lease (ijarah), which permits rescission by excuse. The author then introduces a key principle: the contract is binding on the worker (non-seed provider) but not on the seed owner. This principle governs the subsequent discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify valid excuses
Find the excuses listed: worker being a thief or sick, unable to work. These are valid reasons for the owner to rescind the contract.
Other excuses may be analogized.
2
Recognize the analogy to ijarah
The text states that Masaqah is 'in the meaning of ijarah'. Understand that ijarah allows rescission by excuse, so the same applies here.
This is a qiyas (analogy).
3
Understand the binding principle
The principle: the contract is binding on the one who does not provide seed (worker) but not on the seed owner. Therefore, the seed owner can rescind before work begins.
This contrasts with the general rule that contracts are binding on both parties.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a disagreement on whether the worker can abandon work without an excuse. Two opinions are mentioned: possible and not possible.
This shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وتفسخ بالعذر كالمزارعة بأن يكون العامل سارقاً أو مريضاً لا يقدر على العمل لأنها في معنى الإجارة وقد بينا أنها تفسخ بالأعذار وكونه سارقاً عذر ظاهر لأنه يسرق الثمر والسعف ويحلق الآخر الضرر ولو أراد العامل ترك العمل في الصحيح، وقيل يمكن وقيل لا يمكن بالاتفاق . قال أصله أن المزارعة لازمة من جهة من لا بذر منه غير لازمة من جهة رب البذر ، ثم مسائله على ثلاثة أقسام : قسم في الموت، وقسم في فسخ قيله بالدين، وقسم في انقضاء المدة. وإذا أراد . من قبله البذر قبل العمل ليس له ذلك إلا أن يكون عليه دين لا وفاء إلا منه، فإن باعها بالدين لم يكن عليه من نفقة العامل شيء في حفر الأنهار وإصلاحها لأن المنافع لا تتقوم إلا
الأرض
الاستنماء
بالعقد أو شبهه ولم يوجد ذلك ومتى كان البذر من قبله بأن يكون مستأجراً للأرض فإن نبت الزرع لا يباع حتى يستحصد لكن القاضي يخرجه من الحبس ولا يحول بينه وبين الغرماء لأن في البيع إبطال حق العامل وفي ترك البيع تأخير حق رب الدين والتأخير أهون من الإبطال، فلو زرع ولم ينبت فقد اختلفوا فيه؛ قيل لصاحب الأرض بيعها بالدين لأنه ليس للزرع في الأرض حق قائم لأن القاء البذر استهلاك، وقيل ليس له البيع لأن القاء البذر من وليس باستهلاك. وأما القسم الثاني وهو ما لو دفعها إليه ثلاث سنين ثم مات رب الأرض في الأولى قبل الحصاد يبقى الزرع حتى يستحصد استحساناً فإذا حصد ينفسخ في السنتين الباقيتين، ولو مات قبل الزرع بطلت المزارعة فإن مات بعد الزراعة قبل النبات اختلفوا فيه على نحو ما ذكرنا في الدين ولو مات المزارع والزرع بقل فقد قدمنا بيانه، وهذه فروع ذكرناها تتميماً للفائدة.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And it is rescinded by excuse like Muzara'ah, e.g., the worker being a thief or sick, unable to work, because it is in the meaning of leasing, and we have explained that it is rescinded by excuses. His being a thief is an obvious excuse because he steals fruit and palm leaves and causes harm to others. If the worker wants to leave work in the sound opinion, it is said possible and said not possible, by agreement. He said: The principle is that Muzara'ah is binding on the one who does not provide seed, not binding on the owner of the seed. Then its issues are of three types: a type regarding death, a type regarding rescission of his statement due to debt, and a type regarding expiry of the term. If one wants [from] whom the seed is from him before work, he does not have that unless he has a debt that cannot be paid except from it. If he sells it for the debt, nothing of the worker's expenses for digging rivers and repairing them is on him because benefits do not become a property except through contract or its like, and that was not found. When the seed is from him such that he is a lessee of the land, if the crop grows, it is not sold until it is harvested, but the judge removes it from seizure and does not obstruct between him and the creditors, because selling would nullify the worker's right, whereas delaying the sale postpones the creditor's right, and postponement is easier than nullification. If he sows and it does not grow, there is disagreement: it is said the landowner may sell it for the debt because the crop has no established right in the land, since casting seed is consumption; it is said he may not sell it because casting seed is not consumption. As for the second type: if he gave it to him for three years, then the landowner dies in the first year before harvest, the crop remains until it is harvested by istihsan; when harvested, it is rescinded for the remaining two years. If he dies before sowing, the Muzara'ah is void; if he dies after sowing but before germination, there is disagreement similar to what we mentioned about debt. If the sharecropper dies while the crop is still small, we have already explained. These are branches we mentioned to complete the benefit.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the commentary on the matn's statement about rescission by excuse. The author (Ibn Nujaym) quotes the matn and explains that a worker being a thief or sick constitutes a valid excuse to rescind the Masaqah contract because it is akin to a leasing contract (ijarah), which is rescinded by excuses. He notes disagreement on whether the worker may abandon work without excuse. Then he introduces a key principle: Muzara'ah (and by analogy Masaqah) is binding on the party who does not provide the seed (i.e., the worker if seed from owner, or owner if seed from worker) but not binding on the party who provides the seed. This contrasts with the general ruling. He then enumerates three categories of issues: (1) death, (2) rescission due to debt, and (3) expiry of term. The subsequent paragraphs discuss the debt scenario in detail: if the worker has debt, he may sell his share with permission; the worker's expenses for land improvements are not recoverable because benefits are not a property unless by contract. There is also a discussion on selling the crop when it has not sprouted, with two opinions. The second category covers death of the landowner at various stages, with rulings by istihsan. The passage ends by noting these are branches for benefit.

Key Terms
الفسخ بالعذر (al-faskh bi al-‘udhr): Termination of a contract due to a legitimate excuse that makes continuation harmful or impossible.
الأصل أن المزارعة لازمة من جهة من لا بذر منه غير لازمة من جهة رب البذر (al-aṣl anna al-muzāra‘ah lāzimah min jihat man lā badhr minhu ghayr lāzimah min jihat rabb al-badhr): The principle that Muzara'ah is binding on the party who does not provide seed (worker), but not binding on the seed provider (owner).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following excuses permits rescission of a Masaqah contract?
A) Worker's financial difficulty
B) Worker being a thief
C) Worker's lack of tools
D) Landowner's change of mind

Key Takeaway
Masaqah can be rescinded by valid excuses like theft or illness because it is analogous to ijarah, and the seed-provider is not bound by the contract before work begins.

Three Categories of Issues in Muzara'ah/Masaqah: Death, Debt, and Expiry
Detailed branches on death, debt, and expiry in Muzara'ah/Masaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize the issues arising in Muzara'ah/Masaqah into death, debt, and expiry, and apply the Hanafi rulings for each scenario, including the role of istihsan.

Core Idea
The rulings differ based on timing of death, debt status, and whether the crop has sprouted, with istihsan often protecting the worker's right.

After establishing the binding principle, the passage enumerates three categories of issues: death, debt, and expiry. It then provides detailed rulings for various sub-scenarios, often invoking istihsan to achieve fair outcomes. This lesson walks through each category, emphasizing the nuances when the seed provider or worker dies at different stages, how debt affects the right to sell, and what happens at term end.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage explicitly states: 'then its issues are of three types: a type regarding death, a type regarding rescission of his statement due to debt, and a type regarding expiry of the term.'
These categories cover the main contingencies in Muzara'ah/Masaqah.
2
Analyze the debt scenario
If the worker has debt, he may sell his share with permission from the judge. The landowner's expenses for improvements are not recoverable because benefits are not property without a contract. There is a dispute on selling the land when the crop hasn't grown.
This shows the interplay between debtor rights and contract obligations.
3
Analyze death scenarios
If the landowner dies before harvest, the crop remains until harvest by istihsan, then the contract rescinds for remaining years. If he dies before sowing, the contract is void. If after sowing but before germination, there is disagreement.
Istihsan overrides qiyas to protect the worker's labor.
4
Note the role of istihsan
In several rulings (e.g., landowner dies before harvest), the text says 'by istihsan' to justify keeping the crop for the worker. Recognize istihsan as a Hanafi source of law.
Istihsan balances equity with strict analogy.
5
Apply to expiry and other cases
The passage ends with branches about the worker dying while crop is small (already explained) and the expiry of term. Understand that these are applications of the same principles.
The three categories cover most contingencies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الأرض
الاستنماء
بالعقد أو شبهه ولم يوجد ذلك ومتى كان البذر من قبله بأن يكون مستأجراً للأرض فإن نبت الزرع لا يباع حتى يستحصد لكن القاضي يخرجه من الحبس ولا يحول بينه وبين الغرماء لأن في البيع إبطال حق العامل وفي ترك البيع تأخير حق رب الدين والتأخير أهون من الإبطال، فلو زرع ولم ينبت فقد اختلفوا فيه؛ قيل لصاحب الأرض بيعها بالدين لأنه ليس للزرع في الأرض حق قائم لأن القاء البذر استهلاك، وقيل ليس له البيع لأن القاء البذر من وليس باستهلاك. وأما القسم الثاني وهو ما لو دفعها إليه ثلاث سنين ثم مات رب الأرض في الأولى قبل الحصاد يبقى الزرع حتى يستحصد استحساناً فإذا حصد ينفسخ في السنتين الباقيتين، ولو مات قبل الزرع بطلت المزارعة فإن مات بعد الزراعة قبل النبات اختلفوا فيه على نحو ما ذكرنا في الدين ولو مات المزارع والزرع بقل فقد قدمنا بيانه، وهذه فروع ذكرناها تتميماً للفائدة.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And it is rescinded by excuse like Muzara'ah, e.g., the worker being a thief or sick, unable to work, because it is in the meaning of leasing, and we have explained that it is rescinded by excuses. His being a thief is an obvious excuse because he steals fruit and palm leaves and causes harm to others. If the worker wants to leave work in the sound opinion, it is said possible and said not possible, by agreement. He said: The principle is that Muzara'ah is binding on the one who does not provide seed, not binding on the owner of the seed. Then its issues are of three types: a type regarding death, a type regarding rescission of his statement due to debt, and a type regarding expiry of the term. If one wants [from] whom the seed is from him before work, he does not have that unless he has a debt that cannot be paid except from it. If he sells it for the debt, nothing of the worker's expenses for digging rivers and repairing them is on him because benefits do not become a property except through contract or its like, and that was not found. When the seed is from him such that he is a lessee of the land, if the crop grows, it is not sold until it is harvested, but the judge removes it from seizure and does not obstruct between him and the creditors, because selling would nullify the worker's right, whereas delaying the sale postpones the creditor's right, and postponement is easier than nullification. If he sows and it does not grow, there is disagreement: it is said the landowner may sell it for the debt because the crop has no established right in the land, since casting seed is consumption; it is said he may not sell it because casting seed is not consumption. As for the second type: if he gave it to him for three years, then the landowner dies in the first year before harvest, the crop remains until it is harvested by istihsan; when harvested, it is rescinded for the remaining two years. If he dies before sowing, the Muzara'ah is void; if he dies after sowing but before germination, there is disagreement similar to what we mentioned about debt. If the sharecropper dies while the crop is still small, we have already explained. These are branches we mentioned to complete the benefit.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the commentary on the matn's statement about rescission by excuse. The author (Ibn Nujaym) quotes the matn and explains that a worker being a thief or sick constitutes a valid excuse to rescind the Masaqah contract because it is akin to a leasing contract (ijarah), which is rescinded by excuses. He notes disagreement on whether the worker may abandon work without excuse. Then he introduces a key principle: Muzara'ah (and by analogy Masaqah) is binding on the party who does not provide the seed (i.e., the worker if seed from owner, or owner if seed from worker) but not binding on the party who provides the seed. This contrasts with the general ruling. He then enumerates three categories of issues: (1) death, (2) rescission due to debt, and (3) expiry of term. The subsequent paragraphs discuss the debt scenario in detail: if the worker has debt, he may sell his share with permission; the worker's expenses for land improvements are not recoverable because benefits are not a property unless by contract. There is also a discussion on selling the crop when it has not sprouted, with two opinions. The second category covers death of the landowner at various stages, with rulings by istihsan. The passage ends by noting these are branches for benefit.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from qiyas (analogy) for a stronger evidence or equity consideration.
القاء البذر استهلاك (ilqā' al-badhr istihlāk): The act of casting seed is considered consumption, therefore the crop has no established right in the land before germination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the crop if the landowner dies before harvest in the first year of a three-year Muzara'ah contract?
A) The crop is destroyed
B) The crop is left to rot
C) The crop remains until harvest by istihsan
D) The contract is void immediately

Key Takeaway
In Muzara'ah/Masaqah, death, debt, and expiry scenarios have nuanced rulings that often employ istihsan to balance the rights of the parties.

Rulings on Debt and Death in Muzara'ah
Explains subsidiary rulings on debt, seed, and death in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each scenario concerning debt, seed failure, and death of parties in a muzara'ah contract, and explain the role of istihsan in delaying the sale of the crop.

Core Idea
Delay is easier than annulment: the worker's right to the crop protects it from immediate sale for the landowner's debt.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents several important subsidiary rulings (furu') in the contract of muzara'ah. These scenarios involve the interaction of the sharecropping contract with the landowner's debts, the failure of the seed, and the death of either party. Understanding these rulings helps clarify how istihsan (juristic preference) is applied to balance the rights of the worker, the landowner, and the creditors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key variables
The passage discusses three main situations: (1) seed from worker and landowner's debt with growing crop, (2) seed failure, and (3) death of landowner or worker at different stages. List each scenario.
These are subsidiary branches (furu') derived from the main rulings of muzara'ah.
2
Analyze the ruling for growing crop with debt
When the seed is from the worker and the crop grows, the crop cannot be sold until it ripens because the worker has a right. The judge removes the lien and delays the creditors. This is by istihsan: delay is easier than annulment.
The worker's right to the crop is ongoing; selling would annul it (ibṭāl ḥaqq al-'āmil).
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf on seed failure
If the seed fails to grow, there is a difference of opinion. One view considers casting seed as consumption (istihlāk), so the landowner can sell the land for the debt. Another view disagrees, saying it is not consumption.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the passage does not settle which is preferred.
4
Analyze rulings on death of the landowner
If the landowner dies after sowing but before harvest (for a multi-year contract), the crop remains until it ripens by istihsan, then the contract terminates for the remaining years. If he dies before sowing, the contract is void ab initio. If he dies after sowing but before growth, there is ikhtilaf similar to the debt case.
The timing of death relative to sowing is critical.
5
Analyze the ruling on death of the worker
The passage notes that the ruling for the worker's death (when the crop is green) has been explained earlier. This branches are presented to complete the benefit.
The focus is on the landowner's death; the worker's death is referenced for completeness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المساقاة الأرض الاستنماء بالعقد أو شبهه ولم يوجد ذلك ومتى كان البذر من قبله بأن يكون مستأجراً للأرض فإن نبت الزرع لا يباع حتى يستحصد لكن القاضي يخرجه من الحبس ولا يحول بينه وبين الغرماء لأن في البيع إبطال حق العامل وفي ترك البيع تأخير حق رب الدين والتأخير أهون من الإبطال، فلو زرع ولم ينبت فقد اختلفوا فيه؛ قيل لصاحب الأرض بيعها بالدين لأنه ليس للزرع في الأرض حق قائم لأن القاء البذر استهلاك، وقيل ليس له البيع لأن القاء البذر من وليس باستهلاك. وأما القسم الثاني وهو ما لو دفعها إليه ثلاث سنين ثم مات رب الأرض في الأولى قبل الحصاد يبقى الزرع حتى يستحصد استحساناً فإذا حصد ينفسخ في السنتين الباقيتين، ولو مات قبل الزرع بطلت المزارعة فإن مات بعد الزراعة قبل النبات اختلفوا فيه على نحو ما ذكرنا في الدين ولو مات المزارع والزرع بقل فقد قدمنا بيانه، وهذه فروع ذكرناها تتميماً للفائدة.
Book of Sharecropping: The land: growth through contract or its like, and that does not exist. And whenever the seed is from him, meaning the worker, then if the crop grows, it is not sold until it ripens, but the judge removes it from the lien and does not prevent the creditors, because in selling there is annulment of the worker's right, and in leaving the sale there is delay of the debt-owner's right, and delay is easier than annulment. If he sowed and it did not grow, they differed: it is said the landowner may sell the land for the debt because the crop has no established right in the land since casting the seed is consumption; and it is said he may not sell because casting the seed is not consumption. As for the second type, that he gave it to him for three years, then the landowner died in the first year before harvest: the crop remains until it ripens by istihsan; when harvested, the contract is annulled for the remaining two years. If he died before sowing, the muzara'ah is void. If he died after sowing but before growth, they differed similarly to what we mentioned regarding debt. And if the sharecropper died while the crop was green, we have already explained it. These are branches we mentioned to complete the benefit.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses subsidiary rulings in muzara'ah (sharecropping). The author first addresses a scenario where the landowner has debts and the seed comes from the worker. If the crop grows, it cannot be sold to pay the debt until it ripens because the worker has a right. The judge can remove the lien on the crop to protect the worker's right, but the creditor's right is merely delayed. If the crop fails to grow, there is a difference of opinion: one view likens seeding to consumption, so the landowner can sell the land; another view disagrees. Next, if the landowner dies mid-contract after sowing, the crop is left to ripen by istihsan, then the contract ends for the remaining years. If the landowner dies before sowing, the contract is void. Similar ikhtilaf applies for death after sowing but before growth. These are detailed branches to clarify the rulings.

Key Terms
الاستنماء (al-istinma'): The growth or development of crops through a contract or similar arrangement.
المزارعة (al-muzara'ah): A contract of sharecropping where one provides land and the other works it, with the crop shared.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to derive a ruling that departs from qiyas for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the landowner dies after the crop is sown but before harvest, what happens to the crop?
A) It is immediately taken by creditors
B) It remains until it ripens, then the contract ends
C) The worker takes it all
D) The contract is void

Key Takeaway
In muzara'ah, the worker's right to the crop overrides immediate debt collection, and death after sowing preserves the crop until ripening by istihsan.
