Examples of Fasid Contracts in Muzara'ah and Mu'amalah
Specific examples of invalid conditions and their correction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whether a muzara'ah or mu'amalah contract is fasid given specific invalid conditions and determine the correct distribution of output and compensation.

Core Idea
Stipulating shared ownership of land or fixed payment alongside output makes the contract fasid.

The text presents three concrete scenarios where conditions invalidate a sharecropping or tree tenancy contract. By analyzing these examples, you will learn the key principles that distinguish a valid contract from a corrupt one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type and condition
Read each scenario and note whether it is muzara'ah or mu'amalah. Identify the specific condition that is being challenged.
The first example involves sharing the land itself, not just the produce.
2
Determine if the condition violates the nature of the contract
Check if the condition undermines the equal sharing of output or introduces a fixed payment. Such conditions are invalid.
Sharing the land (not just produce) is invalid because the land is not subject to sharing.
3
State the ruling: fasid
Conclude that the contract is corrupt (fasid). In Hanafi fiqh, fasid means the contract is not entirely void but requires correction.
The contract is not batil; it can be rectified by removing the invalid condition.
4
Apply the correction for a fasid contract
The output goes to the owner of the seed/plants (or land if seed is from landowner), and the other party receives compensation (ajr al-mithl or rent).
The planter gets the wage of his work; the landowner gets rent of his land; output goes to the one whose seed was used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو دفع أرضاً بيضاء على أن يغرس فيها نخلاً وشجراً على أن ما خرج من شجر أو نخل فهو بينهما نصفين وعلى أن الأرض بينهما نصفين فهذا فساد، فإن فعل فما خرج من الأرض فجميعه لرب الأرض وللغارس أجر مثل عمله. دفع أرضاً على أن يغرسها المدفوع إليه لنفسه ما بدا له ويزرعها من عنده ما بدا له على أن الخارج نصفان بينهما وللعامل على رب الأرض مائة درهم فهو فاسد والخارج للغارس ولرب الأرض أجر أرضه، ولو كان البذر والغراس من رب على أن يغرس ويبذرهما بهما والخارج نصفان بينهما ولرب الأرض علي العامل مائة درهم فهو فاسد والخارج لرب الأرض وللعامل أجر مثله وتوجيهه يطلب من المحيط. واشتراط العمل في المعاملة والمزارعة على أقسام : أحدها أن يشترطا البعض على العامل وسكتا عن الباقي أو شرطا بعضه على الدافع وسكتا من الباقي أو شرطا بعضه على الدافع وبعضه على العامل وكل قسم على قسمين: الأول لو شرطا البعض على العامل وسكتا من الباقي فإن كان المسكوت عنه لا يخرج من ذلك شيء إلا به أو يخرج شيء لا يرغب في مثله فالمعاملة فاسدة، والثاني لو شرطا على نفسه السقي والحفظ لا غير فالمزارعة فاسدة إلا إذا علم أن السقي لا يزيد فيه الثالث لو شرط السقي على رب النخل والحفظ والتلقيح على العامل لم يجز، والمزارعة كالمعاملة في هذه الأحكام إذا كان البذر من رب الأرض وتوجيهه يطلب من المحيط .
And if he gave white land on the condition that he plant dates and trees, and that whatever comes out of trees or dates is half between them, and that the land is half between them, this is corrupt. If he did it, then whatever comes out of the land is all for the landowner, and the planter has the wage of his work. He gave land on condition that the recipient plant for himself whatever he wishes and sow from himself whatever he wishes, on condition that the output is half between them, and the worker has against the landowner one hundred dirhams: this is corrupt, the output is for the planter, and the landowner has the rent of his land. And if the seed and planting were from the owner on condition that he plant and sow them, and the output is half between them, and the landowner has against the worker one hundred dirhams: this is corrupt, the output is for the landowner, and the worker has the wage of his work. Its reasoning is sought from al-Muhit. And stipulating work in mu'amalah and muzara'ah: it has categories: one is that they stipulate some work on the worker and remain silent about the rest, or stipulate some on the payer and remain silent about the rest, or stipulate some on the payer and some on the worker. Each category has two divisions: the first, if they stipulate some work on the worker and remain silent about the rest: then if the unmentioned work cannot produce anything without it, or produces something undesirable, then the mu'amalah is corrupt. The second: if they stipulate on themselves watering and guarding only, then the muzara'ah is corrupt, unless it is known that watering does not increase it. The third: if he stipulates watering on the owner of the palms, and guarding and pollination on the worker, it is not permissible. And muzara'ah is like mu'amalah in these rulings if the seed is from the landowner. Its reasoning is sought from al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This section presents specific examples of corrupt (fasid) contracts in sharecropping and tree tenancy. The author lists conditions that invalidate the contract, such as stipulating that the land itself be shared (not just the produce), or adding a fixed payment alongside the share. The correct rule is that the output belongs to the one whose seed and planting were used, and the other party gets compensation. Then the author categorizes stipulations of work: if the contract is silent on some essential work, the contract becomes fasid unless the omitted work is insignificant. For example, if only watering and guarding are stipulated, it is fasid because other work like pollination is needed. If the landowner stipulates watering and the worker pollination, it is also fasid. Muzara'ah follows the same rules as mu'amalah when the seed is from the landowner. The full reasoning is in al-Muhit.

Key Terms
فساد (fasad): Corruption of a contract due to invalid conditions; the contract is not entirely void but must be rectified.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The standard market wage for similar work.
المعاملة (al-mu'amalah): A contract of tree tenancy similar to muzara'ah but for trees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the seed is from the owner and a fixed payment is demanded from the worker, to whom does the output belong?
A) The worker
B) The landowner
C) Shared equally
D) Given to charity

Key Takeaway
Any condition that distorts the sharing of produce or adds a guaranteed payment makes the contract fasid; the output goes to the owner of the seed/land, and the other party receives compensation.

Classification of Work Conditions in Muzara'ah and Mu'amalah
Systematic classification of work stipulations and their effect on validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify work conditions in muzara'ah and mu'amalah contracts as leading to validity or fasid based on whether essential work is assigned or trivial.

Core Idea
Stipulating only trivial work or leaving essential work unassigned makes the contract corrupt.

This part of the text provides a systematic classification of how stipulations of work affect the validity of sharecropping and tree tenancy contracts. Understanding this helps avoid common pitfalls when drafting such agreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of work stipulation
Determine whether the work is stipulated on the worker, on the payer (landowner), or on both, and what is left unspecified (sukut).
There are three broad categories based on who bears the stipulated work.
2
Check the nature of the unassigned work
If the unmentioned work is essential for production (e.g., planting, watering) or produces output that no one would accept, the contract is fasid.
Essential work that is not stipulated means the contract is incomplete.
3
Evaluate the specific examples given
Apply the rule: if only watering and guarding are stipulated, it's fasid unless watering does not increase output. If watering is on the landowner and pollination on the worker, it's fasid.
The third example: watering by landowner, pollination by worker – this splits essential work in a way that creates uncertainty.
4
Apply the same rules to muzara'ah and mu'amalah
The rulings for mu'amalah apply to muzara'ah when the seed is from the landowner.
This ensures consistency across both contract types.

Combining Muzara'ah and Mu'amalah in One Contract
Ruling on a contract that combines sharecropping and tree tenancy with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a combined muzara'ah and mu'amalah contract based on seed ownership, and apply the rules for subleasing without permission.

Core Idea
A combined contract is valid only if seed is from the landowner; if from worker, it is corrupt.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a common scenario: a landowner with palms wants a worker to both cultivate annual crops and tend the trees. The ruling splits based on who provides the seed for the crops. Furthermore, if the worker tries to sublease the land or trees without permission, different consequences follow. Understanding these rules protects both parties and clarifies liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the combined contract and its condition
The contract includes both muzara'ah (sharecropping for annuals) and mu'amalah (tree tenancy). The key condition is who provides the seed for the crops.
Seed ownership is the decisive factor.
2
Determine validity based on seed ownership
If seed is from the worker, the contract is fasid (corrupt) because it bundles two separate contracts. If seed is from the landowner, it is sahih (valid) as a single hire agreement.
The reasoning is from al-Muhit.
3
Analyze subleasing scenarios
If seed is from the landowner, the worker cannot sublease without permission; unauthorized sublease makes him a usurper (ghasib) and voids the original contract. If seed is from the worker, he may sublease even without permission (per Fatawa al-Khulasa).
The default rule is that permission is required when the landowner provides seed.
4
Recognize consequences of unauthorized subleasing
When the worker subleases without permission, the landowner can claim rent (ujrat al-ard) from either the original worker or the subtenant. The subtenant can recover from the original worker due to deception (ghurur).
This establishes liability and prevents unjust enrichment.
5
Understand the exception in Fatawa al-Khulasa
If seed is from the worker, the worker may sublease even without the landowner's permission. The relationship becomes akin to a corrupt lease (ijarah fasidah).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the later fatwa authority (al-Fatawa al-Kubra) follows the stricter rule when seed is from the landowner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المزارعة إذا شرط فيها المعاملة فالمعاملة متى شرطت في المزارعة بأن دفع أرضاً فيها نخل على أن يزرعها من بذره بالنصف وعلى أن يعمل في النخل ويسقيه ويلحقه بالنصف فإنه ينظر؛ إن كان البذر من قبل العامل فسدت لأنهما عقدان اشترط أحدهما في الآخر، وإن كان البذر من قبل رب الأرض جاز لأنه عقد واحد لأنه استأجره ليعمل في أرضه ونخله وتوجيهه يطلب من المحيط. وأما لو دفع المزارع أو العامل الأرض أو النخل لغيره مزارعة أو معاملة فهي على وجهين: إما أن يكون البذر من قبل رب الأرض وفي هذا لا يملك أن يدفع الأرض مزارعة أو معاملة إلا أن يأذن له رب البذر في ذلك أو يقول له اعمل برأيك ولكن له أن يستأجر أجيرا من لإقامة عمل المزارعة، وإن قال رب البذر اعمل الله تعالى برأيك جاز له أن يدفعها لغيره مزارعة، وإذا لم يأذن له ولم يقل اعمل برأيك فدفعها لغيره مزارعة فصار مخالفاً غاصباً وبطلت المزارعة بينه وبين رب الأرض ولرب الأرض أن يضمن أيهما شاء أجرة الأرض، فإذا ضمن الأول لم يرجع على صاحبه، وإن ضمن الثاني رجع على الأول لأنه مغرور من جهته؛ كذا الفتاوى الكبرى. وأما لو أذن له رب الأرض أو قال له اعمل برأيك فدفعها جاز، وإن كان رب الأرض شرط للمزارع النصف فدفعها للثاني بالنصف فمهما خرج منها فنصفه لرب الأرض ونصفه للمزارع الثاني، وإن شرط المزارع الأول للثاني الربع وللأول الربع وحكمهما حكم المضاربة . وفي فتاوى الخلاصة : وإن كان البذر من قبل العامل له أن يدفع إلى آخر مزارعة وإن لم يأذن له رب الأرض أصلاً، ولو دفع صار الزارع الأول مؤجراً ما إذا استأجره إجارة فاسدة صار الأول مستأجراً للمزارع الثاني ببعض الخارج ويعمل في الأرض .اهـ.
As for muzara'ah when mu'amalah is stipulated in it: mu'amalah whenever stipulated in muzara'ah – such as giving land containing palms on condition that he sow it with his seed for half, and that he work on the palms, water them, and pollinate them for half – then it is considered: if the seed is from the worker, it is corrupt because they are two contracts one stipulated in the other. If the seed is from the landowner, it is permissible because it is one contract – he hired him to work in his land and his palms. Its reasoning is sought from al-Muhit. As for if the sharecropper or the worker gave the land or palms to someone else for muzara'ah or mu'amalah, it is of two types: either the seed is from the landowner; in this case he does not have the right to give the land for muzara'ah or mu'amalah unless the owner of the seed permits him or says 'act on your own opinion.' But he may hire a laborer to perform the work of muzara'ah. If the owner of the seed says 'act on your own opinion,' he may give it to someone else for muzara'ah. If he did not permit him and did not say 'act on your opinion,' and he gave it to someone else for muzara'ah, he becomes a transgressor and usurper, and the muzara'ah between him and the landowner is void. The landowner may claim the rent of the land from whichever he wishes. If he claims from the first, he cannot recover from his partner; if he claims from the second, he can recover from the first because he was deceived by him. This is in al-Fatawa al-Kubra. As for if the landowner permitted him or said 'act on your opinion,' and he gave it, it is permissible. If the landowner stipulated half for the sharecropper, and he gave it to the second for half, then whatever comes out, half is for the landowner and half for the second sharecropper. If the first sharecropper stipulated for the second a quarter and for himself a quarter, their ruling is like mudarabah. In Fatawa al-Khulasa: If the seed is from the worker, he may give it to another for muzara'ah even if the landowner did not permit at all. If he gave, the first farmer becomes a lessor? When he hires him with a corrupt lease, the first becomes a lessee of the second sharecropper with some of the output and works in the land. End.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage addresses compound contracts combining muzara'ah (sharecropping for annual crops) and mu'amalah (tree tenancy). If the seed is from the worker, the contract is fasid because it bundles two separate contracts. If seed is from the landowner, it is valid as a single hiring. The discussion then shifts to subleasing or transferring the contract to a third party. If the seed is from the landowner, the worker cannot sublease without permission; if he does, he becomes a usurper. The landowner can recover rent from either the first or second party. If the landowner permits, subleasing is valid. The rules differ when the seed is from the worker: he may sublease without permission. The Fatawa al-Khulasa clarifies that the first worker becomes a lessor in a corrupt lease. These detailed rules prevent exploitation and define liability.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A profit-sharing partnership in trade; here analogized for the distribution of output in a sub-muzara'ah.
غاصب (ghasib): A usurper who takes property without right; here the worker who subleases without permission becomes a usurper.
مغرور (maghrur): One who is deceived; the second party is considered deceived by the first, allowing recourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a combined muzara'ah and mu'amalah contract, what happens when the worker subleases the land without permission of the landowner, and the seed was provided by the landowner?
A) The sublease is valid, and the original contract continues.
B) The worker becomes a usurper, and the original contract is void.
C) The landowner must accept the sublease.
D) The worker is not liable for any rent.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a combined muzara'ah and mu'amalah contract, and the permissibility of subleasing, both depend critically on who provides the seed.

Rulings on Landowner's Work in Muzara'ah
Detailed scenarios of landowner's work in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each scenario when a landowner works on the crop without the worker's permission, and distinguish between the qiyas and istihsan outcomes.

Core Idea
The landowner who works without permission is a volunteer; output stays on the condition unless qiyas transfers it.

This passage from al-Muhit details several scenarios where the landowner performs agricultural work on the muzara'ah crop. The key principle is that the landowner's work is voluntary (tatawwu'), and the output generally follows the original contract terms. However, in cases where the worker neglects his duties, a difference arises between qiyas and istihsan. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify seed ownership
First, determine whether the seed belongs to the landowner or the worker. This is the primary factor in many rulings.
2
Identify the worker's action
Check whether the worker performed his duties (sowing, watering) or neglected them. The landowner's intervention is often a response to neglect.
3
Apply the general rule: landowner as volunteer
In most cases, the landowner's work is voluntary, and the output is distributed according to the original contract (condition). The landowner is like a third party.
4
Note the qiyas vs istihsan exception
When the worker fails to water and the landowner does so, qiyas gives the entire output to the landowner, but istihsan keeps it on the condition. Recognize this difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : إذا عمل صاحب الأرض مع العامل بأمره أو بغير أمره فهو على قسمين: إما أن يكون البذر من قبل رب الأرض أو من قبل العامل، فلو كان من قبل رب الأرض بأن دفع أرضه وبذره مزارعة بالنصف فزرع العامل وسقى فلما نبت قام عليه رب الأرض حتى استحصد بغير أمر العامل فالخارج على الشرط ورب الأرض متطوع بعمله كما لو قام عليه أجنبي، ولو بذر المزارع ولم ينبت ولم يسقه فسقاه رب الأرض وقام عليه حتى استحصد فالخارج لرب الأرض قياساً، وفي الاستحسان على الشروط ورب الأرض متطوع كما لو قام عليه أجنبي، ولو لم يزرع العامل حتى زرعه رب الأرض وسقاه ثم قام عليه المزارع حتى استحصد فالخارج لرب الأرض والمزارع متطوع، وإن بذره رب الأرض بغير إذن الزارع ولم يسقه ولم ينبت المزارع وقام عليه حتى استحصد فالخارج على الشرط القسم الثاني لو كان البذر من قبل المزارع فبذر ولم يسقه ولم ينبت فقام عليه رب الأرض حتى استحصد فالخارج بينهما، وكذا لو بذره رب الأرض ولم ينبت ولم يسقه حتى قام عليه المزارع فالخارج على الشرط، ولو كان رب الأرض سقاه حتى نبت ثم قام عليه المزارع وسقاه فهو لرب الأرض ويضمن البذر لربه والمزارع متطوع في سقيه، وما علمته من الجواب في المزارعة فهو الجواب في المعاملة؛ كذا في المحيط. وأما لو اختلفا في المزارعة أو المعاملة فلا يخلو إما أن يختلفا في العقد أو الشروط أو في جواز العقد وفساده فلو اتفقا على جواز واختلفا في المشروط والبذر من قبل رب إن كان قبل المزارعة وأقاما بينة فبينة الزارع أولى لأنها أكثر إثباتاً، وإن لم تقم لأحدهما الأرض بينة تحالفا وتراد، وإن اختلفا بعد الزراعة والنبات فالقول لرب الأرض مع يمينه والبينة للآخر، وإن كان البذر من قبل العامل فالقول له والبيئة للآخر بعد عقد المزارعة وقبلها
And in al-Muhit: If the landowner works with the worker by his command or without, it is of two types: either the seed is from the landowner or from the worker. If from the landowner – that is, he gave his land and seed for muzara'ah for half, then the worker sowed and watered, and when it grew, the landowner tended it until harvest without the worker's order – the output is on the condition, and the landowner is a volunteer in his work, just as if an outsider had tended it. If the sharecropper sowed but it did not grow and he did not water it, then the landowner watered it and tended it until harvest, then the output is for the landowner by qiyas; by istihsan it is on the condition, and the landowner is a volunteer like an outsider. If the worker did not sow until the landowner sowed and watered it, then the sharecropper tended it until harvest, then the output is for the landowner, and the sharecropper is a volunteer. If the landowner sowed without the worker's permission and did not water, and the worker did not sow, and then the landowner tended it until harvest, then the output is on the condition. The second type: if the seed was from the worker, and he sowed but did not water and it did not grow, then the landowner tended it until harvest, then the output is between them. Similarly, if the landowner sowed it and it did not grow and did not water, until the worker tended it, then the output is on the condition. If the landowner watered it until it grew, then the worker tended it and watered it, then it is for the landowner, and he guarantees the seed to its owner, and the worker is a volunteer in his watering. And whatever ruling you know in muzara'ah, the same is the ruling in mu'amalah; thus in al-Muhit. As for if they dispute in muzara'ah or mu'amalah, it is either about the contract, the conditions, or the validity or corruption. If they agree on validity but differ on the condition, and the seed is from the landowner, and if before muzara'ah they produce evidence, the worker's evidence is preferable because it is more confirmatory. If neither has evidence, they take oaths and return (the contract). If they differ after sowing and growth, the landowner's statement is taken with his oath, and the other has the evidence. If the seed was from the worker, his statement is taken and the other has the evidence. After the muzara'ah contract and before it...
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This final passage from al-Muhit and the author's own words deal with two scenarios: (1) when the landowner performs work on the crop without the worker's request, and (2) how to settle disputes. In the first scenario, if the seed is from the landowner, the landowner's work is generally considered voluntary (tatawwu'), and the output still follows the original condition, except in some cases where qiyas and istihsan differ. For example, if the worker fails to water and the landowner does so, by qiyas the output goes to the landowner, but by istihsan it stays on the condition. The landowner is treated like a third party. If the seed is from the worker, and the landowner tends the crop, the output is shared. In disputes, the rules of evidence depend on the timing of the dispute and who owns the seed. If they dispute before planting and the seed is from the landowner, the worker's evidence is preferred; if after planting, the landowner's word with oath is taken. If the seed is from the worker, his word is taken. The text ends abruptly, likely a continuation in the original.

Key Terms
متطوع (mutatawwi'): A volunteer who works without expecting compensation; here the landowner is considered a volunteer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the seed is from the landowner and the worker fails to water, and the landowner waters and tends the crop, what is the ruling by istihsan?
A) The output is entirely for the landowner
B) The output is shared according to the contract condition
C) The output is entirely for the worker
D) The contract is voided

Key Takeaway
The landowner's voluntary work does not alter the contract's output distribution, except by qiyas in specific negligence cases, but istihsan retains the original terms.

Resolving Disputes in Muzara'ah and Mu'amalah
Rules for resolving disputes in muzara'ah and mu'amalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of evidence and oath-taking to resolve disputes in muzara'ah and mu'amalah contracts.

Core Idea
In disputes, whose word is taken depends on seed ownership and timing; evidence rules shift accordingly.

This passage outlines the procedural rules for when parties in a muzara'ah or mu'amalah contract disagree. The key is to determine who owns the seed and when the dispute occurs. The rules of evidence (bayyinah) and mutual oath-taking (tahaluf) are applied accordingly. Understanding these rules is essential for a mufti or judge to resolve contractual disputes equitably.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of dispute
Is the dispute about the contract itself, its conditions, or its validity? The text categorizes these.
2
Determine seed ownership
The ruling on who has the statement (qawl) and evidence depends on whether the seed is from the landowner or the worker.
3
Determine timing of dispute
Disputes before sowing/planting are treated differently from disputes after planting and growth.
4
Apply the evidence rule
If both provide evidence, the worker's evidence is preferable when seed from landowner and dispute before planting. If no evidence, they take oaths and rescind. After planting, the landowner's statement is taken with his oath, and the other must provide evidence.
5
Reverse rule when seed from worker
If seed is from the worker, his statement is taken and the other must provide evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : إذا عمل صاحب الأرض مع العامل بأمره أو بغير أمره فهو على قسمين: إما أن يكون البذر من قبل رب الأرض أو من قبل العامل، فلو كان من قبل رب الأرض بأن دفع أرضه وبذره مزارعة بالنصف فزرع العامل وسقى فلما نبت قام عليه رب الأرض حتى استحصد بغير أمر العامل فالخارج على الشرط ورب الأرض متطوع بعمله كما لو قام عليه أجنبي، ولو بذر المزارع ولم ينبت ولم يسقه فسقاه رب الأرض وقام عليه حتى استحصد فالخارج لرب الأرض قياساً، وفي الاستحسان على الشروط ورب الأرض متطوع كما لو قام عليه أجنبي، ولو لم يزرع العامل حتى زرعه رب الأرض وسقاه ثم قام عليه المزارع حتى استحصد فالخارج لرب الأرض والمزارع متطوع، وإن بذره رب الأرض بغير إذن الزارع ولم يسقه ولم ينبت المزارع وقام عليه حتى استحصد فالخارج على الشرط القسم الثاني لو كان البذر من قبل المزارع فبذر ولم يسقه ولم ينبت فقام عليه رب الأرض حتى استحصد فالخارج بينهما، وكذا لو بذره رب الأرض ولم ينبت ولم يسقه حتى قام عليه المزارع فالخارج على الشرط، ولو كان رب الأرض سقاه حتى نبت ثم قام عليه المزارع وسقاه فهو لرب الأرض ويضمن البذر لربه والمزارع متطوع في سقيه، وما علمته من الجواب في المزارعة فهو الجواب في المعاملة؛ كذا في المحيط. وأما لو اختلفا في المزارعة أو المعاملة فلا يخلو إما أن يختلفا في العقد أو الشروط أو في جواز العقد وفساده فلو اتفقا على جواز واختلفا في المشروط والبذر من قبل رب إن كان قبل المزارعة وأقاما بينة فبينة الزارع أولى لأنها أكثر إثباتاً، وإن لم تقم لأحدهما الأرض بينة تحالفا وتراد، وإن اختلفا بعد الزراعة والنبات فالقول لرب الأرض مع يمينه والبينة للآخر، وإن كان البذر من قبل العامل فالقول له والبيئة للآخر بعد عقد المزارعة وقبلها

Key Terms
التحالف (al-tahaluf): Mutual oath-taking by both parties when evidence is lacking; followed by rescission of contract.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Evidence, typically witness testimony; the rule of preference depends on the case.

Delegation of Muraba'ah by the Worker: Permission and Seed Ownership
Rulings on worker delegating muraba'ah contract with and without permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a muraba'ah worker delegates the work to another, distinguishing cases based on whether the seed belongs to the landowner or the worker and whether the landowner permitted delegation.

Core Idea
Without permission, delegation voids the contract and the worker becomes a usurper; but if the seed is from the worker, delegation is allowed even without permission.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with a common scenario in sharecropping: can the worker (muzari') sub-contract the work to someone else? The answer depends on whether the landowner permitted delegation, and crucially, on who owns the seed. The text presents clear rulings with practical consequences for contract validity and liability for the land's rent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seed owner
The first condition to determine is who provided the seed. The text treats two scenarios: seed from landowner and seed from worker. This foundational fact changes the ruling significantly.
The default assumption in the first part is seed from landowner.
2
Assess permission status (if seed from landowner)
If the seed belongs to the landowner, check whether the landowner gave permission to delegate. Permission can be explicit or by saying 'act according to your opinion'.
Without permission, the worker becomes a violator and usurper.
3
Determine ruling for seed-from-landowner scenario
Without permission: the original muraba'ah contract becomes void (batil), the worker is a usurper (ghasib), and the landowner can claim rent from either the worker or the delegate. With permission: delegation is valid, and the produce is shared according to the agreement.
Liability details: if landowner recovers from worker, no recourse; if from delegate, delegate recourses against worker.
4
Determine ruling for seed-from-worker scenario
If the seed is from the worker, delegation is allowed even without the landowner's permission. However, the arrangement is treated as a void lease (ijarah fasidah) rather than muraba'ah.
This is based on Fatawa al-Khulasah.
5
Apply liability rules
In the no-permission case with seed from landowner, the landowner may claim rent from either the original worker or the delegate. If from the original worker, no recourse; if from the delegate, the delegate can recover from the original worker because he was deceived.
The principle of 'maghrur' (deceived) applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المساقاة مال له يأذن له رب البذر في ذلك أو يقول له اعمل برأيك ولكن له أن يستأجر أجبرا من لإقامة عمل المزارعة، وإن قال رب البذر اعمل الله تعالى برأيك جاز له أن يدفعها لغيره مزارعة، وإذا لم يأذن له ولم يقل اعمل برأيك فدفعها لغيره مزارعة فصار مخالفاً غاصباً وبطلت المزارعة بينه وبين رب الأرض ولرب الأرض أن يضمن أيهما شاء أجرة الأرض، فإذا ضمن الأول لم يرجع على صاحبه، وإن ضمن الثاني رجع على الأول لأنه مغرور من جهته ؛ كذا الفتاوى الكبرى. في وأما لو أذن له رب الأرض أو قال له اعمل برأيك فدفعها جاز، وإن كان رب الأرض شرط للمزارع النصف فدفعها للثاني بالنصف فمهما خرج منها فنصفه لرب الأرض ونصفه للمزارع الثاني، وإن شرط المزارع الأول للثاني الربع وللأول الربع وحكمهما حكم المضاربة . وفي فتاوى الخلاصة : وإن كان البذر من قبل العامل له أن يدفع إلى آخر مزارعة وإن لم يأذن له رب الأرض أصلاً، ولو دفع صار الزارع الأول مؤجراً ما إذا استأجره إجارة فاسدة صار الأول مستأجراً للمزارع الثاني ببعض الخارج ويعمل في الأرض .اهـ.
Book of Musaqah. What? The owner of the seed permits him in that or says to him: act according to your opinion, but he has the right to hire a worker to carry out the work of muraba'ah. If the owner of the seed says: act according to your opinion, it is permissible for him to give it to another as muraba'ah. If he does not permit him and does not say act according to your opinion, and he gives it to another as muraba'ah, then he becomes a violator and usurper, and the muraba'ah is void between him and the landowner, and the landowner has the right to hold either of them liable for the rent of the land. If he holds the first liable, he does not recourse against his companion; if he holds the second liable, he recourses against the first because he was deceived by him. Thus in al-Fatawa al-Kubra. As for if the landowner permits him or says act according to your opinion, and he gives it, it is permissible. If the landowner stipulated half for the muraba'ah worker and he gave it to the second for half, then whatever comes out, half belongs to the landowner and half to the second muraba'ah worker. If the first muraba'ah worker stipulated a quarter for the second and a quarter for the first, their ruling is like mudarabah. And in Fatawa al-Khulasah: If the seed was from the worker, he has the right to give it to another as muraba'ah even if the landowner did not permit him at all. If he gave it, the first farmer becomes a lessor; if he hired him with a void lease, the first becomes a lessee of the second farmer for part of the produce and he works in the land. End.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the delegation of a muraba'ah contract by the worker (muzari'). The text opens with the scenario where the seed belongs to the landowner. If the landowner explicitly permits the worker to delegate or says 'act according to your opinion', the worker may delegate the work to another. Without such permission, delegating makes the worker a usurper (ghasib), the contract between the worker and landowner is void, and the landowner may claim the land's rent from either party. If the landowner recovers from the first (the worker), the worker cannot recover from the delegate; if from the delegate, the delegate can recover from the worker because the delegate was misled. The text then states that if the seed is from the worker (as in Fatawa al-Khulasah), the worker may delegate even without the landowner's permission, but then the arrangement is treated as a void lease (ijarah fasidah) rather than muraba'ah. The passage thus distinguishes delegation with and without permission, and between seed ownership.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzara'ah): A contract of sharecropping where one party provides land and/or seed and the other works for a share of the produce.
غاصب (ghasib): One who takes possession of another's property without right; here, the worker who acts without permission in delegating the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a muraba'ah contract where the seed belongs to the landowner, if the landowner does not permit the worker to delegate, and the worker delegates anyway, what is the ruling on the original muraba'ah contract?
A) The contract remains valid but the landowner can claim rent.
B) The contract becomes void and the worker is a usurper.
C) The contract becomes void but the worker is not liable.
D) The contract becomes a mudarabah.

Key Takeaway
Delegation of muraba'ah work is void without the landowner's permission when the seed is from the landowner; but if the seed is from the worker, delegation is allowed even without permission, though it becomes a void lease.

Landowner Working on the Crop Without Permission in Muraba'ah
Detailed scenarios of landowner working on the crop in muraba'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for each scenario where the landowner works on the crop without permission, distinguishing cases based on seed ownership and work performed.

Core Idea
The landowner who works without permission is a volunteer; produce follows contract or, exceptionally, qiyas.

This lesson examines detailed scenarios from al-Muhit where the landowner intervenes in the crop without the worker's permission. The general principle is that such work is voluntary (tatawwu'), and the distribution of the harvest depends on who provided the seed and who performed the essential work. We will walk through the cases to understand when the produce goes according to the original contract and when it is given to the landowner by qiyas, with istihsan sometimes returning it to the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify seed ownership
First, determine whether the seed belongs to the landowner or the worker. This is the primary division in the text.
2
Examine the worker's actions before the landowner's intervention
Check whether the worker planted, watered, or tended the crop before the landowner stepped in. The stage of work affects the ruling.
3
Classify the landowner's role
The landowner is a volunteer (mutatawwi') if he works without the worker's command. His work does not automatically give him a share of the produce.
4
Apply the default ruling: contract or qiyas
The text presents two approaches: by qiyas, the produce may go to the landowner if he did all the work; by istihsan, the original contract conditions prevail. Note which is preferred (mufta bihi).
5
Observe the final distribution
In each scenario, state who gets the produce and any compensation owed for seed. The text also extends these rulings to mu'amalah contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : إذا عمل صاحب الأرض مع العامل بأمره أو بغير أمره فهو على قسمين: إما أن يكون البذر من قبل رب الأرض أو من قبل العامل، فلو كان من قبل رب الأرض بأن دفع أرضه وبذره مزارعة بالنصف فزرع العامل وسقى فلما نبت قام عليه رب الأرض حتى استحصد بغير أمر العامل فالخارج على الشرط ورب الأرض متطوع بعمله كما لو قام عليه أجنبي، ولو بذر المزارع ولم ينبت ولم يسقه فسقاه رب الأرض وقام عليه حتى استحصد فالخارج لرب الأرض قياساً، وفي الاستحسان على الشروط ورب الأرض متطوع كما لو قام عليه أجنبي، ولو لم يزرع العامل حتى زرعه رب الأرض وسقاه ثم قام عليه المزارع حتى استحصد فالخارج لرب الأرض والمزارع متطوع، وإن بذره رب الأرض بغير إذن الزارع ولم يسقه ولم ينبت المزارع وقام عليه حتى استحصد فالخارج على الشرط القسم الثاني لو كان البذر من قبل المزارع فبذر ولم يسقه ولم ينبت فقام عليه رب الأرض حتى استحصد فالخارج بينهما، وكذا لو بذره رب الأرض ولم ينبت ولم يسقه حتى قام عليه المزارع فالخارج على الشرط، ولو كان رب الأرض سقاه حتى نبت ثم قام عليه المزارع وسقاه فهو لرب الأرض ويضمن البذر لربه والمزارع متطوع في سقيه، وما علمته من الجواب في المزارعة فهو الجواب في المعاملة؛ كذا في المحيط.
In al-Muhit: When the landowner works with the worker by his command or without his command, it is two divisions: either the seed is from the landowner or from the worker. If it is from the landowner, that he gave his land and seed in muraba'ah for half, then the worker planted and watered, then when it sprouted the landowner tended it until harvest without the worker's command, then the produce is according to the condition and the landowner is a volunteer in his work, as if an outsider tended it. If the worker sowed but it did not grow and he did not water it, then the landowner watered it and tended it until harvest, then the produce belongs to the landowner by qiyas, but by istihsan it is on the conditions, and the landowner is a volunteer as if an outsider tended it. If the worker did not plant until the landowner planted and watered it, then the worker tended it until harvest, then the produce belongs to the landowner and the worker is a volunteer. If the landowner sowed without the farmer's permission and did not water, and the farmer did not grow, and he tended it until harvest, then the produce is on the conditions. The second division: if the seed was from the farmer, so he sowed but did not water and it did not grow, then the landowner tended it until harvest, then the produce is between them. Likewise, if the landowner sowed it and it did not grow and he did not water it until the farmer tended it, then the produce is on the conditions. If the landowner watered it until it grew, then the farmer tended it and watered it, then it belongs to the landowner, and he guarantees the seed to its owner, and the farmer is a volunteer in his watering. Whatever I know of the answer in muraba'ah is the answer in mu'amalah. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit presents detailed cases when the landowner works on the crop without the worker's permission. The general principle is that if the landowner works without permission, he is considered a volunteer (mutatawwi'), and the distribution of the produce follows the original contract or, in some cases, qiyas. The text is divided into two main categories based on who provided the seed. For seed from the landowner, the produce usually goes according to the contract, but if the landowner does all the work after the worker abandoned it, by qiyas the produce belongs to the landowner, but istihsan returns it to the contract. For seed from the worker, the produce is shared unless the landowner initially planted it, in which case the produce is his. The passage ends by stating that the rulings for muraba'ah apply similarly to mu'amalah (a similar contract).

Key Terms
متطوع (mutatawwi'): One who performs an act voluntarily without compensation; here, the landowner who works without being obligated.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here applied to compare the landowner's work to an outsider's.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; here used to prefer adherence to the contract over the outcome of qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the seed is from the landowner and the worker planted and watered, then the landowner tended the crop until harvest without the worker's command, what is the ruling by istihsan?
A) The produce belongs entirely to the landowner.
B) The produce is divided according to the original contract.
C) The produce belongs to the worker.
D) The produce is given to charity.

Key Takeaway
When the landowner works on the crop without permission, he is a volunteer, and the produce distribution follows the original contract except when the worker completely abandons the crop, where qiyas may give the produce to the landowner, but istihsan restores the contract.

Dispute Resolution in Muraba'ah and Musaqah Contracts
Evidentiary rules for sharecropping disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi evidentiary rules for resolving disputes in sharecropping contracts by identifying which party's statement is accepted with oath and when evidence (bayyinah) overrides.

Core Idea
Whoever provides the seed controls the dispute after planting; before planting, the claimant of voidness wins.

In sharecropping and irrigation contracts, disputes can arise over stipulated shares, contract validity, or after death. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules to resolve these disputes based on seed ownership, timing relative to planting, and availability of evidence. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out these rules systematically, guiding you through the burden of proof and the order of oaths. Understanding these rules is crucial for a mufti or judge to adjudicate such agricultural contracts fairly.

Guided Path
1
Classify the dispute
First, determine whether the dispute is about the contract conditions (shurut) or about the validity/voidness (jawaz/fasad) of the contract. The rules differ based on this classification.
If they agree on validity but differ on conditions, the rules of condition disputes apply. If they differ on validity itself, special rules for voidness claims apply.
2
Identify the seed owner
Identify which party provided the seed (bazr): the landowner (rabb al-ard) or the worker/ farmer (amil/zarra'?). The seed owner has significant evidentiary privileges.
Seed ownership is a key determinant; the rules change whether the seed is from the landowner or the worker.
3
Determine the timing
Establish whether the dispute occurred before planting (qabl al-zira'ah) or after planting (ba'd al-zira'ah). The timing affects whose statement is credited.
After planting, the seed owner's statement is generally preferred; before planting, the rules differ.
4
Apply the evidence hierarchy
Check if any party brings evidence (bayyinah). If both have evidence, certain evidence is given precedence (e.g., farmer's evidence before planting). If neither has evidence, they take mutual oaths (tahaluf) and the contract is rescinded. If one has evidence and the other has a statement, the evidence prevails.
The text explicitly states: 'If neither has evidence, they each take an oath and rescind.' For validity disputes, the one claiming voidness wins before planting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما لو اختلفا في المزارعة أو المعاملة فلا يخلو إما أن يختلفا في العقد أو الشروط أو في جواز العقد وفساده فلو اتفقا على جواز واختلفا في المشروط والبذر من قبل رب إن كان قبل المزارعة وأقاما بينة فبينة الزارع أولى لأنها أكثر إثباتاً، وإن لم تقم لأحدهما الأرض بينة تحالفا وتراد، وإن اختلفا بعد الزراعة والنبات فالقول لرب الأرض مع يمينه والبينة للآخر، وإن كان البذر من قبل العامل فالقول له والبيئة للآخر بعد عقد المزارعة وقبلها يتحالفان وبديء بيمين رب الأرض، وأما لو اختلفا في الجواز والفساد فهو على ثلاثة أوجه : إما إن اختلفا قبل الزراعة فالقول لمدعي الفساد وإن اختلفا بعد الزراعة فالقول لصاحب البذر. هذا إذا كان البذر من قبل العامل، فإن كان من قبل رب الأرض فاختلفا فالقول للعامل والبينة لرب الأرض، سواء اختلفا قبل الزرع أو بعده، وأما لو اختلفت ورثتهما بعد موتهما فإما أن يختلفا في مقدار الأنصباء والبذر من قبل العامل فالقول لورثة صاحب الأرض والبينة للآخر، وإن كان البذر من رب الأرض فالقول لورثة صاحب البذر والبيئة للآخر، وإن أقاما معاً بينة فبينة صاحب البذر أولى، وإن اختلفا في صاحب البذر كان القول قول ورثة المزارع والبينة للآخر، وإن اختلفا في البذر وفي شرط وأقاما بينة فالبينة بينة رب الأرض. ولو مات المزارع بعد الاستحصاد ولم يدر ما فعل بحصة المزارع فضمان حصة المزارع في ماله لأنه مات مجهلاً للوديعة، ولو مات العامل بعدما انتهت الثمرة فلم يوجد في النخل شيء إن علم خروج الثمرة ضمن حصة الآخر وإلا فلا كذا في المحيط. وتفاصيله تطلب منه اهـ والله تعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
As for if they differ in muraba'ah or mu'amalah, it is not free from being either a dispute in the contract, or in the conditions, or in the validity and voidness of the contract. If they agree on validity and differ in what was stipulated, and the seed is from the landowner, if it is before muraba'ah and they bring evidence, the evidence of the farmer is preferable because it is more confirming. If neither has evidence, they each take an oath and rescind. If they differ after planting and growth, the statement of the landowner is accepted with his oath, and the evidence is for the other. If the seed is from the worker, his statement is accepted and the evidence is for the other. After the contract of muraba'ah and before it, they each take an oath and begin with the oath of the landowner. As for if they differ in validity and voidness, it has three aspects: if they differ before planting, the statement of the one claiming voidness is accepted; if they differ after planting, the statement of the seed owner is accepted. This is if the seed was from the worker; if it was from the landowner and they differ, the statement of the worker is accepted and the evidence is for the landowner, whether they differ before or after planting. As for if their heirs differ after their death, if they differ in the amount of shares and the seed was from the worker, the statement of the heirs of the landowner is accepted and the evidence is for the other. If the seed was from the landowner, the statement of the heirs of the seed owner is accepted and the evidence is for the other. If they both bring evidence, the evidence of the seed owner is preferable. If they differ about who is the seed owner, the statement of the heirs of the farmer is accepted and the evidence is for the other. If they differ about the seed and a condition and they bring evidence, the evidence is of the landowner. If the farmer dies after harvest and it is unknown what he did with the farmer's share, the guarantee of the farmer's share is in his wealth because he died having concealed the deposit. If the worker dies after the fruit season and nothing is found in the palm trees, if the emergence of fruit was known, he guarantees the other's share; otherwise not. Thus in al-Muhit. Its details are sought from it. End. And Allah knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and resort.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage provides rules for handling disputes between parties in muraba'ah and mu'amalah contracts. The disputes can be about the contract terms, conditions, or validity. The text outlines who has the burden of proof and whose statement is credited based on factors: timing (before/after planting), seed ownership, and whether it's between original parties or their heirs. Generally, if the seed is from the landowner, his statement is preferred after planting; if from the worker, his statement is preferred. For validity disputes, before planting the one claiming voidness wins; after planting, the seed owner wins. For heirs, the rules shift: the seed owner's heirs' evidence is preferred if both have evidence. The passage also covers cases where a party dies: the farmer's death after harvest with unknown disposition of shares leads to liability; the worker's death after fruit season requires knowledge of fruit emergence for liability.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically witness testimony; the party with stronger evidence prevails.
تحالف (tahaluf): Mutual oath-taking when neither party has evidence; after which the contract is rescinded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a muraba'ah dispute before planting where the seed is from the landowner, both parties have witnesses. Whose evidence is preferred?
A) The landowner's evidence
B) The farmer's evidence
C) Neither, they take oaths
D) The evidence is rejected because the contract is void

Key Takeaway
In sharecropping disputes, seed ownership and timing determine whose statement is accepted; evidence always trumps mere statement.

Introduction to Slaughter: Definitions, Conditions, and Ruling
Opening definitions and conditions of slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four conditions of valid slaughter (dhabh) in the Hanafi school and distinguish between the terms dhabihah (animal) and dhabh (act).

Core Idea
Slaughter (dhakaat) requires four conditions: tool, slaughterer, permissible animal, and tasmiyah.

This lesson opens the Book of Slaughter from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. We begin with the connection between this chapter and the previous one (muzara'ah), then define key terms: dhabihah (the slaughtered animal) vs dhabh (the act), and dhakaat (ritual slaughter). The passage then outlines the pillar (cutting) and four conditions: a sharp tool, a Muslim or Kitabi slaughterer, a permissible animal, and the tasmiyah. Understanding these conditions is essential because each is a prerequisite for the meat to be halal and pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the connection between chapters
The commentator explains why the Book of Slaughter follows Muzara'ah: both involve immediate destruction for eventual benefit—destroying seeds for crops, and taking the animal's life for food. This logical link frames the subject.
Note that Musaqah is included under Muzara'ah, so the connection suffices.
2
Distinguish dhabihah from dhabh
The text clarifies that the book's title 'Dhaba'ih' (plural of dhabihah) refers to the animal slaughtered, not the act (dhabh). The author kept the literal meaning, though discussing the act would be more appropriate for fiqh.
Remember: dhabihah = the animal; dhabh = the cutting action.
3
Understand dhakaat linguistically and legally
Dhakaat has two linguistic roots: sharpness (rapid death) and purification (removing impurity). Both apply: the cut is sharp and it purifies the animal. Legally, dhakaat is the process that makes the animal halal.
The word 'dhakaat' is used in hadith for purification of a hide by tanning.
4
List the pillar and four conditions
The pillar (rukn) is the cutting/wounding. The conditions (shurut) are: (1) a sharp cutting tool, (2) the slaughterer is Muslim or Kitabi, (3) the animal is permissible (edible or usable for skin/hair), (4) recitation of tasmiyah (Bismillah) — a Hanafi condition, details to follow.
The fourth condition (tasmiyah) is disputed; the text says 'according to us' (Hanafi).
5
State the ruling of slaughter
The ruling (hukm) is that the slaughtered animal becomes pure (tahir) and permissible to eat if it is edible; if not edible (e.g., a non-edible but permissible animal), its carcass becomes pure for use (like hide).
This ruling comes from al-Muhit, a Hanafi reference.

Source Text

هي جمع ذبيحة وهي اسم لما يذبح والذبح قطع الأوداج وحل ذبيحة مسلم وكتابي

قال جمهور الشراح : المناسبة بين المزارعة والذبائح كونها إتلافاً في الحال للانتفاع في المآل، فإن المزارعة إتلاف الحب في الأرض للانتفاع بما ينبت منها والذبح إتلاف الحيوان بإزهاق روحه للانتفاع به بعد ذلك قيل هذا إنما يقتضي تعقيب المزارعة بالذبائح دون تعقيب المساقاة، وأجيب بأن المساقاة كالمزارعة في غالب الأحكام فكانت المناسبة المذكورة بين المزارعة والذبائح لدخول المساقاة في المزارعة ضمناً فاكتفي بذلك. ويحتاج إلى معرفة تفسير الذكاة لغة وشرعاً وركنها وشرط جوازها .وحكمها. أما تفسيرها لغة فهي إما مشتقة يقال سراج ذكي إذا كان يراه في غاية الحدة، ويقال فلان ذكي إذا كان سريع الفهم والإدراك لحدة خاطره وفهمه، ويقال مسك ذكي إذا كان طيب الرائحة يقوم منه الريح. وإما مشتقة من الطهارة قال عليه الصلاة والسلام دباغ الأديم (ذكاة أي طهارته وقال «ذكاة الأرض . أي طهارتها وكلا المعنيين موجود في الذكاة فإن فيها حدة من حيث إنها مسرعة إلى الموت وتطهر الحيوان عن الدماء المسفوحات والرطوبات السائلة النجسة. وأما ركنها فهو القطع والجرح. وأما شرطها فأربعة آلة قاطعة جارحة، والثاني كون الذبح ممن له ملة حقيقة كالمسلم أو ادعاء كالكافر، والثالث كون المحل من المحللات إما من كل وجه كمأكول اللحم من وجه كغيره وهو ما يباح الانتفاع بجلده وشعره والرابع التسمية عندنا لما سيأتي. وأما حكمها فطهارة المذبوح وحل أكله إن كان من المأكولات وطهارة عينه للانتفاع إذا كان لا يؤكل ؛ كذا في المحيط . وأما شرعاً فهو قوله «والذبح إلى آخره». وترجم بالذبائح والظاهر أنه أراد بالذبائح الذبح الذي هو الذكاة والمؤلف أبقاه على ظاهره فلذا قال : (هي جمع ذبيحة وهي اسم لما يذبح) يعني الذبائح جمع ذبيحة والذبيحة اسم للشيء المذبوح ولا يخفى أن المناسب أن يترجم بالذبح لأن فعل والمكلف إنما يبحث عن الأفعال أولاً بالذات لا عن
The Book of Slaughter: It is the plural of dhabihah, which is a name for that which is slaughtered. Slaughter (dhabh) is cutting the jugular veins. The slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi is permissible. The majority of commentators said: The connection between muzara'ah and slaughter is that both involve immediate destruction for eventual benefit. Muzara'ah destroys seeds in the ground for benefit from what grows, and slaughter destroys the animal by taking its life for benefit from it thereafter. It was said that this necessitates juxtaposing muzara'ah with slaughter, not musaqah. It was answered that musaqah is like muzara'ah in most rulings, so the mentioned connection between muzara'ah and slaughter suffices because musaqah is included in muzara'ah implicitly. One needs to know the interpretation of dhakaat linguistically and legally, its pillar, condition of permissibility, and its ruling. As for its linguistic interpretation: it is either derived from a root meaning sharpness—e.g., a bright lamp, a sharp-minded person, or fragrant musk—or from purity, as the Prophet said: 'Tanning a hide is its purification (dhabh),' and 'The purification of the earth...' Both meanings are present in dhakaat: it has sharpness in that it rapidly causes death, and it purifies the animal from spilled blood and impure fluids. Its pillar is cutting and wounding. Its conditions are four: (1) a cutting, wounding tool; (2) that the slaughterer be one who has a true religion like a Muslim, or one who claims it like a disbeliever; (3) that the animal be permissible either absolutely (e.g., edible meat) or partially (e.g., what is permissible to use its hide and hair); (4) the saying of the tasmiyah according to us, as will come. Its ruling: purification of the slaughtered animal and permissibility of eating it if it is edible, and purification of its substance for use if it is not eaten. Thus in al-Muhit. As for the legal definition, he said: 'And slaughtering...' He titled it 'Slaughtered Animals' and it appears he meant by it the act of slaughter (dhabh) which is dhakaat, but the author kept it apparent, so he said: 'It is the plural of dhabihah, which is a name for that which is slaughtered.' That is, dhaba'ih is plural of dhabihah, and dhabihah is a name for the thing slaughtered. It is not hidden that it would be more appropriate to title it by the act (dhabh) because it is an action, and the obligated person only researches actions primarily, not...
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Slaughter (Dhaba'ih) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator first explains the connection between the previous book (Muzara'ah/Musaqah) and this one: both involve immediate destruction for eventual benefit—destroying seeds or animals. He then defines key terms: dhabh (slaughter) linguistically as cutting the jugular veins, and dhakaat (ritual slaughter) as having two linguistic roots: sharpness (because it causes rapid death) and purification (because it purifies the animal from impurities). The legal pillar (rukn) is the cutting/wounding. Four conditions are listed: a sharp cutting tool, the slaughterer must be a person of a revealed religion (Muslim or Kitabi from People of the Book), the animal must be permissible as food or at least permissible to use its skin/hair, and the recitation of tasmiyah (Bismillah) as per the Hanafi school, details to follow. The ruling (hukm) is that the animal becomes purified and permissible to eat if edible, or its carcass becomes pure for non-edible uses. The commentator notes that the author used the term dhaba'ih (slaughtered animals) instead of dhabh (the act) to stay close to the literal meaning, though discussing actions would be more appropriate.

Key Terms
الذبيحة (al-dhabihah): The slaughtered animal; the object of slaughter, not the act itself.
الذكاة (al-dhakaat): Ritual slaughter that makes the animal halal and pure; encompasses both dhabh and nahr (stabbing in the neck).
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' (in the name of Allah) at the time of slaughter, which is a condition for validity in the Hanafi school.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition external to the act that must be present for validity; missing a condition renders the act invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many conditions are mentioned for the validity of slaughter?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Valid slaughter in the Hanafi school requires four conditions: a sharp tool, a Muslim/Kitabi slaughterer, a permissible animal, and the recitation of tasmiyah.

Definition and General Ruling of Dhabh
Defines dhabh linguistically and legally, lists pillars and conditions, states general ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definition of dhabh, list its four conditions, and identify the ruling on the slaughtered animal.

Core Idea
Slaughter is permissible by Shariah; its validity depends on proper cutting, permissible animal, qualified slaughterer, and tasmiyah.

This lesson introduces the Book of Sacrifices (Kitab al-Dhaba'ih) and establishes the foundational definitions. You will learn what dhabh means linguistically and legally, its essential elements (rukn), conditions (shurut), and the overall ruling (hukm) of the act. Understanding these basics is the first step in mastering the rules of halal slaughter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
Read the linguistic explanation: 'dhabh' is cutting the awdaj (jugular veins). Note the root meanings of sharpness and purification.
The term 'dhabh' also relates to quickness and cleansing.
2
Extract the legal definition
From the phrase 'Wa amma shar'an fahuwa qawluhu (wa al-dhabh ila akhira)', find the legal definition: it is the act of cutting the throat in a specific manner.
3
List the conditions (shurut)
The author mentions four conditions: a cutting tool, a slaughterer with a millah (Muslim or Kitabi), a permissible animal, and tasmiyah. Write each down.
The Hanafi school uniquely requires tasmiyah as wajib.
4
Identify the ruling (hukm)
The passage states: 'the slaughtered animal becomes pure and permissible to eat if edible, otherwise its body becomes pure for use.' Note this general hukm.
5
Connect to the broader text
Understand why this chapter follows muzara'ah: both involve immediate destruction for future benefit.
This is a thematic link, not a legal one.

رحمه الله : (وحل ذبيحة مسلم وكتابي لقوله تعالى وطعام الذين أوتوا الكتاب حل لكم [المائدة : ٥] والمراد به ذبائحهم لأن مطلق الطعام غير المذكى يحل من أي كافر ولا يشترط أن يكون من أهل الكتاب ولا فرق في الكتابي بين أن يكون ذمياً أو حربياً، ويشترط أن لا يذكر فيه غير الله تعالى حتى لو ذكر الكتابي المسيح أو عزيراً لا يحل لقوله تعالى ﴿وما أهل به لغير الله ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۷۳] وهو كالمسلم في ذلك فإنه لو أهل به لغير الله لا يحل. قال في العناية : الكتابي إذا أتى بالذبيحة مذبوحة أكلنا فلو ذبح بالحضور فلا بد من الشرط وهو أن لا يذكر عليها غير اسم الله . ولا فرق في الذابح بين أن يكون صبياً أو مجنوناً. قال في النهاية : المراد بالمجنون المعتوه لأن المجنون لا قصد له ولا بد من التسمية وهي القصد أن يعقلها. قال. رحمه الله : (وصبي وامرأة وأخرس وأقلف) يعني تحل ذبيحة هؤلاء. والمراد بالصبي الذي يعقل التسمية ويضبط وإن لم يكن كذلك لا يحل لأن التسمية على الذبيحة شرط بالنص وذلك بالعقد وصحة العقد بالمعرفة والضبط هو أن يعلم شرائط الذبح من فري الأوداج والتسمية والمعتوه كالصبي إذا كان صابطاً والقلقة ولا الفراسة لا تحل بذلك فيحل والأخرس عاجز عن الذكر فيكون معذوراً وتقوم الملة مقامه كالناسي بل أولى لأنه ألزم. قال رحمه الله : (لا مجوسي ووثني ومرتد ومحرم وتارك التسمية (عمداً يعني لا تحل ذبيحة هؤلاء؛ أما المجوسي فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «سنوا بهم سنة أهل الكتاب غير ناكحي نسائهم ولا
Book of Sacrifices. They (Al-Dhaba'ih) are the plural of dhabihah, which is a name for what is slaughtered. And al-dhabh is cutting the jugular veins. And the permissibility of the slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi. ... (continues) ... said: (And the slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi is permissible) due to His statement: 'And the food of those who were given the Scripture is permissible for you' [Maidah 5]. And what is meant is their slaughter because absolute unslaughtered food is not permissible from any disbeliever. And it is not required that he be from the People of the Book. And there is no difference in the Kitabi between being a dhimmi or a harbi. And it is required that he not mention other than Allah's name over it, such that if the Kitabi mentions the Messiah or 'Uzayr, it is not permissible due to His statement: 'And what has been dedicated to other than Allah' [Baqarah 173]. And he is like the Muslim in that: if he dedicates to other than Allah, it is not permissible. ... (continues) ... said: (No to a Magian, idolater, apostate, muhrim, and one who deliberately abandons the tasmiyah) meaning the slaughter of these is not permissible.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Sacrifices (Kitab al-Dhaba'ih) from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author begins by explaining the connection between the previous section (muzara'ah) and dhaba'ih: both involve immediate destruction for future benefit. He then defines dhabh linguistically and legally. Linguistically, 'dhabh' means cutting the jugular veins (awdaj). The legal definition (shar'an) is that it is the cutting of the throat in a specific manner. The author explains that the essential element (rukn) is the cutting or wounding. The conditions (shurut) are four: a cutting tool; that the slaughterer be one who follows a divine law (millah) whether truly like a Muslim or claimingly like a disbeliever from Ahl al-Kitab; that the animal be permissible to eat or use; and the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) according to the Hanafi school. The ruling (hukm) is that the slaughtered animal becomes pure and permissible to eat if it is edible, or its body becomes pure for use if not eaten. The author then discusses the permissibility of slaughter by various persons: a Muslim, a Kitabi (Jew or Christian), a child who understands, a woman, a mute, and an uncircumcised (aqla'). He excludes Magians (majusi), idolaters (wathani), apostates (murtadd), those in ihram (muhrim), and those who deliberately omit the tasmiyah. For the Kitabi, it is required that he not mention other than Allah's name. If he mentions the Messiah or 'Uzayr, it is not permissible. The author also mentions an intra-Hanafi debate: some Iraqi scholars held that slaughter is inherently prohibited by reason (due to pain caused to the animal) but allowed by Shariah. Imam Sarakhsi refutes this, arguing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) slaughtered before prophethood, and he would not do what is rationally prohibited like lying or tyranny. This shows that slaughter is not prohibited by pure reason but is permissible by Shariah. The overall ruling is that the meat of an animal properly slaughtered by a Muslim or Kitabi is halal.

Key Terms
ذبيحة (dhabīḥah): The animal that is slaughtered
ذبح (dhabḥ): Cutting the jugular veins (awdaj) of the animal in a specific manner
أوداج (awdāj): Plural of wadaj; the jugular veins, including the windpipe (halqum) and esophagus (mari')
تسمية (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' at the time of slaughter

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition (shart) for valid slaughter?
A) The slaughterer must be a Muslim or Kitabi.
B) The animal must be permissible to eat.
C) The knife must be facing the qibla.
D) The tasmiyah must be recited.

Key Takeaway
Slaughter is permissible by Shariah; its validity depends on four conditions: a cutting tool, a qualified slaughterer, a permissible animal, and tasmiyah.

Permissible and Impermissible Slaughterers
Lists permissible and impermissible slaughterers, with conditions for Kitabi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list who may and may not slaughter according to the Hanafi school, and explain the condition of tasmiyah for a Kitabi slaughterer.

Core Idea
Only the slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi is halal; Magians, idolaters, apostates, muhrims, and deliberate omitters of tasmiyah are not permissible.

This lesson focuses on the person performing the slaughter (al-dhabih). The Hanafi school specifies that the slaughterer must be a Muslim or a Kitabi (Jew/Christian) who does not mention other than Allah's name. The text provides a detailed list of permissible and impermissible individuals, including exceptions for a discerning child, woman, mute, and uncircumcised person, and excludes Magians, idolaters, apostates, those in ihram, and those who deliberately omit tasmiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The passage begins with 'Wa hallu dhabihati muslimin wa kitabiyyin' – the slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi is permissible. Memorize this foundational rule.
The Quranic verse from Al-Ma'idah 5:5 is cited as proof.
2
Examine the condition for Kitabi
The text stipulates that a Kitabi must not mention other than Allah's name. If he mentions the Messiah or 'Uzayr, the meat is not halal.
This is derived from the verse 'Wa ma uhilla bihi li ghayrillah' (Al-Baqarah 173).
3
List permissible categories beyond Muslim and Kitabi
The author extends permissibility to a child (who understands tasmiyah), a woman, a mute person, and an uncircumcised person. Note the rationale for each.
The mute is excused from verbal tasmiyah because of inability.
4
List impermissible categories
The text explicitly excludes: Majusi (Magian), wathani (idolater), murtadd (apostate), muhrim (in ihram), and one who deliberately omits tasmiyah.
For the Magian, a hadith is cited: 'Treat them like the People of the Book, but do not marry their women nor eat their slaughtered meat.'
5
Understand exceptions for forgetfulness
The deliberate omiter of tasmiyah is impermissible; if forgetful, the slaughter is valid. This aligns with the Hanafi position on tasmiyah.
The passage does not repeat this here, but the earlier lesson established it.

قيل هذا إنما يقتضي تعقيب المزارعة بالذبائح دون تعقيب المساقاة، وأجيب بأن المساقاة كالمزارعة في غالب الأحكام فكانت المناسبة المذكورة بين المزارعة والذبائح لدخول المساقاة في المزارعة ضمناً فاكتفي بذلك. ويحتاج إلى معرفة تفسير الذكاة لغة وشرعاً وركنها وشرط جوازها .وحكمها. أما تفسيرها لغة فهي إما مشتقة يقال سراج ذكي إذا كان يراه في غاية الحدة، ويقال فلان ذكي إذا كان سريع الفهم والإدراك لحدة خاطره وفهمه، ويقال مسك ذكي إذا كان طيب الرائحة يقوم منه الريح. وإما مشتقة من الطهارة قال عليه الصلاة والسلام دباغ الأديم (ذكاة أي طهارته وقال «ذكاة الأرض . أي طهارتها وكلا المعنيين موجود في الذكاة فإن فيها حدة من حيث إنها مسرعة إلى الموت وتطهر الحيوان عن الدماء المسفوحات والرطوبات السائلة النجسة. وأما ركنها فهو القطع والجرح. وأما شرطها فأربعة آلة قاطعة جارحة، والثاني كون الذبح ممن له ملة حقيقة كالمسلم أو ادعاء كالكافر، والثالث كون المحل من المحللات إما من كل وجه كمأكول اللحم من وجه كغيره وهو ما يباح الانتفاع بجلده وشعره والرابع التسمية عندنا لما سيأتي. وأما حكمها فطهارة المذبوح وحل أكله إن كان من المأكولات وطهارة عينه للانتفاع إذا كان لا يؤكل؛ كذا في المحيط . وأما شرعاً فهو قوله «والذبح إلى آخره». وترجم بالذبائح والظاهر أنه أراد بالذبائح الذبح الذي هو الذكاة والمؤلف أبقاه على ظاهره فلذا قال : (هي جمع ذبيحة وهي اسم لما يذبح) يعني الذبائح جمع ذبيحة والذبيحة اسم للشيء المذبوح ولا يخفى أن المناسب أن يترجم بالذبح لأن فعل والمكلف إنما يبحث عن الأفعال أولاً بالذات لا عن الأعيان إلا بطريق التبع. وقوله جمع ذبيحة الأولى تركه لأن الفقية لا يبحث عن الأفراد والجمع وإنما يبحث عن الأحكام قال رحمه الله : ( والذبح قطع الأوداج) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام أفر الأوداج بما شئت والمراد الحلقوم والمريء والودجان، وإنما عبر بالأوداج تغليباً وبه يحل المذبوح لقوله تعالى إلا ما ذكيتم ﴾ [المائدة : ٣] ولأن المحرم هو الدم المسفوح وبالذبح يقع التمييز بينه وبين اللحم فيطهر به إن كان غير مأكول ويقال ذكاء السن بالمد لنهاية الشباب، وذكاة النار بالقصر لتمام اشتعالها وهي اختيارية واضطرارية فالأول الجرح ما بين اللبة واللحيين، والثاني الجرح في أي موضع كان من البدن وهذا كالبدل عن الأول لأنه لا يصار إليه إلا عند العجز عن الأول، وإنما كان كذلك لأن الأول أبلغ في إخراج الدم من الثاني فلا يترك إلا بالعجز عنه، ويكتفي بالثاني للضرورة لأن التكليف بحسب الوسع . وذهب العراقيون من مشايخنا إلى أن الذبح محظور عقلاً لما فيه من إيلام الحيوان ولكن الشرع أحلة. قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي في المبسوط : وهذا عندي باطل لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يتناول اللحم قبل البعثة ولا يظن به أنه كان يأكل ذبائح المشركين لذبحهم بأسماء الهتهم فعرفنا أنه كان يصطاد ويذبح بنفسه وما كان يفعل ما هو المحظور عقلاً كالكذب والظلم والسفه.
قال
وهو
رحمه الله : (وحل ذبيحة مسلم وكتابي لقوله تعالى وطعام الذين أوتوا الكتاب حل لكم [المائدة : ٥] والمراد به ذبائحهم لأن مطلق الطعام غير المذكى يحل من أي كافر ولا يشترط أن يكون من أهل الكتاب ولا فرق في الكتابي بين أن يكون ذمياً أو حربياً، ويشترط أن لا يذكر فيه غير الله تعالى حتى لو ذكر الكتابي المسيح أو عزيراً لا يحل لقوله تعالى ﴿وما أهل به لغير الله ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۷۳] وهو كالمسلم في ذلك فإنه لو أهل به لغير الله لا يحل. قال في العناية : الكتابي إذا أتى بالذبيحة مذبوحة أكلنا فلو ذبح بالحضور فلا بد من الشرط وهو أن لا يذكر عليها غير اسم الله . ولا فرق في الذابح بين أن يكون صبياً أو مجنوناً. قال في النهاية : المراد بالمجنون المعتوه لأن المجنون لا قصد له ولا بد من التسمية وهي القصد أن يعقلها. قال. رحمه الله : (وصبي وامرأة وأخرس وأقلف) يعني تحل ذبيحة هؤلاء. والمراد بالصبي الذي يعقل التسمية ويضبط وإن لم يكن كذلك لا يحل لأن التسمية على الذبيحة شرط بالنص وذلك بالعقد وصحة العقد بالمعرفة والضبط هو أن يعلم شرائط الذبح من فري الأوداج والتسمية والمعتوه كالصبي إذا كان صابطاً والقلقة ولا الفراسة لا تحل بذلك فيحل والأخرس عاجز عن الذكر فيكون معذوراً وتقوم الملة مقامه كالناسي بل أولى لأنه ألزم. قال رحمه الله : (لا مجوسي ووثني ومرتد ومحرم وتارك التسمية (عمداً يعني لا تحل ذبيحة هؤلاء؛ أما المجوسي فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «سنوا بهم سنة أهل الكتاب غير ناكحي نسائهم ولا
Book of Sacrifices. They (Al-Dhaba'ih) are the plural of dhabihah, which is a name for what is slaughtered. And al-dhabh is cutting the jugular veins. And the permissibility of the slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi. ... (continues) ... said: (And the slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi is permissible) due to His statement: 'And the food of those who were given the Scripture is permissible for you' [Maidah 5]. And what is meant is their slaughter because absolute unslaughtered food is not permissible from any disbeliever. And it is not required that he be from the People of the Book. And there is no difference in the Kitabi between being a dhimmi or a harbi. And it is required that he not mention other than Allah's name over it, such that if the Kitabi mentions the Messiah or 'Uzayr, it is not permissible due to His statement: 'And what has been dedicated to other than Allah' [Baqarah 173]. And he is like the Muslim in that: if he dedicates to other than Allah, it is not permissible. ... (continues) ... said: (No to a Magian, idolater, apostate, muhrim, and one who deliberately abandons the tasmiyah) meaning the slaughter of these is not permissible.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Sacrifices (Kitab al-Dhaba'ih) from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author begins by explaining the connection between the previous section (muzara'ah) and dhaba'ih: both involve immediate destruction for future benefit. He then defines dhabh linguistically and legally. Linguistically, 'dhabh' means cutting the jugular veins (awdaj). The legal definition (shar'an) is that it is the cutting of the throat in a specific manner. The author explains that the essential element (rukn) is the cutting or wounding. The conditions (shurut) are four: a cutting tool; that the slaughterer be one who follows a divine law (millah) whether truly like a Muslim or claimingly like a disbeliever from Ahl al-Kitab; that the animal be permissible to eat or use; and the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) according to the Hanafi school. The ruling (hukm) is that the slaughtered animal becomes pure and permissible to eat if it is edible, or its body becomes pure for use if not eaten. The author then discusses the permissibility of slaughter by various persons: a Muslim, a Kitabi (Jew or Christian), a child who understands, a woman, a mute, and an uncircumcised (aqla'). He excludes Magians (majusi), idolaters (wathani), apostates (murtadd), those in ihram (muhrim), and those who deliberately omit the tasmiyah. For the Kitabi, it is required that he not mention other than Allah's name. If he mentions the Messiah or 'Uzayr, it is not permissible. The author also mentions an intra-Hanafi debate: some Iraqi scholars held that slaughter is inherently prohibited by reason (due to pain caused to the animal) but allowed by Shariah. Imam Sarakhsi refutes this, arguing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) slaughtered before prophethood, and he would not do what is rationally prohibited like lying or tyranny. This shows that slaughter is not prohibited by pure reason but is permissible by Shariah. The overall ruling is that the meat of an animal properly slaughtered by a Muslim or Kitabi is halal.

Key Terms
مجوسي (majūsī): Zoroastrian/Magian; a non-Kitabi disbeliever
مرتد (murtadd): Apostate from Islam; one who leaves the religion
محرم (muhrim): Person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah
أخرس (akhras): A mute person; unable to speak
أقلف (aqlaf): Uncircumcised person

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a permissible slaughterer?
A) A Muslim woman
B) A Jewish man
C) A Christian who says 'In the name of the Messiah'
D) A mute Muslim person

Key Takeaway
Only a Muslim or a Kitabi who does not mention other than Allah's name may slaughter; Magians, idolaters, apostates, muhrims, and deliberate omitters of tasmiyah are prohibited.

8 min
The Rational Permissibility of Slaughter: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on the rational permissibility of slaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two positions on the rational permissibility of slaughter within the Hanafi school and state which one is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Slaughter is rationally permissible; the Prophet's own practice refutes the claim that it is prohibited by reason.

This lesson addresses a theoretical dispute among early Hanafi scholars: Is the act of slaughtering an animal rationally prohibited (because it causes pain) but allowed by revelation, or is it rationally permissible from the outset? The Iraqi school of Hanafis held the former view, while Imam Sarakhsi rejected it. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's methodology regarding the relationship between reason and revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Iraqi position
The passage states: 'Iraqi scholars from our masters held that slaughter is prohibited by reason (mahzur aqlan) because it causes pain to the animal, but the Shariah permitted it.'
This is a 'rational prohibition overruled by revelation' approach.
2
Find Sarakhsi's refutation
Sarakhsi declares this view 'batil' (invalid). He argues that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to eat meat before prophethood and would not do something rationally prohibited like lying or tyranny.
This implies that slaughter was always permissible, even before revelation.
3
Understand the usul point
The dispute is about the source of the ruling: does reason itself prohibit causing pain, or is permission established by Shariah such that reason cannot override? Sarakhsi's view is that the act is not inherently bad.
This relates to the Hanafi usul principle that acts are considered mubah (permissible) unless there is a prohibition.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage states that Sarakhsi's view is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The Iraqi view is rejected.
This is consistent with the dominant Hanafi position.
