Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Sacrifices (Kitab al-Dhaba'ih) from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author begins by explaining the connection between the previous section (muzara'ah) and dhaba'ih: both involve immediate destruction for future benefit. He then defines dhabh linguistically and legally. Linguistically, 'dhabh' means cutting the jugular veins (awdaj). The legal definition (shar'an) is that it is the cutting of the throat in a specific manner. The author explains that the essential element (rukn) is the cutting or wounding. The conditions (shurut) are four: a cutting tool; that the slaughterer be one who follows a divine law (millah) whether truly like a Muslim or claimingly like a disbeliever from Ahl al-Kitab; that the animal be permissible to eat or use; and the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) according to the Hanafi school. The ruling (hukm) is that the slaughtered animal becomes pure and permissible to eat if it is edible, or its body becomes pure for use if not eaten. The author then discusses the permissibility of slaughter by various persons: a Muslim, a Kitabi (Jew or Christian), a child who understands, a woman, a mute, and an uncircumcised (aqla'). He excludes Magians (majusi), idolaters (wathani), apostates (murtadd), those in ihram (muhrim), and those who deliberately omit the tasmiyah. For the Kitabi, it is required that he not mention other than Allah's name. If he mentions the Messiah or 'Uzayr, it is not permissible. The author also mentions an intra-Hanafi debate: some Iraqi scholars held that slaughter is inherently prohibited by reason (due to pain caused to the animal) but allowed by Shariah. Imam Sarakhsi refutes this, arguing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) slaughtered before prophethood, and he would not do what is rationally prohibited like lying or tyranny. This shows that slaughter is not prohibited by pure reason but is permissible by Shariah. The overall ruling is that the meat of an animal properly slaughtered by a Muslim or Kitabi is halal.

Key Terms
محظور عقلاً (maḥẓūr ʿaqlan): Prohibited by reason; an act that reason deems evil regardless of revelation
البعثة (al-biʿthah): The sending of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as a messenger; the beginning of prophethood
الشرع أحله (al-sharʿ aḥallah): The Shariah permitted it; a ruling that overrides a rational prohibition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence does Sarakhsi cite to reject the Iraqi view that slaughter is rationally prohibited?
A) A Quranic verse about permissibility.
B) A hadith that slaughter is only for food.
C) The Prophet's practice of slaughtering before prophethood.
D) Consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (majority) holds that slaughter is rationally permissible; the Iraqi view that reason prohibits it is rejected.

Conditions of Tasmiyah at Slaughter
Rulings on valid and invalid formulas of tasmiyah at slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasmiyah at slaughter, identify valid and invalid formulas, and apply the condition of 'dhikr khalis' to determine if the meat is lawful.

Core Idea
Tasmiyah must be pure remembrance of Allah; mixing supplication invalidates the slaughter.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the conditions of tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah') when slaughtering an animal. The key principle is that the tasmiyah must be a pure remembrance of Allah (dhikr khalis) without mixing it with supplication. We will explore various formulas and scenarios to understand what constitutes a valid tasmiyah and what does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tasmiyah at slaughter is wajib according to the Hanafi school. Omitting it intentionally makes the meat haram.
The ruling is based on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet's practice after slaughter shows that supplication after tasmiyah is allowed if separated, proving the tasmiyah must be distinct.
Hadith: 'Allahumma taqabbal hadha' and 'Inna salati wa nusuki'.
3
Trace the condition
The condition is that tasmiyah must be dhikr khalis (pure remembrance); if mixed with du'a (e.g., 'Allahumma ighfir li'), the meat is not lawful.
The text explicitly states: 'The condition is pure remembrance'.
4
Apply to formulas
Examine various formulas: 'Bismillah' alone is valid; 'Alhamdulillah' if intended as tasmiyah is valid but disliked if after sneeze; 'Allahumma taqabbal' before/after is permissible if separated; mentioning Muhammad alongside Allah in a connected phrase may invalidate.
The passage mentions several cases from al-Nawazil, Khizanat al-Fiqh, and others.
5
Note special cases
The passage also covers slaughter by Ahl al-Kitab, tasmiyah by the owner vs slaughterer, and multiple animals with one tasmiyah.
See the later part of the passage regarding different scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على اسم الله يحل لأنه مبتدأ واختلفوا في النصب قيل يكره فيهما بالاتفاق لوجود الوصل صورة. الثالث أن يقول مفصولاً عنه صورة ومعنى بأن يقول قبل أن يضجع الشاة أو قبل التسمية أو بعد الذبح اللهم تقبل هذا أو فلان وهذا لا يكره لما روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال بعد الذبح : اللهم تقبل هذا من أمة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ممن شهد لك بالوحدانية ولي بالبلاغ، وكان عليه الصلاة والسلام يقول إذا أراد الذبح : اللهم هذا منك ولك إن صلاتي ونسكي الخ. والشرط هو الذكر الخالص حتى لو قال اللهم اغفر لي واكتفي لا يحل لأنه دعاء وسؤال. ولو قال الحمد لله أو سبحان الله وأراد به التسمية حل ولو عطس عند الذبح وقال الحمد لله لا يحل في الأصح لأنه أراد بذلك الحمد على النعمة دون التسمية. وذكر الحلواني أن المستحب أن يقول باسم الله الله أكبر ثلاثاً. وفي النوازل : إذا قال الله ومحمد بالخفض قال بعضهم على قياس ما روي عن محمد في باب الصلاة تحرم الذبيحة، وكذا لو الله وصلى الله على سيدنا ومحمد بالواو، ولو قال بغير واو حلت الذبيحة ولكن يكره. وفي خزانة الفقه : رجلان ذبحا صيداً. أحدهما وترك الآخر التسمية لم يحرم وسمى : ولو ذبح شاة فسمى ثم ذبح أخرى فظن أن التسمية الأولى أكله . وفي الذخيرة والينابيع : تجزيه عنها لم تؤكل . وفي الحاوي : جمع العصافير فذبح واحدة وسمى وذبح أخرى على أثره بتلك التسمية لا تؤكل، ولو أمر السكين عليهم بتسمية واحدة جاز. وفي شرح الطحاوي : وذبيحة أهل الكتاب إنما تؤكل إذا أتى بها مذبوحة وإن ذبح بين يديك فإن سمى الله تعالى لا بأس بأكلها، وكذا إذا لم يسمع منه شيء، وإن سمى باسم المسيح وسمعه منه فلا يؤكل . وفي جامع الجوامع : من اشترى لحماً وعلم أنه ذبيحة مجوسي وأراد الرد فقال البائع الذابح مسلم لا يرد ويحل أكله مع الكراهية وفيه عن أبي يوسف ذئب أخذ حلقوم شاة وأوداجها فذبحها فأكلها إذا كانت تضطرب إذا سمى تحل ولو انفلتت الشاة أو البقرة من يده وقامت من مضجعها ثم أعادها إلى مضجعها اكتفى بتلك التسمية، وإن ذبح الذابح وسمى صاحب الأضحية أو غيره لم يجز اهـ .
[It is lawful if said] upon the name of Allah because it is a beginning. They differed concerning nasb (accusative). It is said it is disliked in both by agreement due to the existence of connection in form. The third is that he says it separated in form and meaning, such as saying before laying down the sheep or before the tasmiyah or after slaughter: O Allah accept this or so-and-so. This is not disliked due to what is narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said after slaughter: O Allah accept this from the nation of Muhammad ﷺ from those who testified to You with oneness and to me with delivery. And he ﷺ used to say when intending to slaughter: O Allah this is from You and to You, indeed my prayer and my sacrifice... The condition is pure remembrance, so if he says O Allah forgive me and suffices, it is not lawful because it is supplication and request. If he says Alhamdulillah or Subhanallah intending tasmiyah, it is lawful. If he sneezes at slaughter and says Alhamdulillah, it is not lawful in the most correct view because he intended praise for the blessing not tasmiyah. Al-Halawani mentioned that the recommended is to say Bismillah Allahu Akbar three times. In al-Nawazil: If he says Allah and Muhammad in jarr, some said by analogy with what is narrated from Muhammad in the chapter of prayer, the slaughtered animal becomes unlawful. Likewise if he says Allah and Salla Allahu ala Sayyidina wa Muhammad with waw. If he says without waw, the slaughter is lawful but disliked. In Khizanat al-Fiqh: Two men slaughtered game; one said tasmiyah and the other left it—it is not unlawful [for the one who said it? unclear]. If he slaughtered a sheep and said tasmiyah, then slaughtered another thinking the first tasmiyah suffices... In al-Dhakhira and al-Yanabi': it does not suffice, it is not eaten. In al-Hawi: He collected sparrows, slaughtered one with tasmiyah, and slaughtered another immediately with that same tasmiyah—it is not eaten. If he passed the knife over them with one tasmiyah, it is permissible. In Sharh al-Tahawi: The slaughter of the People of the Book is only eaten if it is brought slaughtered. If he slaughters before you and mentions Allah's name, there is no harm in eating it. Likewise if nothing is heard from him. If he mentions the name of the Messiah and it is heard from him, it is not eaten. In Jami' al-Jawami': Whoever buys meat and knows it is the slaughter of a Magian and wants to return it, and the seller says the slaughterer is Muslim—he cannot return it and it is lawful to eat it with dislike. In it from Abu Yusuf: A wolf seized the throat and jugular veins of a sheep and slaughtered it and ate it—if it was jerking, and he said tasmiyah, it is lawful. If the sheep or cow escaped from his hand and stood up from its lying place then he returned it to its lying place, that tasmiyah suffices. If the slaughterer slaughters and the owner of the udhiyah or someone else says tasmiyah, it does not suffice. End.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the conditions of tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) at the time of slaughter. The author, commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explains various scenarios. The key principle is that the tasmiyah must be a pure remembrance of Allah (dhikr khalis) without mixing it with supplication (du'a) if the supplication is connected. If the speech is separated from the tasmiyah in form and meaning, such as saying 'Allahumma taqabbal hadha' before or after, it is not disliked because it is a separate act. The condition for lawfulness is that the tasmiyah be intended as such; if one intends praise of Allah (like Alhamdulillah after sneezing) but not tasmiyah, the meat is not lawful. The Hanafi school holds that the tasmiyah is wajib (obligatory) at the time of slaughter according to the relied-upon view, and omitting it intentionally makes the meat unlawful (haram), though unintentional omission is excused. The passage also covers issues of tasmiyah on behalf of others, slaughter by Ahl al-Kitab, and the case of an animal killed by a predator but still alive at slaughter.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The utterance of 'Bismillah' at the time of slaughter, considered wajib according to the Hanafi school.
الذكر الخالص (al-dhikr al-khalis): Pure remembrance of Allah without mixing with supplication, required for a valid tasmiyah.
الذبيحة (al-dhabihah): The animal that is slaughtered according to Islamic law; the meat becomes lawful only if all conditions are met.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person says 'Allahumma ighfir li' (O Allah, forgive me) at the time of slaughter, is the meat lawful according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because it includes Allah's name
B) No, because it is a supplication and not tasmiyah
C) Yes, if he intended it as tasmiyah
D) No, because it is not in Arabic

Key Takeaway
Tasmiyah must be pure remembrance of Allah; mixing supplication or other names in a connected phrase invalidates the slaughter according to the Hanafi school.

Place of Slaughter: Between Throat and Upper Chest
Ruling on the precise location for valid slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise location for valid slaughter according to the Hanafi school and apply the ruling to cases of partial cutting or recutting.

Core Idea
Slaughter is valid only between the throat (halqah) and upper chest (labbah); cutting elsewhere renders the meat haram.

The Hanafi school establishes a precise anatomical zone for valid slaughter: between the throat (halqah) and the upper chest (labbah). This ruling is derived from the Prophet's ﷺ hadith and the rational understanding that this area contains the passages for breath, food, and blood. The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling, addressing practical problems such as partial cuts and the location of the throat knot. This lesson will guide you through the proof and its applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is slaughter (dhabh) of an animal. The Hanafi school rules that the slaughter must be performed between the throat and the upper chest. If done above or below this area, the meat becomes haram (unlawful).
The hukm level is wajib, meaning it is obligatory to slaughter in this specific zone.
2
Locate the Dalil
The primary proof is the hadith 'al-dhakatu fi al-halq' (slaughter is in the throat). This hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but considered reliable. The text also mentions rational reasoning: the throat is the meeting point of the passages for air, food, and blood vessels, so cutting there achieves the purpose of blood flow most completely.
The hadith is quoted in the original Arabic as part of the passage.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith explicitly restricts the place of slaughter to the throat. The Hanafi scholars define 'throat' precisely as the area between the halqah (Adam's apple region) and labbah (upper chest). Thus, the dalil yields the ruling that slaughter in any other location is not valid.
This is a clear example of a zanni al-dalala text being interpreted with precise anatomical definition.
4
Note the Intra-Madhhab and Cross-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there is a discussion about when a knot (uqda) of the trachea remains on the chest side: some earlier Hanafis (like al-Rustaghfani) considered the slaughter valid if the jugular veins (awdaj) are cut, even if the knot remains on the chest side. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that at least one of the trachea or esophagus must be cut. Across madhhabs, some Shafi'is allow a wider area as long as blood flows.
The text highlights a consensus that if the knot remains on the head side, cutting neither trachea nor esophagus, the slaughter is invalid.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is the restricted view: slaughter between halq and labbah is necessary. Evidence from al-Waqi'at and Fatawa Samarqand supports this. The view of al-Rustaghfani is noted as 'problematic' by the commentator because it overlooks the requirement to cut the trachea or esophagus.
The tarjih authority is the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (Ibn Nujaym) and the Hanafi textual tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والذبح بين الحلقة واللبة) بفتح اللام وتشديد الباء الموحدة وفي الجامع الصغير لا بأس بالذبح في الحلق كله وأعلاه وأسفله والأصل فيه روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال «الذكاة في الحلق ولأنه مجمع مجرى النفس ومجرى الطعام ومجرى العروق فيحصل بقطعه المقصود على أبلغ الوجوه وهو أنهار الدم. والتقييد بالحلق واللبة يفيد أنه لو ذبح أعلى من الحلقوم أو أسفل منه يحرم لأنه أهل في غير محل الذكاة ؛ ذكره في الواقعات. وفي فتاوى السمرقندي: ونقل في النهاية عن الإمام الرستغفني رحمه الله تعالى سئل عمن ذبح شاة فبقيت عقدة الحلقوم مما يلي الصدر وكان يحب أن يبقى غير ما يلي الرأس أيؤكل أم لا؟ قال : هذا قول العوام من الناس وليس هذا بمعتبر ويجوز أكلها، سواء كانت العقدة مما يلي الصدر أو مما يلي الرأس قال : لأن المعتبر عندنا قطع الأوداج وقد وجد، وذكر أن شيخه كان يفتي به وهذا مشكل فإنه لم يوجد فيه قطع الحلقوم ولا المريء وأصحابنا . رضي الله عنهم وإن شرطوا قطع الأكثر فلا بد من قطع أحدهما عند الكل. وإذا بقي شيء من عقدة الحلقوم مما يلي الرأس لم يحصل قطع واحد منهما فلا يؤكل بالإجماع. وفي الواقعات: لو قطع الأعلى أو الأسفل ثم علم بها فقطع مرة أخرى الحلقوم من قبل أن يموت ينظر؛ فإن قطع بتمامه لا يحل لأن موته بالأول أسرع منه بالقطع الثاني وإلا حل. وذكر في فتاوى أهل سمرقند قصاب ذبح شاة في ليلة مظلمة فقطع أعلى من الحلقوم أو أسفل منه يحرم أكلها اهـ .
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And the slaughter is between the throat [halqah] and the upper chest [labbah]). With fatha on the lam and tashdid on the ba' muwahhidah. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: There is no harm in slaughtering at any part of the throat, its top and bottom. The basis for it is that it is narrated that he ﷺ said: 'The slaughter is in the throat.' And because it is the meeting place of the passage of breath, the passage of food, and the passage of veins, so cutting it achieves the purpose in the most complete manner, which is the flowing of blood. The restriction to the throat and upper chest indicates that if he slaughters above the throat or below it, it is unlawful because he acts in a place other than the place of slaughter; mentioned in al-Waqi'at. In Fatawa al-Samarqandi: It is transmitted in al-Nihayah from Imam al-Rustaghfani, may Allah have mercy on him: He was asked about a person who slaughtered a sheep and a knot of the throat remained on the chest side, and he preferred that it remain on the head side—is it eaten or not? He said: This is the saying of common people and it is not considered, and it is permissible to eat it, whether the knot is on the chest side or the head side. He said: Because what is considered with us is the cutting of the jugular veins, and that has occurred. And he mentioned that his teacher used to give fatwa according to this. But this is problematic because there is no cutting of the throat or esophagus. And our companions, may Allah be pleased with them, although they stipulated cutting the majority, still at least one of them must be cut according to all. If something of the throat knot remains on the head side, then neither of them is cut, so it is not eaten by consensus. In al-Waqi'at: If he cuts the upper or lower part, then learns about it and cuts the throat again before it dies—he considers: if he cuts it completely, it is not lawful because its death by the first cut is faster than by the second cut; otherwise it is lawful. And it is mentioned in the Fatawa of the people of Samarqand: A butcher slaughtered a sheep on a dark night and cut above the throat or below it—eating it is unlawful. End.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the precise location for valid slaughter. The matn states that slaughter must be between the halqah (throat) and the labbah (upper chest). The commentator explains that the basis is the Prophet's ﷺ hadith 'al-dhakah fi al-halq' (slaughter is in the throat). The throat is the meeting point of the passages for breath, food, and blood vessels, so cutting there achieves the purpose of blood flow. Slaughtering above or below this area is invalid. A key issue discussed is when a knot (uqda) of the throat remains after cutting: if the knot remains on the chest side, it is still considered valid because the jugular veins are cut. However, if the knot remains on the head side, then neither the throat nor the esophagus is cut, so it is invalid by consensus. The passage also addresses cases of cutting too high or too low and then recutting: if the animal dies from the first cut, the second cut does not help; if it is still alive, recutting may be valid. The Hanafi position is that the place of slaughter is restricted to this area, and deviation makes the meat unlawful.

Key Terms
الحلقة (al-halqah): The throat; the upper part of the neck where the Adam's apple is located, the starting point for valid slaughter.
اللبة (al-labbah): The upper chest, just below the throat; the lower limit for valid slaughter.
عقدة الحلقوم (uqdat al-halqum): The knot or hard part of the trachea; its location relative to the cut determines validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a butcher slaughters a sheep in the dark and cuts above the throat (higher than the halq), is the meat lawful according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Yes, because the animal died
B) No, because it was done outside the proper place of slaughter
C) Yes, if he said tasmiyah
D) No, because it is makruh but still halal

Key Takeaway
Slaughter is only valid when performed between the throat (halqah) and the upper chest (labbah), and at least one of the trachea or esophagus must be severed.

Required Vessels in Slaughter: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Definition of four vessels and rule on cutting three

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the minimum vessels required for valid slaughter, explain their proofs, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Cutting three of four vessels suffices according to Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require specific cuts for validity.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minimum number of vessels that must be cut in ritual slaughter (dhabh). The matn outlines the four vessels: the esophagus (mari'), the trachea (halqum), and the two jugular veins (wadajan). While all Hanafi imams agree that cutting these vessels is wajib, they differ on how many are strictly necessary. Understanding this ikhtilaf illustrates how each imam derives the ruling from the same primary evidence and applies the principle that 'the majority stands for the whole'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four vessels and their functions
Recognize the mari', halqum, and two wadajan. Note that the mari' and halqum allow death, while the wadajan allow blood flow.
2
State the agreed-upon purpose of slaughter
The goal is to take life and drain blood. This underlies the dispute.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
He says any three of the four suffice, based on the hadith 'Afr al-awdaj' and the principle that the majority represents the whole.
4
State Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's positions
Abu Yusuf initially agreed with Abu Hanifa, then required the trachea, esophagus, and one jugular. Muhammad requires the majority of each of the four vessels.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For example, if only the two jugulars and the trachea are cut, Abu Hanifa says it's valid, but Abu Yusuf's later view may not accept it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والمذبح المريء والحلقوم والودجان لما روي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه قال «أفر الأوداج بما شئت وهي عروق الحلق في المذبح والمريء مجرى الطعام والشراب والحلقوم مجرى النفس، والمراد بالأوداج كلها وأطلق عليه تغليباً وإنما قلنا ذلك لأن المقصود يحصل بقطعهن وهو إزهاق الروح وإخراج الدم لأنه بقطع المريء والحلقوم يحصل الإزهاق، وبقطع الودجين يحصل إنهار الدم ولو قطع الأوداج وهي العروق من غير قطع المريء والحلقوم لا يموت . فضلاً عن التوجه فلا بد من قطعهما ليحصل التوجه، ولا بد من قطع الودجين أو أحدهما ليحصل إنهار الدم. وفي المحيط والمريء وهو مجرى النفس، والودجان مجرى الدم، والحلقوم مجرى الطعام والشراب. ولو خر عنق شاة بسيف من قبل الأوداج وسمى يحل لأنه أتى بالذكاة وزيادة وقد أساء لأنه جاوز النخاع اهـ. قال رحمه الله : (وقطع الثلاث كاف والاكتفاء بالثلاث مطلقاً هو قول الإمام وقول أبي يوسف أولاً، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يشترط قطع الحلقوم والمريء واحد الودجين، وعن محمد لا بد من قطع الأكثر من كل واحد من هذه الأربعة، وأجمعوا أنه يكتفي بقطع الأكثر من هذه العروق الأربعة، فأما الحلقوم والمريء فمخالفان للأوداج ولك واحد منهما مخالف للآخر فلا بد من قطعهم، وأبو حنيفة يقول الأكثر يقوم مقام الكل وفي التتمة سئل أبو علي عن انتزاع السبع رأس الشاة وفيها حياة هل تحل بالذكاة وإن كانت تتحرك
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (The place of slaughter is the esophagus, trachea, and the two jugular veins) because it is narrated from him ﷺ that he said: 'Slice the jugular veins as you wish' and they are the veins of the throat. The esophagus is the passage of food and drink, the trachea is the passage of breath. What is meant by 'awdaj' (veins) is all of them, and it is used metaphorically. We only say that because the purpose is achieved by cutting them: the taking of life and the flowing of blood. Because by cutting the esophagus and trachea, the taking of life is achieved, and by cutting the two jugular veins, the flowing of blood is achieved. If he cuts the jugular veins (the blood vessels) without cutting the esophagus and trachea, it will not die, let alone the turning (of the animal to face qibla), so it is necessary to cut both to achieve turning, and it is necessary to cut the two jugular veins or one of them to achieve the flowing of blood. In al-Muhit: The esophagus is the passage of breath, the two jugular veins are the passage of blood, and the trachea is the passage of food and drink. If he cuts the neck of a sheep with a sword from the side of the jugular veins and says tasmiyah, it is lawful because he has performed slaughter and more, but he has done wrong because he has gone beyond the spinal cord. End. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (Cutting three is sufficient. And relying on three absolutely is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa and the first statement of Abu Yusuf. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he stipulates cutting the trachea and esophagus and one of the two jugular veins. From Muhammad: it is necessary to cut the majority of each of these four. They all agree that cutting the majority of these four vessels suffices. As for the trachea and esophagus, they are distinct from the jugular veins, and each of the two is distinct from the other, so cutting them is necessary. Abu Hanifa says: the majority stands for the whole. In al-Tatimah: Abu Ali was asked about a predator tearing off the head of a sheep while it still has life—is it lawful by slaughter if it is still moving?
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum number of vessels to cut for valid slaughter. The matn identifies four vessels: the esophagus (mari'), the trachea (halqum), and the two jugular veins (wadajan). The commentator explains their functions and the necessity of cutting at least the trachea and esophagus for death to occur, and at least one jugular vein for blood flow. The ruling on cutting three being sufficient is then detailed with the positions of the imams: Abu Hanifa holds that cutting any three (of the four) is sufficient, even if one of the three is a jugular vein and the other two are the other vessels, or any combination, as long as the majority is cut. Abu Yusuf initially agreed but later stipulated that the trachea and esophagus plus one jugular vein must be cut. Muhammad requires cutting the majority of each of the four vessels (i.e., at least a little from each). The consensus among them is that cutting the majority of the four vessels is sufficient, but they differ on the interpretation. The passage ends with a question about a predator removing the head, but no answer is provided here.

Key Terms
المريء (al-mari'): The esophagus; the passage for food and drink. Along with the trachea, cutting it effects death.
الحلقوم (al-halqum): The trachea; the passage for breath. Its cut is necessary for the animal to die.
الودجان (al-wadajan): The two jugular veins; their cut ensures the flow of blood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the minimum number of vessels that must be cut for a valid slaughter?
A) All four vessels
B) Three of the four vessels
C) The trachea and esophagus only
D) The two jugular veins only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows flexibility: cutting three of four vessels suffices according to Abu Hanifa, but the operative fatwa requires the trachea, esophagus, and one jugular vein.

Permissible Tools for Slaughter
Ruling on what tools can be used for valid slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on permissible slaughter tools and apply the condition that the tool must cut the jugular veins and cause blood to flow, except for attached teeth and nails.

Core Idea
Any sharp tool that causes blood to flow is valid for slaughter, except attached teeth and nails.

This lesson examines the types of instruments permitted for slaughter (dhabh) according to the Hanafi school. The key principle is that the tool must be capable of cutting the jugular veins and causing blood to flow. The source text from Al-Bahr al-Raiq lists specific examples and provides hadith evidence, clarifying the exception of attached teeth and nails by distinguishing Islamic practice from that of the Abyssinians.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the matn and commentary to list the permissible tools: nail, horn, bone, detached tooth, reed, sharp stone, and anything that effectively cuts. Note that the tool does not have to be a knife.
The tool must be sharp and cause blood to flow.
2
Determine the exception
The exception is clearly stated: 'except a tooth and nail that are attached (قائمين)' to a living being. Understand why these are excluded: they are not proper tools according to Shariah, as the practice of using them was done by the Abyssinians to show endurance.
A detached tooth is permissible because it is no longer part of a living animal.
3
Understand the dalil
The text cites two hadith: 'Every tool that causes blood to flow and cuts the jugular veins' and 'Cut the jugular veins as you wish.' Also the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim who asked about using a sharp stone (marwah) and received tacit approval.
The Prophet's approval of marwah confirms that a stone is permissible.
4
Analyse the prohibition
The prohibition of attached teeth/nails is explained by referring to the Abyssinian custom. The Shariah requires a tool that severs the vessels quickly, not one that tortures the animal.
This shows the principle of ihsan (kindness) in slaughter.
5
Apply the principle
Conclude that any instrument that is sharp enough to cut the jugular veins and cause blood to flow is valid, provided it is not an attached tooth or nail. This includes glass, metal, stone, etc.
Modern tools like stainless steel knives are included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو) بظفر وقرن وعظم وسن منزوع وليطة ومروة وما أنهر الدم إلا سنا وظفراً قائمين يعني يكفي في الحل بما ذكر لقوله عليه الصلاة السلام كل ما أنهر الدم وأفرى «الأوداج ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «أفر الأوداج بما شئت وما روي من المنع في الظفر والسن محمول على غير المشروع فإن الحبشة كانوا يفعلون ذلك إظهاراً للجلد والمشروع آلة جارحة فيحصل به المقصود وهو إنهار الدم. والليطة القصب الفارسي والمروة الحجر الذي له حد، والدليل على جواز الذبح بهما ما روي عن عدي بن حاتم قال :قلت يا رسول الله نجد الصيد وليس معنا سكين إلا المروة
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (Even if with a nail, horn, bone, detached tooth, reed, and sharp stone, and whatever causes blood to flow except a tooth and nail that are attached). Meaning it suffices for lawfulness by what is mentioned due to his saying ﷺ: 'Everything that causes blood to flow and cuts the jugular veins' and his saying ﷺ: 'Cut the jugular veins as you wish.' And what is narrated of prohibition regarding the nail and tooth is applied to the non-Shariah practice, for the Abyssinians used to do that to show endurance. The Shariah practice is an instrument that cuts, so the purpose is achieved, which is the flowing of blood. Al-litah is Persian reed, and al-marwah is a stone that has an edge. The evidence for the permissibility of slaughtering with them is what is narrated from 'Adi ibn Hatim who said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, we find game and we have no knife except the marwah...
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of using various tools for slaughter. The matn states that slaughter with a nail, horn, bone, detached tooth, reed, or sharp stone is valid, provided they are sharp and cause blood to flow. The exception is a tooth or nail that are still attached (to the body) because they are not considered proper instruments. The commentator cites two hadiths: 'Every tool that causes blood to flow and cuts the jugular veins' and 'Cut the jugular veins as you wish.' The prohibition of using teeth and nails is understood to apply to the practice of the Abyssinians who used them to endure pain rather than for quick slaughter. The Shariah requires a tool that cuts and severs. The words 'litah' (reed) and 'marwah' (sharp stone) are defined, and the incident of 'Adi ibn Hatim is cited as evidence for using a stone when no knife is available. The Hanafi school thus allows any tool that effectively cuts the vessels, as long as it is not a tooth or nail attached to a living being.

Key Terms
الليطة (al-litah): Persian reed; a sharp piece of reed used for slaughter.
المروة (al-marwah): A sharp stone or flint used for cutting, permissible for slaughter when a knife is unavailable.
السن المنزوع (al-sinn al-manzu'): A detached tooth (not attached to a live animal), which is permissible to use for slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is it permissible to slaughter an animal with a sharp stone (marwah) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because it causes blood to flow and cuts
B) No, because a knife is required
C) Yes, but only if no other tool is available
D) No, because it is makruh

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of a slaughter tool depends on its ability to cut the jugular veins and cause blood to flow; attached teeth and nails are invalid because they are not considered proper instruments.

Minimum Required Cuts for Valid Slaughter: Three Vessels Suffice
Definition of required cuts and minimum for valid slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum required cuts for valid Hanafi slaughter and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of vessels to be cut.

Core Idea
Cutting three of the four major vessels suffices for valid slaughter in the Hanafi school.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes the fundamental rule for dhabh: the throat (hulqum), gullet (mari'), and two jugular veins (wadjayn) are the required cuts. The relied-upon position is that cutting any three is sufficient, with at least one of the first two. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof from hadith, and the intra-Hanafi differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the required vessels
The act is slaughter (dhabh). The four vessels mentioned are: al-hulqum (windpipe), al-mari' (esophagus), and the two wadjayn (jugular veins).
These four are the channels that must be cut for valid bleeding.
2
State the minimum requirement
The text says 'wa qat'u al-thalath kaf' (cutting three is sufficient). This means any three of the four vessels must be cut for the slaughter to be valid. At least one of hulqum or mari' must be included by consensus.
If only the jugulars are cut, the animal dies strangled, which is not halal.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'Ahrir al-awdaj' (sever the jugular veins). The command indicates obligation, and the Hanafi school interprets 'awdaj' to include the throat and gullet. Cutting three fulfills the command.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but still binding in amal.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa says cutting three suffices absolutely. Abu Yusuf initially agreed, then later required cutting hulqum, mari', and one wadaj. Muhammad requires cutting the majority of each of the four vessels. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
Practical thamarah: if only three are cut and one is missing mari', Abu Hanifa allows it, but Sahibayn do not.
5
Apply to edge cases from the text
The recutting case: if the first cut misses the required vessels and the animal is recut before death, if the recut completes the vessels, it is not halal because the animal died from the first non-compliant cut. If not fully severed, it is halal. The Samarkand fatwa: slaughter in darkness that cuts above or below the throat is unlawful.
These illustrate the principle that valid cuts must be made correctly from the start.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الذبائح
والحلقوم والودجان وقطع الثلاث كاف ولو بظفر وقرن وعظم وسن منزوع وليطة ومروة وما أنهر الدم إلا سنا وظفراً قائمين وندب حد شفرته وكره النخع وقطع الرأس
وجد، وذكر أن شيخه كان يفتي به وهذا مشكل فإنه لم يوجد فيه قطع الحلقوم ولا المريء وأصحابنا . رضي الله عنهم وإن شرطوا قطع الأكثر فلا بد من قطع أحدهما عند الكل. وإذا بقي شيء من عقدة الحلقوم مما يلي الرأس لم يحصل قطع واحد منهما فلا يؤكل بالإجماع. وفي الواقعات: لو قطع الأعلى أو الأسفل ثم علم بها فقطع مرة أخرى الحلقوم من قبل أن يموت ينظر؛ فإن قطع بتمامه لا يحل لأن موته بالأول أسرع منه بالقطع الثاني وإلا حل. وذكر في فتاوى أهل سمرقند قصاب ذبح شاة في ليلة مظلمة فقطع أعلى من الحلقوم أو أسفل منه يحرم أكلها اهـ .
Book of Slaughterings. The throat and the two jugular veins, and cutting three is sufficient, even if with a nail, horn, bone, a detached tooth, a reed, a sharp stone, and whatever causes blood to flow except a fixed tooth and nail. And it is recommended to sharpen his blade, and it is disliked to sever the spinal cord and cut off the head. Found, and it is mentioned that his teacher used to give fatwa with it, and this is problematic because it did not involve cutting the throat nor the gullet. Our companions, may Allah be pleased with them, even if they stipulate cutting the majority, it is necessary to cut one of them according to all. And if something of the knot of the throat remains towards the head, neither of them has been cut, so it is not eaten by consensus. In al-Waqi'at: If he cut the upper or lower [part] and then became aware and cut the throat again before it died, consideration: if he cut it completely, it is not lawful because its death by the first is quicker than by the second cut; otherwise it is lawful. And it is mentioned in the Fatawa of the people of Samarkand: A butcher slaughtered a sheep in a dark night and cut above or below the throat: its eating is unlawful. End.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins with the Book of Slaughterings and states the ruling: For valid slaughter (dhabh), the required cuts are the throat (hulqum), the gullet (mari'), and the two jugular veins (wadjayn). Cutting three of these four is sufficient; it is not necessary to cut all four. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school. The author then lists various tools that may be used, which will be discussed in a later lesson. The commentary then discusses a problematic incident: a scholar's teacher gave a fatwa in a case where the throat and gullet were not cut. The author clarifies that even though the majority of the vessels must be cut, at least one of the throat or gullet must be cut by consensus (ijma'). If a piece of the throat's knot remains towards the head, neither has been cut and eating is prohibited by consensus. The passage then presents a case from al-Waqi'at: if one cuts above or below the throat and then recuts the throat before the animal dies, if the recut completely severs the throat, it is not halal because the animal died by the first cut which was not valid slaughter; otherwise it is halal. Finally, a fatwa from Samarkand states that if a butcher cuts above or below the throat in darkness, the meat is unlawful. This lesson establishes the fundamental requirement: cutting three of the four major vessels, and that at least one of the air and food passages must be severed.

Key Terms
الحلقوم (al-hulqum): The throat, specifically the windpipe or trachea, the passage for air.
المريء (al-mari'): The gullet or esophagus, the passage for food and drink.
الودجان (al-wadjayn): The two jugular veins, the blood vessels on either side of the neck.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the minimum number of vessels that must be cut in valid slaughter?
A) All four: throat, gullet, and both jugulars
B) Three of the four vessels
C) Only the two jugulars
D) Only the throat and gullet

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, cutting any three of the four major vessels (throat, gullet, two jugulars) makes the slaughter valid, with at least one of throat or gullet required by consensus.

The Recommendation to Sharpen the Blade Before Slaughter
Ruling on sharpening blade and tool types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharpening the blade before slaughter and explain the evidence from the hadith of ihsan.

Core Idea
Sharpen your blade before laying the animal down; causing unnecessary pain violates ihsan.

This lesson focuses on the sunnah of sharpening the blade before slaughter. The Prophet ﷺ commanded excellence (ihsan) in all acts, including slaughter. Sharpening the blade ensures a swift death and minimizes suffering. The lesson also covers the dislike of sharpening after the animal is laid down, as this causes additional distress.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act and its evidence
Locate the phrase 'وندب حد شفرته' and then the hadith quoted by Imam Muslim. Note that the hadith is the proof for the recommendation.
The hadith is: 'إن الله كتب الإحسان على كل شيء...'
2
Understand the legal implication of the hadith
The command 'فأحسنوا الذبحة' and 'وليحد أحدكم شفرته' indicates that sharpening is a recommended act (mustahabb) because it fulfills ihsan.
3
Distinguish between permissible and disliked methods of sharpening
The text mentions that sharpening after the animal is laid down is makruh, based on the hadith 'لقد أردت أن تميتها موتتين'. Understand that the timing matters.
Also note the tool types: sharp (haddah) is permissible without dislike, blunt (kalilah) is permissible but disliked.
4
Apply the ruling to tool types
Classify tools as cutting vs non-cutting, and cutting as sharp or blunt. The sharp tool is recommended; the blunt is disliked due to delay in blood flow.
This is from the mention of 'الآلة على ضربين'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وندب حد شفرته لقوله عليه الصلاة إن الله كتب الإحسان على كل شيء فإذا قتلتم فأحسنوا القتلة وإذا ذبحتم فأحسنوا الذبحة وليحد أحدكم شفرته وليرح ذبيحته» رواه مسلم وغيره ويكره أن يضجعها ثم يحد الشفرة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لمن أضجع الشاة وهو يحد شفرته لقد أردت أن تميتها موتتين هلا حددتها قبل أن تضجعها الحديث والآلة على ضربين : قاطعة وغير قاطعة والقاطعة على ضربين : حادة وكليلة ؛ فالحادة اختيارية وضرورية، فالحادة يجوز الذبح بها من غير كراهة والكليلة يجوز الذبح بها ويكره لما مر من الإبطاء في الإراقة؛ كذا في المحيط . قال رحمه الله : (وكره النخع وقطع الرأس والذبح من أن يصل إلى النخاع وهو خيط أبيض في جوف عظم القفاء) النخع هو الرقبة وهو بالفتح والضم لغة فيه. قال في النهاية ومن قال هو عرق أبيض فقدسها. واعترضه صاحب العناية أن من سمى بما ذكر لم يغلط لأن أهل اللغة ذكروه بلفظ الخيط وإنما كره لنهيه عليه الصلاة والسلام عن أن ننح الشاة إذا ذبحت وتفسيره ما ذكرنا. وقيل: أن يمد رأسها حتى يظهر ،مذبحها وقيل أن يكسر رقبتها قبل أن تسكن من الاضطراب وكل ذلك مكروه. وفي قطع الرأس زيادة تعذيب فيكره، ويكره أن يجر ما يريد ذبحه وأن يسلخ قبل أن يبرد ويؤكل في جميع ذلك لأن الكراهة لمعنى زائد وهو زيادة الألم فلا يوجب الحرمة. ويكره أن يذبحها موجهة لغير القبلة لمخالفة السنة في توجيهها للقبلة وتؤكل وفي الذبح من الفقا زيادة ألم فيكره، ويحل لما ذكرنا إذا بقيت حية حتى يقطع العروق لتحقق الموت بالذكاة، وإن ماتت قبل قطع العروق لا تؤكل لوجود الموت بما ليس بذكاة.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And it is recommended to sharpen his blade because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed excellence in everything. So when you kill, do so well; when you slaughter, do so well; let one of you sharpen his blade and let him give comfort to his animal.' Narrated by Muslim and others. And it is disliked to lay it down and then sharpen the blade because of his saying, peace be upon him, to one who laid down a sheep while sharpening his blade: 'You intend to give it two deaths; why did you not sharpen it before laying it down?' The tool is of two types: cutting and non-cutting. The cutting is of two types: sharp and blunt. The sharp is optional and necessary; it is permissible to slaughter with it without dislike. The blunt is permissible to slaughter with but disliked because of the delay in blood flow; thus in al-Muhit. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And it is disliked to sever the spinal cord, cut off the head, and slaughter from the back until reaching the spinal cord—which is a white thread inside the bone of the back of the neck.' 'Nakha' is the neck, with fat-ha and damm in language. Al-Nihaya said: and whoever says it is a white vein has erred. The author of al-'Inaya objected that one who names it as mentioned is not mistaken because linguists mentioned it as a thread. And it is only disliked because of the prohibition of slaughtering the sheep by breaking its neck; its explanation is what we mentioned. It is said: to stretch its head until its throat appears; it is said: to break its neck before it calms from movement; all of that is disliked. Cutting off the head involves extra pain, so it is disliked. It is disliked to drag what one intends to slaughter and to skin it before it has cooled, and it is eaten in all that because the dislike is for an extra meaning—increased pain—so it does not cause prohibition. It is disliked to slaughter it facing other than the qibla, contrary to the sunna of facing it toward the qibla, and it is eaten. And slaughter from the back of the neck involves extra pain, so it is disliked. And it is lawful if it remains alive until the vessels are cut, so death is verified by dhabh; and if it dies before the vessels are cut, it is not eaten because death occurred by something other than dhabh.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This lesson covers the recommended (mandub) and disliked (makruh) acts in slaughter. It is recommended to sharpen the blade before slaughter, based on the hadith 'Allah has prescribed excellence in everything.' This ensures a swift death and minimizes suffering. It is disliked to sharpen the blade after the animal has been laid down, as this causes additional distress. The tool should be sharp (haddah) rather than blunt (kalilah); slaughter with a blunt tool is permissible but disliked due to the delay in blood flow. Several actions are disliked: severing the spinal cord (nakh')—which means breaking the neck before death; cutting off the head; slaughtering from the back of the neck (min al-qafa); dragging the animal; skinning before the body has cooled; and facing the animal away from the qibla. These are disliked due to causing extra pain, but they do not prohibit the meat. The key principle is that as long as the prescribed vessels are cut while the animal is alive, the slaughter is valid. If the animal dies before the vessels are cut, it is carrion and not permissible.

Key Terms
حد الشفرة (hadd al-shafrah): Sharpening the blade
الشفرة (al-shafrah): The blade or knife used for slaughter

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it disliked to sharpen the blade after the animal is laid down?
A) Because the blade may not be sharp enough.
B) Because it causes the animal to suffer an extra 'death' of waiting.
C) Because it is against the sunnah to sharpen at any time.
D) Because the animal might escape.

Key Takeaway
The blade should be sharpened before the animal is laid down to avoid unnecessary suffering; this is a recommended act based on the hadith of ihsan.
